1601 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


SISTERS OF ST. MARY v. AAER SPRAYED INSULATION


Case No. 85CV5952


State of Wisconsin, Circuit Court for the Dane County


1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4440



December 17, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNREPORTED TRIAL COURT DECISION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Order Affirmed by Court of Appeals on July 26, 1989, Reported at 1989 Wisc. App. LEXIS 727.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff hospitals brought an action against named and presently unknown defendants, manufacturers, distributors, and installers of asbestos containing materials, seeking compensatory and punitive damages on a number of grounds, including negligence and strict liability. The hospitals requested a class certification generally described as all hospital entities in the United States.


OVERVIEW: The hospitals proposed a three-phase proceeding. A class trial would proceed on strict liability and negligence; the second phase would establish a trust with the level of funding to be determined; and the third phase would involve individual damage recovery steps. The court looked to the three criteria of Wis. R. Civ. P., Wis. Stat. § 803.08 and determined that (1) the named parties had a right or interest in common because it was not necessary that the interests of every class member were identical; every class member desired the same outcome; and proof would be common in either the strict liability and the negligence contexts; (2) the hospitals' attorneys would adequately represent the interests of the absent class members; and (3) it would be impracticable to bring all interested hospitals before the court. However, given that around 97 percent of the class members would be from outside the state, with minimal, if any, contacts with the state, a material conflict existed with regard to the law to be applied. The court balanced the difficulties inherent in the hospitals' proposal and concluded that a nationwide class action would not be manageable, fair, or more convenient.


OUTCOME: The court denied the hospitals request for certification of a class for a nationwide class action. The court specifically did not dismiss the claim of any named hospital or preclude any class member from filing an action on its own behalf.

 

1602 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Milwaukee v. Nelson


No. 86-2234-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District One


142 Wis. 2d 944; 419 N.W.2d 573; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4402



December 3, 1987 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION -- REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23 (3)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: RUSSELL W. STAMPER, Judge. Reversed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of an adverse declaratory judgment from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) granted pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 806.04, which enjoined enforcement by arrest or citation of Milwaukee, Wis., Code of Ordinances § 106-31(1)(a) (1979), prohibiting loitering.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested pursuant Wis. Stat. § 800.02(6) for loitering in violation of Milwaukee, Wis., Code of Ordinances § 106-31(1)(a). The trial court granted a declaratory judgment enjoining police officers from enforcing the loitering ordinance because it violated equal protection and due process guarantees and because it was vague and overbroad. The city argued that a defendant who sought declaratory relief had to file a separate civil suit. The court found that once disputed conduct had taken place, the equities of the declaratory relief remedy could be properly litigated in defense to a prosecution. However, the court reversed the judgment, finding that a violation of the loitering ordinance might give rise to probable cause to believe that a crime had been committed and that an arrest for such a violation did not necessarily violate the constitutional probable cause requirement. The court held that because defendant's conduct fell within the "hard core" of the ordinance, he could not be heard to complain that its provisions were unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and order.

1604 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Birnbaum v. Birnbaum


No. 87-1235


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


142 Wis. 2d 943; 419 N.W.2d 361; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4238



November 25, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: Jack Aulik, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner former wife appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which granted respondent former husband's motion to dismiss the wife's motion to extend and increase an award of limited term maintenance.


OVERVIEW: The parties' divorce judgment awarded the wife limited term maintenance pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 247.32 (1975), which prohibited alteration of the term of limited maintenance. The wife subsequently sought an extension of maintenance based upon a retroactive application of Wis. Stat. § 767.32(1). On appeal, the court held that 1977 Wis. Laws ch. 105, § 62(1) did not permit the retroactive application of § 767.32(1) to a judgment that was entered under Wis. Stat. § 247.32 (1975). The court determined that ch. 105, § 62(1) permitted the modification of orders only, not final judgments. Because the parties' rights, with respect to the term of maintenance, had been determined by a final judgment, § 62(1) did not apply and the extension of maintenance was prohibited by § 247.32 (1975).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

 

1605 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


City of Madison v. Arness


Nos. 87-0291, 87-0293


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


142 Wis. 2d 941; 419 N.W.2d 360; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4242



November 25, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments of the circuit court for Dane county: MICHAEL B. TORPHY, JR., Judge, Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged an order from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendants and imposed forfeitures for violating Madison, Wis., Gen. Ordinances § 23.07(2), a trespass ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were part of a small group of protestors in a federal courthouse. Defendants were arrested by a city police officer and charged with trespassing when they refused to leave the courthouse after the closing hour, despite a request from a federal security guard. On appeal, the court determined that the trial court erred in concluding that the defense of legal justification was unavailable to defendants, but found that the trial court's error was harmless because defendants' belief that violating the city trespass ordinance was the only means of preventing bodily harm to them and others was not objectively reasonable. The court found that defendants failed to show that justice compelled a decision on the issue of the constitutionality of § 23.07(2), which was the only means for appellate review as the issue was raised for the first time on appeal. The court determined that the record established that the security officer had authority to order defendants to leave and that he did so.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1606 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


City of Sheboygan v. Arnold


No. 87-1002


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Two


142 Wis. 2d 942; 419 N.W.2d 360; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4309



November 25, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Sheboygan county: JOHN BOLGERT, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County (Wisconsin), which convicted her for keeping birds that disturbed the peace by causing frequent or long continued noise, a violation of the Municipal Code of the City of Sheboygan §§ 25-44.


OVERVIEW: Appellant raised approximately 120 cockatiels, parrots, or other birds in her home. A police officer witnessed one bird in particular speaking loudly out of the front window. Upon finding a record of a warning for violation of the same noise ordinance earlier that month, the officer issued a civil complaint to appellant. Appellant questioned whether there was sufficient evidence to support her conviction pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 805.17(2). On appeal, the court affirmed. The court noted that appellant's own witness testified that the birds could be heard half a block away from appellant's house. Moreover, the court's search of the record revealed evidence that appellant kept many birds, and that the birds caused frequent noise, disturbing her neighbor's "comfort or repose." In addition, the court held that the ordinance clearly reached negligent conduct so that appellant's lack of intent was not a defense. Finally, the court rejected appellant's argument that the ordinance was unconstitutional because it did not adopt a precise means of measuring sound by using a meter because she cited no authority to support her proposition, a violation of Wis. Stat. § 809.19(1)(e).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1607 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Otte v. State, Dep't of Natural Resources


No. 87-0154


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


142 Wis. 2d 222; 418 N.W.2d 16; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4326


September 15, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
November 17, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Burnett county: Harry Gundersen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Burnett County (Wisconsin), which affirmed the order of respondent, the Wisconsin Department of Natural Resources (DNR), requiring the landowner to restore a filled portion of a ditch to a condition similar to that which existed prior to the landowner's purchase of the land.


OVERVIEW: After the landowner made alterations to an artificial outlet ditch on his property, a riparian landowner filed a complaint that the ditch was lowering the water level of the lake. Subsequently, the DNR ordered the landowner to restore and maintain the ditch to protect the riparian landowner's private property. On administrative review the order was affirmed, and the landowner sought judicial review. The trial court affirmed the DNR's order, and the landowner sought further review. On appeal, the landowner contended that the DNR's order constituted an unconstitutional taking of property and a denial of due process. The landowner also contended that the DNR was required to follow the procedures under Wis. Stat. § 30.03(4)(a) before it could issue such an order. The court held that § 30.03(4)(a) was inapplicable because there was no alleged violation of any statute relating to navigable waters. However, the court held that the order effectively deprived the landowner of substantially all beneficial use of this portion of his land. Therefore, the court ruled that the DNR's order was invalid because it constituted a taking of the landowner's property without statutory authority.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's affirmance of the DNR's order to the landowner to restore a certain ditch, and the court remanded the matter to the trial court with directions to set aside the DNR order.

 

1608 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. King


No. 86-2088-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


142 Wis. 2d 207; 418 N.W.2d 11; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4233


October 8, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
November 12, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Green county: Franz W. Brand, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Green County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of carrying a concealed weapon in violation of Wis. Stat. § 941.23. The trial court also denied defendant's motion to suppress the weapon on grounds that it was discovered and seized as the result of an illegal search.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped and issued citations for violating municipal ordinances regulating traffic. In preparation for transporting defendant to the police station to post bond, a police officer performed a weapons search. The officer found a "military" knife with a seven-to-nine-inch blade under defendant's clothing. Defendant was arrested for carrying a concealed weapon. The trial court convicted defendant after he pleaded no contest. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the search was proper as incident to a lawful arrest, the weapon was admissible, and that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress. The court found that defendant was properly and lawfully arrested prior to the search. The court concluded that even if the arresting officer violated Wis. Stat. § 345.23(2)(c) by transporting him to the station, the statutory violation could not form the basis for suppression of the knife. The court noted that there was no constitutional bar to searches incident to noncriminal traffic arrests.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of carrying a concealed weapon.

 

1609 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Dunn County v. Svee


No. 87-0915


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Three


142 Wis. 2d 942; 419 N.W.2d 360; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4302



November 10, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Final Disposition By Denial of Review February 16, 1988


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dunn county: DONNA J. MUZA, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant possessor sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dunn County (Wisconsin) that was rendered in favor of plaintiff county and evicted her from property owned by the county.


OVERVIEW: The possessor and her ex-husband owned the property but failed to pay the taxes on it. The county purchased the tax certificates as the exclusive bidder in a sale for delinquent taxes pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 74.44(1). The ex-husband deeded his interest in the property to the trust, and neither the husband nor the trust sought to redeem the tax certificate. The county executed a tax deed conveying all interest in the property to itself. The trial court initiated an eviction action in response to which the possessor and her ex-husband asserted the county's claim to the property was illegal and that its tax deed was false. The trial court found that the defensive allegation was a counterclaim under Wis. Stat. § 75.61(1) that permitted the possessor and ex-husband the opportunity to pay the county's purchase price, along with the taxes due with interest. No money was paid, and the trial court entered a judgment in favor of the county. The court affirmed and held that in order for the possessor to challenge the validity of the county's tax deed she had to pay into the court the statutorily required money for the property, the taxes and interest accrued thereon.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1610 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Dunn County v. Svee


No. 87-0916


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Three


142 Wis. 2d 942; 419 N.W.2d 360; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4293



November 10, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Final Disposition By Denial of Review February 16, 1988


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dunn county, DONNA J. MUZA, Judge, Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Dunn County (Wisconsin) that evicted him from property owned by the county. The county treasurer purchased the property's tax certificate pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 74.44(1) after the owner and his ex-wife failed to pay property taxes. The trial court treated the owner's defensive allegation as a counterclaim challenging the validity of the tax deed pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 75.61(1).


OVERVIEW: The trial court conditionally issued a judgment of eviction against the owner and his ex-wife if they failed to post the required payment. Neither made payment, and the eviction judgment was entered. The owner, appearing pro se, objected to the trial court's requirement that he post sums required by Wis. Stat. § 75.61(1) as a condition of seeking relief and challenged the constitutionality of the tax deed statutes. In affirming, the court held that the provisions of § 75.61(1) applied because the owner challenged the deed's validity. While the statute spoke of a "plaintiff," the intent of the legislation prevailed, so the fact that the owner was a "defendant" was unimportant. Therefore, the owner was properly required to post payment. The court noted that Wis. Stat. § 74.44, which authorized the county treasurer to be the exclusive bidder and purchaser of lands sold for delinquent taxes, had long been held constitutional despite due process and equal protection challenges. Furthermore, the framers of the constitution did not intend Wis. Const. art. I, § 14 to restrict the legislature's power to enforce taxation because the power to tax was an absolute necessity to the sovereignty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1611 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Anderson


No. 86-2306-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


142 Wis. 2d 162; 417 N.W.2d 411; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4272


August 12, 1987, Argued  
November 4, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Walworth county: James L. Carlson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction by the Circuit Court for Walworth County (Wisconsin) for one count of carrying a concealed weapon contrary to Wis. Stat. § 941.23 and one count of possession of a firearm by a felon contrary to Wis. Stat. § 941.29(1), (2). The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress all the evidence discovered in the search of his vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the stop, seizure, and search of his vehicle and person were unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress and found that the police officers did not have probable cause to stop, seize, or search defendant's vehicle because there was no reasonable basis for the officers to conclude that defendant was committing, was about to commit, or had committed a crime, thereby allowing a temporary stop under Terry or Wis. Stat. § 968.24. The court determined that the warrantless search and seizure might have been valid under the community caretaking exception to the warrant requirement but that the record on appeal did not support such a finding where the evidence had not been fully developed. The court remanded the case for a determination of whether the officers were performing a bona fide community caretaker function when they detained defendant and searched his vehicle. While police contacts with citizens seeking to resolve or defuse private disputes were within the community caretaker function, the court suggested that the stop of defendant's vehicle was a subterfuge.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment finding that the stop, seizure, and search of defendant's vehicle and person were constitutional and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

1612 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Mobil Oil Corp. v. Ley


No. 86-1221


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


142 Wis. 2d 108; 416 N.W.2d 680; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4181; 97 Oil & Gas Rep. 228


September 3, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
October 27, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review pending. This petition was not decided at the time the volume went to press. Its disposition will be reported in a later volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: Mark Frankel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporate taxpayer appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which granted summary judgment to defendant, the Secretary of the Wisconsin Department of Revenue. The trial court found that the Wisconsin corporate franchise tax, Wis. Stat. § 71.04(3) (1981), calculated by net income without credit for any windfall profit tax paid, did not violate Wis. Const. art. VIII, § 1.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was engaged in producing and marketing of crude oil and natural gas, and refining and marketing petroleum products. As a domestic oil producer, it was required to pay the federal windfall profit tax as set forth in the Crude Oil Windfall Profit Tax Act of 1980. However, Wis. Stat. § 71.04(3) (1981) provided that the taxpayer could not deduct the windfall profit tax in calculating net income for the purpose of determining its Wisconsin corporate franchise tax. The taxpayer alleged that this was unconstitutional under the income tax provisions of Wis. Const. art. VIII, § 1. The court disagreed, finding that the tax was not an income tax and thus not affected by income tax calculations. Instead, it was a franchise tax enacted under the "privileges" clause of the state constitution. Consequently, the legislature's decisions regarding possible exemptions only had to be "reasonable" which the court found to be true in the case at hand. The Wisconsin legislature was within its discretion to measure the corporate franchise tax by the taxpayer's net income without deducting the windfall profit tax.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the Secretary and against the taxpayer, finding the franchise tax constitutional.

 

1613 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Harris v. Reivitz


No. 86-0324


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


142 Wis. 2d 82; 417 N.W.2d 50; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4145


September 4, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
October 22, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: Angela B. Bartell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion for reconsideration of the dismissal of his complaint that had alleged that Wis. Admin. Code § HSS 309.49(3), which dealt with money inmates kept in their prison accounts, was unconstitutional because of the way it was enforced.


OVERVIEW: The issues on appeal were whether the order denying reconsideration was appealable and whether the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction for the inmate's failure to serve the joint committee for review of administrative rules under Wis. Stat. § 227.05(5) and for failure to serve the attorney general. The court first held that the trial court's order denying the inmate's motion for reconsideration met the new issues test and therefore the order was appealable. The court noted that failure to serve the attorney general had the effect of depriving a trial court of subject matter jurisdiction, when the constitutionality of a statute or an ordinance was attacked under Wis. Stat. § 806.04(11). An action for declaratory judgment as to the validity of an administrative rule was a creature of statute and consequently strict compliance with the procedural requirements of the statute was required. Wis. Stat. § 227.05(5) required service upon the joint committee for review of administrative rules. Therefore, because the statutes were not strictly complied with, the trial court lacked jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the inmate's appeal.

 

1614 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re E. L. D.


No. 87-1128


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Two


142 Wis. 2d 939; 417 N.W.2d 198; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4208



October 21, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Winnebago county: ROBERT HAWLEY, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant inmate appealed an order from the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin), which continued her protective placement under Wis. Stat. § 55.06 as sought by plaintiff county. The inmate alleged that the original placement violated her constitutional rights and that the evidence was insufficient to warrant her continued placement.


OVERVIEW: An inmate was placed in protective placement under Wis. Stat. § 55.06 because her developmental disabilities and other incapacities made her incapable of providing for her own care and created a substantial risk of harm to herself. Two years later, a hearing was held and the trial court authorized her continued placement. On appeal, the court affirmed and held as follows: The inmate's constitutional issues all arose from her original placement. However, because the inmate did not appeal the original placement within the time specified in Wis. Stat. § 55.06(18), the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction over those issues. A psychiatrist and a social worker testified that the inmate suffered from serious mental disorders, could not address her daily living needs without help and supervision, and needed 24-hour supervision in order to prevent her from harming others. Therefore, the evidence was sufficient to meet the dangerousness element of protective custody specified in Wis. Stat. § 55.06(2)(c).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

 

1615 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Wisconsin Wine & Spirit Institute v. Ley


No. 86-2028


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


141 Wis. 2d 958; 416 N.W.2d 914; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4161


October 5, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
October 15, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: Angela B. Bartell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant trade association sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which issued a declaratory judgment in favor of respondents, Wisconsin Department of Revenue and an associated individual, in an action which challenged the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 125.69(1)(a).


OVERVIEW: Wis. Stat. § 125.69(1)(a) prohibits an intoxicating liquor wholesaler, among others, from holding a direct or indirect interest in a retail "Class A" liquor license or establishment, and a retail "Class A" liquor licensee from holding a direct or indirect interest in a liquor wholesale permit or establishment, except that if such prohibited interest existed on October 3, 1963, licenses and permits which would otherwise be in violation of the restriction shall continue to be renewed unless other cause is shown for nonrenewal. Seventeen of the trade association members were in existence before October 3, 1963, but held no interest in a retail "Class A" liquor license. Several members who held a liquor wholesaler's license also held a retail "Class A" liquor license under the grandfather clause contained in § 125.69(1)(a). A declaratory judgment was entered in favor of the Department of Revenue and the associated individual regarding the constitutionality of § 125.69(1)(a). On review, the court reversed. The court held that the grandfather clause contained in § 125.69(1)(a) created a classification without a rational basis and was a denial of the equal protection of the laws.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the declaratory judgment in favor of the Department of Revenue and the associated individual.

 

1616 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Savings League of Wisconsin, Ltd. v. Wisconsin Dep't of Revenue


No. 86-1825


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


141 Wis. 2d 918; 416 N.W.2d 650; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4226


October 5, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
October 14, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review pending. This petition was not decided at the time the volume went to press. Its disposition will be reported in a later volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: Angela B. Bartell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers, comprised of a league of financial institutions, savings and loan associations, and other similar corporations, sought review of the summary judgment granted by the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) for respondents, the Wisconsin Department of Revenue and the Department Secretary, finding that Wis. Stat. § 71.01(2) (1983-1984), which imposed an annual franchise tax on domestic corporations, was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: In computing net income subject to a corporate franchise tax under Wis. Stat. § 71.01(2) (1983-1984), the Department included all income earned on stocks and obligations of the United States. The taxpayers contended that to the extent that § 71.01(2) was a tax imposed on income earned on federal obligations, it violated the Supremacy Clause, U.S. Const. art. VI, cl. 2, and the Borrowing Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 2. On review, the court held that the inclusion of tax-exempt income in the measure of a corporate franchise tax does not invalidate the tax and therefore that Wis. Stat. § 71.01(2) (1983-1984) did not violate the Supremacy or Borrowing Clauses. The court rejected the taxpayers' contention that § 71.01(2) was invalid because the principal purpose of the statute was to reach and tax otherwise unreachable federal income and concluded that the legislative purpose in enacting the taxing statute was irrelevant as long as the tax operated in a constitutional way. Because § 71.02(2) imposed a nondiscriminatory franchise tax on corporations, it was excepted from the exemption for stocks and obligations of the federal government extended by 31 U.S.C.S. § 3142.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment for respondents.

 

1617 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kamin


No. 87-0470-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Two


142 Wis. 2d 937; 417 N.W.2d 197; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4142



October 7, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Final Disposition by Denial of Review March 8, 1988


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Kenosha county: DAVID M. BASTIAN, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of operating a motor vehicle after revocation of his operating privileges in violation of Wis. Stat. § 343.44(1). He appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), contending that the trial court had no jurisdiction over him because the State of Wisconsin could not deprive him of his constitutional right to travel the public roads.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped by a police officer for speeding. When asked for his driver's license, defendant explained his belief that he was not required to be licensed by the State in order to exercise his constitutional right to travel. He presented a typed document entitled "Constitutional license" and was arrested and cited for operating a motor vehicle after revocation. The court held that § 343.44 was constitutional. The licensing requirement did not interrupt the right to pass. Wis. Stat. § 343.05(2)(c) specifically exempted nonresidents licensed in other states from the requirement of a Wisconsin license. Thus, there was no provision of Wisconsin Law that interfered with the right to travel guaranteed by the United States Constitution. Further, the driving of a motor vehicle upon public highways was a privilege, not a right, and thus was subject to reasonable regulation under the State's police power in the interest of public safety and welfare. That police power was exercised by enacting Wis. Stat. § 343.05(1)(a), which established a policy that no person could operate a motor vehicle upon a highway in the State unless a license had been issued that had had not been revoked.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1618 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Fillbach v. Prod. Credit Ass'n


No. 86-0714


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


141 Wis. 2d 767; 416 N.W.2d 617; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4154


April 10, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
September 24, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Crawford county: Kent C. Houck, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sheriffs sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Crawford County (Wisconsin), which granted the motion for summary judgment of respondents, a corporation and an association, in the sheriffs' action to recover on a bond their legal expenses from a replevin action.


OVERVIEW: In a replevin action, a complaint against the sheriffs for seizing certain cattle and farm equipment was dismissed. The sheriffs then filed an action on the bond issued by the corporation pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 810.03, to recover their legal expenses. The trial court granted the corporation and the association's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment, holding that the bond required the corporation and the association to indemnify the sheriffs for their legal expenses in the district court. The court ruled that since § 810.03 does not expressly prohibit a sheriff from demanding indemnification, if a sheriff has a reasonable doubt regarding the lawfulness of the replevin ordered by the court, the sheriff may ask the replevin plaintiff for indemnification. The sheriffs' complaint pled the issuance of the bond, the replevin, the federal district court action and its disposition, and the sheriffs' expenses in defending the action; thus, it stated a claim. The court concluded that the answer to the complaint stated a defense and raised issues of material fact. Therefore, the case was remanded for denial of the motion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment. The case was remanded for dismissal of the motion.

 

1619 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Schlegel


No. 86-1989-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


141 Wis. 2d 512; 415 N.W.2d 164; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4109


August 13, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
September 17, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied. Petition for reconsideration denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Oneida county: James W. Karch, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Oneida County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of making two inconsistent statements under oath knowing that at least one was false in violation of Wis. Stat. § 946.32(1)(b). Defendant alleged that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction and that the State's failure to designate which statement was false denied his right to a unanimous jury verdict.


OVERVIEW: At a supplemental hearing to collect on a judgment against him, defendant testified that he did not know who owned a corporation and that he never owned that corporation. At a later John Doe hearing, defendant testified that he owned the corporation when certain property was transferred to the corporation. As a result, defendant was convicted of violating Wis. Stat. § 946.32(10(b) by knowingly making inconsistent statements under oath. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that defendant was the only incorporator of the corporation and its sole shareholder for over one month. Although the property was transferred before the Wisconsin Secretary of State issued the certificate of incorporation, the jury was entitled to consider matters occurring after the date of transfer to determine defendant's knowledge. The statements made at the two hearings directly contradicted each other. Thus, the circumstantial evidence was sufficient to show that defendant knew that one statement was false. The State was not required to elect which statement was false in order to ensure a unanimous jury verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1620 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re Custody of L.J.G.


No. 86-1197


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


141 Wis. 2d 503; 415 N.W.2d 564; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4122


June 3, 1987, Argued  
September 17, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: Angela B. Bartell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of the visitation provisions of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin). The trial court had awarded custody of the mother's minor child to respondent father.


OVERVIEW: The trial court limited the mother's visitation to visits within the State of Wisconsin. On appeal, the mother claimed that the trial court lacked authority to limit a non-custodial parent's visitation to in-state visits and that the trial court abused its discretion in imposing the limitation on the facts of the case and by limiting visitation without a showing of a threat to the child's physical, mental, or emotional health. The court affirmed the trial court's order. Under Wis. Stat. § 767.245(1), non-custodial parents were entitled to reasonable visitation. They did not have an inviolate right to any particular visitation arrangement. That Wis. Stat. § 767.245(6) provided that the non-custodial parent had the right to seek to prohibit the custodial parent from removing the child from the state for extended periods of time did not mean that the legislature intended to deny a court the power to limit visitation to a particular geographic area, and such a limitation did not unconstitutionally infringe upon the mother's right to travel. The trial court applied the correct standard, the best interests of the child, in determining visitation rights and did not abuse its discretion.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1621 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Ripley v. Brown


No. 86-2027


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


141 Wis. 2d 447; 415 N.W.2d 550; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4092


May 11, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
September 15, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Washburn county: Dennis C. Bailey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff would-be candidate appealed a summary judgment of the Circuit Court for Washburn County (Wisconsin), which dismissed his action to compel the County and its Clerk to place the office of county surveyor on the general election ballot for a particular year. The main issue was whether Wis. Stat. § 59.12, as amended by 1969 Wis. Laws 499, § 1, was unconstitutional under Wis. Const. art. VI, § 4, as amended 1882.


OVERVIEW: Section 59.12, as amended, provided that a county could appoint a surveyor in lieu of electing one. On appeal, the court noted that art. VI, § 4, as amended, had been declared to be ambiguous in a 1907 Wisconsin Supreme Court decision because, if read literally, it would work an absurd or unreasonable result by impliedly repealing the appointment powers granted the legislature in Wis. Const. art. XIII, § 9. The court construed art. XIII, § 9 together with art. VI, § 4 in order to harmonize the provisions. Under the Supreme Court's decision, the phrase "all other county officers" in art. VI, § 4 included all those officers considered as elected county officials under the constitution and the early statutes. After 1882, the previously statutorily elected county officers became constitutionally elected officers, and the legislature could create new county offices under Wis. Const. art. XIII, § 9 and fill them as they saw fit. But the court pointed out that the office of county surveyor had existed since 1849 and had constitutional status. A 1982 amendment of art. VI, § 4 merely clarified existing law. The court referenced other external sources in support of its analysis.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

 

1622 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Bruflat v. Board of Zoning Appeals


No. 86-1156


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District One


141 Wis. 2d 974; 414 N.W.2d 318; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3979



August 25, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County, ELLIOT N. WALSTEAD, Judge. Affirmed in part, reversed in part and caused remanded.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed in part, reversed in part and cause remanded to the Board for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant business owners sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which affirmed respondent Board of Zoning Appeals of the City of Milwaukee's denial of a zoning variance to allow operation of a cat shelter in a residence and local business zoning district.


OVERVIEW: The trial court upheld the Board's denial of the business owners' request for a zoning variance to operate a cat shelter. On appeal, the judgment was affirmed as to the denial of the variance. The court ruled that because Milwaukee, Wis., Ordinance § 78-1 (1979) afforded proper notice, and because there was a reasonable basis in the evidence for the Board's determination that the owners' facility had a detrimental impact on the appropriate use of abutting properties and the neighborhood. The court remanded for further proceedings, because the Board failed to determine whether the facility was a pet shop or a kennel. The court held that § 78-1 was written with sufficient clarity to allow citizens to reasonably recognize what precise activity was regulated and to demonstrate to those who enforce the ordinance what type of activity to regulate. The court concluded that the burden of proof had not been met; thus, the constitutional challenge for vagueness failed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Board's order denying the zoning variance. The case was remanded to the Board for further proceedings on the issue of whether the facility was a pet shop or a kennel.

 

1623 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Waupoose v. Flad & Associates, Inc.


No. 86-2114


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Three


141 Wis. 2d 975; 414 N.W.2d 319; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3981



August 25, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Final Disposition By Denial of Review October 20, 1987


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Brown county, CHARLES KUEHN, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action for personal injuries based on negligence in the design and supervision of a sawmill renovation, plaintiff employee appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Brown County (Wisconsin), which granted defendants' motion for summary judgment on the grounds that the suit was not commenced within six years of substantial completion of the renovation as required by Wis. Stat. § 893.89.


OVERVIEW: The employee of the mill was standing on the upper endless belt when the conveyors were set into motion causing him to fall backward onto the conveyor belt. Unable to free himself, he was pulled into the machinery, which amputated his leg. He brought suit against various defendants, based on negligence in the design and supervision of the sawmill renovation. This action was filed more than six years following the substantial completion of the renovation. Defendants filed a motion for summary judgment on the grounds that the suit was not commenced within six years of substantial completion as required by Wis. Stat. § 893.89. The trial court granted the motion and dismissed the action. The employee appealed. The court affirmed after it concluded that the machinery and equipment, specifically the conveyor system, were improvements to real estate as defined by § 893.89. The conveyor system increased the value of the real estate, and while it could have been removed without damage to the property, it functioned as an integral component of the entire manufacturing process. The court also held that the statute was constitutional because it was unambiguous and not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the employee's personal injury action based on negligence in the design and supervision of the sawmill renovation brought against various defendants.

 

1624 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Geiger


No. 87-0320-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Three


141 Wis. 2d 976; 414 N.W.2d 320; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4008



August 25, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Final Disposition By Denial of Review January 12, 1988


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Taylor county: DOUGLAS T. FOX, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant farmer appealed from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Taylor County (Wisconsin), which found him guilty of producing milk not properly protected from filth, dust, or other contaminants contrary to Wis. Stat. § 97.10(2). The farmer challenged the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 97.12(2) that authorized the search and asserted that the search conducted was a violation of his federal and state constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: The Wisconsin Department of Agriculture received a complaint that the farmer's milk contained excessive amounts of sediments and other particles. Department agents arrived at the farm at approximately 11 a.m., introduced themselves, and inspected the dairy barn, milkhouse, and milking equipment, taking photographs and specimens. The farmer challenged the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 97.12(1), which authorized the agents to inspect and obtain samples at his barn and milkhouse, alleging that it violated his right to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures under the Fourth Amendment and Wis. Const. art. I, § 1, and that it was unconstitutionally overbroad because it authorized searches of private homes and vague because the terms "farm" and "places" were indefinite. The court disagreed, finding the statute to be constitutional. There was a substantial interest in keeping the marketplace free from contaminants to protect the public's health. Milk production was a closely regulated industry. The inspection was conducted at a reasonable time and limited to those areas that were involved in milk production. The farmer's overbreadth and vagueness arguments were rejected.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and order.

State v. Wheeler


No. 86-0183-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


141 Wis. 2d 973; 414 N.W.2d 318; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4036



August 20, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Final Disposition By Denial of Review December 14, 1987


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: MARK A. FRANKEL, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in a child support dispute with his ex-wife. When the ex-wife refused to allow defendant to visit with their children, defendant told the wife that she should be shot. Defendant's hairdresser told defendant that he had a friend that could take care of his problem. Defendant told the friend that he wanted to get the ex-wife off his back. Defendant's wife mailed cash to the friend along with a picture of the ex-wife. The friend killed the ex-wife. The friend testified that defendant asked him to kill the ex-wife. Defendant testified that he hired the friend to scare his ex-wife. The friend pled guilty to first-degree murder, while defendant and his hairdresser were convicted of first-degree murder. On review, the court affirmed. The court held that based on the evidence the trial court did not abuse its discretion in refusing to instruct on aiding and abetting because the thrust of the evidence was clearly on conspiracy. Given the friend's admission that he intended to kill the ex-wife, it would have been unreasonable for the trial court to instruct on felony-murder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Akre v. Labor & Industry Review Com.


No. 87-0257


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


141 Wis. 2d 976; 414 N.W.2d 319; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3988



August 13, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION -- REFER TO THE LOCAL RULE 809.23(3)


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Final Disposition By Denial of Review January 19, 1988


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Green county: Franz W. Brand, Judge, Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Green County (Wisconsin), which affirmed an order of the Wisconsin Labor and Industry Review Commission that reduced the employee's permanent partial disability benefits by 50 percent because of his age.


OVERVIEW: The employee was injured in the course of his employment. Because he was age 77 at the time the injury occurred, the Commission, upon his filing for worker's compensation benefits, reduced the employee's permanent partial disability award by 50 percent pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 102.53(2). The employee sought judicial review, contending that his claim was not controlled by Wis. Stat. § 102.53(2) because the statute had since been repealed and that he had filed his claim after such repeal date. The trial court affirmed the Commission's order. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court ruled that Wis. Stat. § 102.53(2) was applicable because the employee's rights to compensation vested and the obligation for payment was fixed as of the date of his injury, not the date that he filed his claim for benefits. The court noted that the legislature was precluded from enacting retrospective laws which impaired vested rights acquired under prior law or which created new obligations regarding past transactions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1627 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Graf


Nos. 86-2008, 86-2009


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


140 Wis. 2d 867; 412 N.W.2d 902; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3906



July 30, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Monroe county: JAMES W. RICE, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Monroe County (Wisconsin), which convicted her of operating a motor vehicle after her driving privileges were suspended under Wis. Stat. § 343.44(1), and operating an unregistered vehicle, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 341.04(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that the circuit court erred in denying her motions to dismiss the charges under Wis. Stat. §§ 343.44(1) and 341.04(1) as a matter of law for lack of jurisdiction. Defendant alleged that the state driver licensing and registration requirements interfered with her right to drive on public highways. The court concluded that the circuit court had subject matter jurisdiction and affirmed defendant's convictions and the denial of her motions. The court was bound by the state supreme court's decision that citizens did not have a constitutional right and had only a privilege to drive automobiles on public highways. The licensing requirement did not completely lack a reasonable basis because it appeared to increase the likelihood that drivers were competent and responsible. The court held that defendant was not denied due process of law because she acknowledged that she had timely notice when she received two written traffic citations and notice of the return dates. Defendant failed to make a timely appearance at the hearing date or to reschedule the hearing on the citations, and there was no need for the appearance when she did not contest the facts of the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against defendant.

State v. Gulrud


No. 86-1610-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


140 Wis. 2d 721; 412 N.W.2d 139; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3920; 81 A.L.R.4th 1063


March 10, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
July 16, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: Michael B. Torphy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of three counts of second-degree sexual assault, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.225(2)(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the alleged assaults consisted of a single consensual act of vaginal intercourse, that he did not physically harm the victim, and that the injuries claimed by the victim were inflicted by a third party. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court concluded that evidence that the victim had sexual intercourse with another man after the alleged assault was inadmissible under Wis. Stat. § 972.11(2)(b)2. Defendant's right to confrontation was not violated by the exclusion of the evidence because its slight probative value was substantially outweighed by the danger of unfair prejudice and was properly excluded under Wis. Stat. § 904.03.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Robinson


No. 86-1789-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


140 Wis. 2d 673; 412 N.W.2d 535; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3936


May 5, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
July 14, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Michael D. Guolee, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed orders of the Circuit Court of Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of robbery while possessing a dangerous weapon in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 943.32(1)(b), 939.63(1)(a)(2), false imprisonment while possessing a dangerous weapon in violation of §§ 940.30, 939.63(1)(a)(4), and possession of a firearm by a felon in violation of § 941.29(1)(a), (2) and denied his request for a new trial or to vacate the judgment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that he was denied due process because the robbery charge was improperly enhanced under § 939.63(1)(a)(2), which resulted in his conviction for robbery while possessing a dangerous weapon. In addition, he contended that he was denied his state and federal due process rights when the prosecutor raised the issue of his post-arrest silence during both cross-examination and closing argument. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's convictions. The court held that the issue of whether § 939.63 could be used in conjunction with § 943.32 was a question of statutory construction, which was a question of law. The court found that both statutes were clear and unambiguous. The court held that § 939.63 could be applied to a charge of robbery under § 943.32(1) so defendant was not denied due process when he was convicted under both §§ 943.32(1)(b), 939.63(1)(a)(2).The court ruled that the prosecutor's comments did not infringe on defendant's due process rights under the state and federal constitutions to remain silent because the comments were aimed at defendant's credibility and were not aimed at his silence at the time of arrest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

In re Paternity of C.A.S.


No. 86-1207


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


140 Wis. 2d 863; 411 N.W.2d 428; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3816



June 25, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Final Disposition By Denial of Review August 18, 1987


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: ANGELA B. BARTELL, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, mother, husband, and children by their guardian ad litem, sought review of the order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which required them and respondent putative father to submit to blood tests to determine the paternity of the children. The trial court also denied appellants' motions to dismiss the putative father's paternity action and for summary judgment recognizing the husband as the father of the children.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether the trial court erred in ordering the blood tests or denying the motions. The court rejected appellants' contention that the paternity statutes should be construed to require a finding that continuation of the action was in the child's best interest before a blood test could be ordered. The court dismissed appellants' contention that the constitutional rights of an unmarried male who has not been adjudicated a father depended on his participation in the rearing of his child. The court held that if it was determined that the putative father was the children's father, the best interest of the child standard would be applied before the putative father was afforded custody or visitation. The court held that the trial court's interpretation of Wis. Stat. § 767.48(1) did not deprive appellants of due process. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment when it denied the motion for judgment on the pleadings as material facts were disputed in the putative father's petition and the mother's response as to whether the putative father was the father.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which ordered appellants and the putative father to submit to blood tests and denied their motions for summary judgment and judgment on the pleadings.

 

1631 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Fritsch v. General Acci. Ins. Co.


No. 85-2190


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


140 Wis. 2d 862; 411 N.W.2d 428; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3823



June 25, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Final Disposition By Denial of Review November 10, 1987


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Portage county, FREDERIC W. FLEISHAUER, Judge. Affirmed in part and reversed in part with directions.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed in part and affirmed in part with directions; order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Portage County (Wisconsin), which dismissed an inverse condemnation action against respondent town and granted costs to the town.


OVERVIEW: The landowners appealed from a judgment dismissing their inverse condemnation action against the town and from an order granting cost to the town. The dispute concerned a town road which was mistakenly laid out so that it encroached on a strip of land owned. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment in part. The court held that based on the undisputed facts, the landowners had no cause of action against the town, and a reasonable and impartial jury could come to no other conclusion. Because the court found nothing in the statutes or the case law which prohibited portions of the same public highway from being created under both Wis. Stat. § 80.01(1) and (2), the court rejected the landowners' argument that the town could not legally acquire the land when it laid out the road. The trial court erred in giving the town title to the land upon which the road encroached. Absent a statute expressly providing for acquisition of title, or a deed expressly conveying title, the landowner retained title to the underlying land when a road was established by prescription or adverse use. The public acquired only an easement to use the land.


OUTCOME: The order of the lower court dismissing the landowners' inverse condemnation action was reversed to the extent that it gave title to land upon which the road encroached to the town.

 

1632 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Crowley


No. 86-0432-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


140 Wis. 2d 862; 411 N.W.2d 428; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3827



June 25, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION -- REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(3)


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Granted August 18, 1987


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Crawford county: MICHAEL KIRCHMAN, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Crawford County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of aggravated battery in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.19(3)(b). Defendant also appealed from the trial court's denial of his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant battered his victim as he was walking home from a tavern. The victim, who was 48 years old, was four feet nine inches tall, weighed 90 pounds, had poor eyesight, and wore thick glasses. The victim testified that defendant took his glasses off and struck him twice in the face. A physician testified that the victim's injuries would create a high probability of death. Defendant was convicted and appealed. He argued that the trial court erred in instructing the jury on the victim's disability. The court held that defendant's failure to object to the instructions waived his right to challenge them. The court rejected defendant's argument that the evidence was insufficient to convict. The direct evidence of the victim's injuries from the victim's and the physician's testimony sustained the conviction. Moreover, the physician's testimony that the victim had a discernible physical disability would also have allowed the jury to presume the ultimate fact that defendant's conduct created a high probability of great bodily harm to the victim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the judgment of the trial court.

 

1633 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Potosnyak


No. 86-0156-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Two


140 Wis. 2d 862; 411 N.W.2d 428; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3812



June 17, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Final Disposition By Denial of Review October 20, 1987


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Waukesha county: HARRY G. SNYDER, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin) that convicted her of homicide by intoxicated use of a motor vehicle in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.09(1)(a) and from an order that denied her any postconviction relief. An issue presented on appeal was whether or not rejection of the defense based on Wis. Stat. § 940.09(2) was sufficiently supported by evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the victim had suddenly moved into the roadway so that his death would have ensued, regardless of whether or not she was under the influence of an intoxicant or had a certain blood-alcohol level. Wis. Stat. § 940.09(2) provided an affirmative defense if the death would have happened regardless of intoxication. The court found based on an eyewitness and a pathologist's testimony that the victim had been dragged a substantial distance before defendant stopped her car. This testimony supported the inference that the intoxication caused defendant not to stop immediately after impact and that the dragging contributed to the death. The court stated the jury's rejection of the defense of § 940.09(2) was supported by sufficient evidence. The court rejected defendant's other arguments, including one that posited that it was an error for the trial court to refuse her request to instruct the jury on the emergency doctrine and avoidability of accidents. The court ruled that those instructions were proper for civil cases but not justified in this case because a driver's negligent operation of a vehicle was not an element of the crime defined by Wis. Stat. § 940.09.


OUTCOME: Ruling against defendant, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment and order.

 

1634 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Flakes


No. 86-1248-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


140 Wis. 2d 411; 410 N.W.2d 614; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3851


April 7, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
June 12, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Janine P. Geske, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of second-degree murder, second degree sexual assault, and that denied his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a parolee, was arrested for selling marijuana to an undercover officer. The police sought permission to search defendant's apartment, but he denied such permission. Two days later, the police told defendant's parole agent of the new arrest. The parole agent searched defendant's apartment and discovered the nude body of a 14-year-old boy in the closet. Defendant gave a confession in which he admitted that he killed the boy while the two were engaged in anal intercourse. At the trial, because the State failed to prove second-degree sexual assault with a person whom defendant knew to be unconscious, the State was allowed to amend the information to charge second-degree sexual assault, sexual contact or sexual intercourse with a person contrary to Wis. Stat. § 940.225(2)(e) to conform to the proof. Defendant was convicted of second degree murder and second-degree sexual assault. His postconviction motion was denied. On review, defendant's major assertion was that the amendment to the information was error. The court affirmed. The court held that defendant's ability to defend himself was not prejudiced by the amendment; therefore, he was not prejudiced by the amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and the denial of his postconviction relief.

Coe v. Board of Regents


No. 85-2030


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


140 Wis. 2d 261; 409 N.W.2d 166; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3711


February 25, 1987, Argued  
May 26, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review filed. This petition was not decided at the time the volume went to press. Its disposition will be reported in a later volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Portage county: Robert C. Jenkins, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner former professor appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Portage County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision by respondent, the Board of Regents of the University of Wisconsin System, not to hold a formal hearing to review the chancellor's denial of tenure to the professor. On appeal, the professor contended that faculty members who had been denied tenure had rights under Wis. Admin. Code § UWS ch. 3.


OVERVIEW: The professor had a series of yearly probationary contracts for seven years; the eighth year was her "up or out" year in which she had to become tenured or her employment with the university would terminate. The chancellor decided not to renew her employment or grant tenure. The professor argued that she met the tenure criteria set in Wis. Admin. Code § UWS 3.06(1)(b). She also argued that because tenure density was not an enumerated criterion, the chancellor exceeded his authority in considering it. On appeal, the court affirmed. It concluded that the chancellor properly applied the tenure criteria and that the professor had not met the requirements for a contested case hearing, as set forth in Wis. Stat. § 227.064(1) (1981-82). The court found that the professor had merely a "unilateral expectation" of becoming tenured, not a "substantial interest." Furthermore, a contested case hearing before the Board regarding the denial of tenure was not required because the legislature intended to deny nonrenewed probationary faculty members a hearing, having specified in § 227.064(1) when such a hearing was required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

State v. Robinette


No. 86-2182-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Two


140 Wis. 2d 861; 409 N.W.2d 671; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3718



May 20, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Final Disposition By Denial of Review October 13, 1987


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Waukesha county: ROGER P. MURPHY, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the adverse decision of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which rendered a conviction judgment for his operation of a motor vehicle while intoxicated and operation with an illegal blood and breath concentration in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a), (b). Defendant contended the trial court erred in giving a jury instruction and that his trial counsel was ineffective.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought review of the trial court's conviction judgment and denial of his request for post-conviction relief for his violation of § 346.63(1)(a). Defendant asserted that the trial court gave a jury instruction which created a mandatory presumption, thereby reducing the state's burden of proof in violation of his due process rights. He also contended that he had ineffective assistance from his trial counsel. The court on appeal affirmed the conviction decision of the trial court based on its conclusion that, even though the trial court erred in its phrasing of the instruction about the concentration of alcohol in defendant's blood, the instruction did not improperly reduce the state's burden of proof because it did not deal with an elemental fact. Therefore, defendant's constitutional rights were not violated. As to an alleged statutory violation occasioned by the erroneous instruction, the court on appeal concluded that no prejudice resulted. The appellate court also determined that defendant's trial counsel was not ineffective and no prejudice was shown to have disadvantaged defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and order of the trial court.

State v. Coley


No. 86-0434


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


140 Wis. 2d 857; 409 N.W.2d 669; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3777



May 14, 1987, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: GEORGE A. NORTHROP, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion for a sentence reduction under Wis. Stat. § 974.06. He claimed that a five year prison sentence for the theft of two sheep was cruel and unusual punishment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a plea of no contest to the charge of stealing two sheep and agreed to the five year sentence with probation. When he violated the terms of his probation, it was revoked and the five year sentence was imposed. The trial court denied his motion for a sentence reduction, and on appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the sentence was not cruel or unusual punishment under either the Wisconsin or United States constitutions. The court concluded that the sentence was proportionate to the crime in light of defendant's extensive prior record and the fact that he had violated probation. Defendant's agreement to the sentence was also relevant in determining that the sentence was not unduly harsh. The court found that Wisconsin's penalty for theft of livestock was not extreme in relation to penalties for similar crimes in other states. The court refused to reverse in the interest of justice under Wis. Stat. § 752.35. Defendant was not entitled to use that statute to raise the issue of abuse of discretion in sentencing that could not have been raised in his motion to reduce the sentence under Wis. Stat. § 974.06.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

State v. Foust


No. 86-1491-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Three


140 Wis. 2d 859; 409 N.W.2d 670; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3762



May 12, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Door county: EDWIN STEPHAN, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Door County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of five counts of second-degree sexual assault. Defendant also appealed from the trial court's denial of his motion for post conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from his conviction and argued that comments made by the district attorney during closing arguments constituted plain error, and that the trial court improperly excluded evidence of the nature of the victim's prior sexual experience. The court held that some comments made by the district attorney were not error. Comments about the victim's credibility were hinged on the evidence adduced at trial and were not erroneous. The district attorney did not refer to defendant's silence, but to the absence of other evidence to impeach the State's witnesses. Some of the remarks were improper, such as derogatory remarks about the victim's mother, who was defendant's girlfriend. However, the remarks did not deprive defendant of a fair trial. The court held that evidence of a previous sexual assault on the victim was properly ruled inadmissible under the rape shield law, Wis. Stat. § 972.11(2).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the trial court's judgment.

Kohnke v. St. Paul Fire & Marine Ins. Co.


No. 86-0988


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


140 Wis. 2d 80; 410 N.W.2d 585; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3725


February 10, 1987, Orally argued  
May 12, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Eau Claire county: William D. O'Brien, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient sought review of a summary judgment from the Circuit Court for Eau Claire County (Wisconsin), which dismissed his medical malpractice action against defendants, a clinic and its insurer, for failing to file his claim within the statute of limitations, Wis. Stat. § 893.55(1)(b). Plaintiff wife appealed from the denial of her claim for loss of society and companionship.


OVERVIEW: The patient was allegedly rendered sterile during surgery performed when he was an infant. He first discovered his injury 22 years later when he sought medical advice for a fertility problem. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the clinic in the patient's medical malpractice action on the ground that the patient failed to file his claim within the statute of limitations, § 893.55(1)(b). On appeal, the court declared the statute unconstitutional in its application to the patient and reversed. Under § 893.55(1)(b), a medical malpractice claim could never be commenced more than five years from the act or omission. Thus, the patient's claim expired before he could have discovered his injury with reasonable diligence. Therefore, he was deprived of a remedy for his injuries contrary to Wis. Const. art. I, § 9. The court rejected a contention that the controlling statutes of limitation were those that existed at the time of the patient's injury. His medical malpractice claim did not accrue at the time of his injury but only after discovery. The court rejected the wife's claim for loss of society and companionship because it was raised but not briefed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment dismissing the patient's claim. It summarily rejected the wife's claim.

State v. Viken

Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Sauk County (Wisconsin). The trial court denied his motion to dismiss charges of violating Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a) by operating a motor vehicle under the influence of an intoxicant and Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(b) by operating a motor vehicle with a blood alcohol content of .10 percent or more. Defendant contended that the State had failed to timely prosecute the action.


OVERVIEW: Defendant first unsuccessfully moved to dismiss his case on the grounds that the statutes under which he was charged were unconstitutionally vague. The trial court adjourned the case until a ruling on appeal was made. For some reason, the trial court did not consider the case again for almost three years, when it denied defendant's second motion to dismiss for failure to prosecute. On review, defendant contended that the trial court had abused its discretion in denying his motion and had failed to adequately state its reasons for denial on the record. The court ruled that any speedy trial argument was misplaced and that while the reason for the delay was not clear on the record, it appeared that defendant's actions contributed to it. The court also noted that the record contained adequate evidence of the trial court's exercise of discretion, considering the extensive briefing and arguments of counsel.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.
