State v. Link


No. 86-0020


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


139 Wis. 2d 856; 407 N.W.2d 566; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3626



April 23, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Jackson county: ROBERT W. RADCLIFFE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Jackson County (Wisconsin) that denied his postconviction motions to dismiss a nonsupport charge under Wis. Stat. § 52.05(1) (1983) or in the alternative to withdraw his plea of nolo contendere. An issue on appeal was the constitutionality of § 52.05.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that § 52.05(1) was unconstitutional. Preliminarily, the court ruled that it was neither unconstitutional nor a violation of the equal protection of the laws. Regarding the motion to withdraw the plea, the court reviewed the trial court's denial of the motion for any abuse of discretion. Defendant argued that the trial court insufficiently explained the elements of the crime to him. The court refused to hold that the trial court had an unequivocal duty in every case to explain every element of the charged crime to the accused. The court determined that defendant understood the nature of the charge upon making the plea. The court relied on, inter alia, the written plea negotiation that defendant had signed, which included his admission that he understood that an inability to provide support was a defense to the allegations against him. The court rejected the contention that the record of the plea proceeding did not have an adequate explanation of the elements of the offense with which defendant had been charged. The court rejected defendant's other arguments.


OUTCOME: Ruling against defendant, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Drusch


No. 86-1580-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


139 Wis. 2d 312; 407 N.W.2d 328; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3634

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of two counts of first degree sexual assault in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.225(1)(d), and from an order denying his motions for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The issues were: (1) whether the trial court erred in allowing a transcript of the preliminary hearing testimony of one of the child victims to be read to the jury; (2) whether the evidence was sufficient to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant had sexual contact with the victims with the intent to become sexually aroused or gratified; (3) whether defendant's six-year sentence was so excessive and harsh as to constitute an abuse of the trial court's discretion; and (4) whether a new trial should have been ordered in the interest of justice. Defendant's motion for a new trial was also properly denied.


OUTCOME: The judgment and the order were affirmed.

State v. McCoy


No. 86-1992-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


139 Wis. 2d 291; 407 N.W.2d 319; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3613


March 2, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
April 21, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Barron county: James C. Eaton and Frederick A. Henderson, Judges.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Barron County (Wisconsin) convicting him of intentionally concealing two of his minor children from the other parent, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 946.715(1)(a), and denying his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was living in Wisconsin with his wife and three minor children. One day, defendant picked his two oldest children up from school and left the state. Defendant's wife obtained a divorce and custody of all three children. Defendant was charged with intentionally concealing the two older children from their mother. At trial, defendant argued that his actions were privileged because the children they were in danger of imminent physical harm. On appeal, defendant argued that § 946.715(2)(a) was unconstitutionally vague because it failed to specify what constituted "imminent physical harm." The court held that § 946.715(2)(a) was constitutional because it used common terms and sufficiently alerted a person of ordinary intelligence that if a child was in close danger of bodily injury, a parent could conceal that child from the other parent in order to protect the child from that danger. The trial court erred by including the words "necessary" and immediate" in its instruction because § 946.715(2)(a) did not contemplate the use of such terms within the context of the privilege. However, such error was harmless because the degree of danger was not at issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the trial court's denial of post-conviction relief.

Racine Steel Castings


No. 86-1016


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


139 Wis. 2d 232; 407 N.W.2d 299; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3668


November 11, 1986, Submitted on briefs  
April 9, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: George A. Burns, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant worker sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which ruled in favor of respondent employer in the employer's action for a declaratory judgment declaring Wis. Stat. § 102.29(3) unconstitutional insofar as it precluded an employer from sharing in the proceeds of a medical malpractice claim against a physician, chiropractor, or podiatrist.


OVERVIEW: The worker sustained a work-related injury. Medical treatment left him a quadriplegic; he was permanently and totally disabled. The worker settled a medical malpractice claim against his treating physician. The employer sought subrogation rights in the settlement because it was obligated to pay worker's compensation for the injury as enhanced by the physician's negligence. The trial court held that § 102.29(3) violated equal protection of the laws and was unconstitutional. The worker appealed. The court noted that § 102.29(3) denied subrogation to a limited class of employers: those whose employees' work related injuries were caused or aggravated by the negligent treatment of physicians, chiropractors, or podiatrists. All other employers whose employees' injuries were aggravated by a third party could recover under § 102.29(1). The court held that the limited application of § 102.29(3) denied certain employer equal protection of the law because it was arbitrary and not rationally related to a legitimate state interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Bond


No. 86-0593-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


139 Wis. 2d 179; 407 N.W.2d 277; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3663


December 16, 1986, Submitted on briefs  
April 8, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Green Lake county: Earl J. McMahon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from an order of the Circuit Curt for Green Lake County (Wisconsin), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss a prosecution for theft in violation of Wis. Stat. § 943.20(1)(a). The main issue was whether, after a prior dismissal of a charge of theft by fraud, Wis. Stat. § 943.20(1)(d), the subsequent prosecution for theft was unconstitutional because jeopardy had attached.


OVERVIEW: The original complaint contained three charges. After numerous amendments to the complaint and the information, the trial court engaged in a dialogue with the State and defendant, during which the State agreed to proceed only with the original information charging theft by fraud, Wis. Stat. § 943.20(1)(d), (3)(c), but broadening the theft by fraud charge to a longer time period. The prosecutor told the trial judge that he was not planning to recharge defendant in any way regarding the other counts and agreed with the judge's statement that the theft by fraud charge was the only charge that the prosecutor would be proceeding against defendant on. However, after the theft by fraud charge was dismissed, the State filed a new complaint against defendant alleging theft in violation of § 943.20(1)(a). On appeal, the court held that, under any standard of review, the State's promise not to recharge defendant barred the State from prosecuting him further on the same facts. A prosecutorial promise was considered binding and had to be fulfilled. The State's failure to keep its promise was a deprivation of defendant's right to due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

 

1646 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Grundman


No. 86-1570


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District One


138 Wis. 2d 528; 406 N.W.2d 172; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3580



March 26, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: ARLENE D. CONNORS, Judge. Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded with directions. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed in part, reversed in part and cause remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant driver appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied the driver's motions to dismiss and his request for an evidentiary hearing. The driver also appealed the trial court's order that declared the driver to be a habitual traffic offender under Wis. Stat. ch. 351, thereby revoking his operating privileges for five years.


OVERVIEW: The driver appealed the trial court's order, which revoked his operator's license for five years for being a habitual traffic offender. The court held that where the driver specifically raised the issue of whether due diligence was actually exercised prior to service by publication, the driver raised not only the legal issue of due diligence, but factual issues that could only be resolved by an evidentiary hearing. Thus, the trial court erred in failing to hold an evidentiary hearing on the issue of the trial court's personal jurisdiction over the driver. Wis. Stat. ch. 351 was not unconstitutionally vague because a person of ordinary intelligence was able to determine when he or she fell under ch. 351. Minor out-of-state traffic offenses could be used as a basis for convicting an individual as a habitual traffic offender in Wisconsin under the clear language of Wis. Stat. § 351.02(1)(c). The driver was not deprived of his right to a jury trial under Wis. Const. art. I, § 5 because habitual traffic offender proceedings were not known to the common law when the state constitution was passed; thus, there was no right to a jury trial in such proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which denied the driver's request for an evidentiary hearing on the issue of personal jurisdiction. The court remanded to the trial court with directions to hold an evidentiary hearing to determine whether the State exercised due diligence in its attempt to personally serve the driver prior to using service by publication. The court affirmed the remainder of the trial court's judgment.

First Bank Southeast, N.A. v. Bentkowski


No. 86-1386


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


138 Wis. 2d 283; 405 N.W.2d 764; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3523


January 29, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
March 25, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Kenosha county: William U. Zievers, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bank challenged an order from the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which denied the bank's motion for summary judgment on the bank's amended complaint against respondent parents under the parental liability statute, Wis. Stat. § 895.035 (1983-84), for the parents' son's forgery.


OVERVIEW: The parent's son forged withdrawal slips with the father's name and withdrew funds held in the parent's savings account with the bank. The bank restored the funds and filed an action seeking damages under § 895.035. The circuit court found that contributory negligence was a viable defense in the action and dismissed the bank's complaint. On appeal, the court concluded that the contributory negligence defense was not viable under § 895.035. The court held that the plain meaning of § 895.035 imposed an absolute liability, not subject to exceptions or defenses, on the parents of a minor child for that minor's wilful, malicious, or wanton acts. The court found that § 895.035 was a valid exercise of the State of Wisconsin's police power and that it raised no due process implications.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment and remanded the action.

Brown County v. Wisconsin Employment Relations Com.


Nos. 86-0731, 86-0732


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


138 Wis. 2d 254; 405 N.W.2d 752; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3579


November 20, 1986, Submitted on briefs  
March 24, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Brown county: Charles D. Heath, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Brown County (Wisconsin), which affirmed an order of respondent Employment Relations Commission. The commission had concluded that that the county had committed a "prohibited practice," in violation of the Municipal Employment Relations Act (MERA) by refusing to bargain with respondent union concerning the employment of nonunion personnel in a youth home.


OVERVIEW: The county argued that because of the Commission's limited experience in like situations, the court should apply MERA to the facts without deference to the Commission. The court disagreed, finding the Commission's conclusion should be upheld. A private corporation responsible for the operation of a youth home, which had been previously run by the county, hired only one of the county's previous employees when it took over the group home. The court held that a rational basis supported the Commission's conclusion that the county's decision to subcontract its youth home services related primarily to wages, hours, or conditions of employment. When the county decided to move the youth home to a smaller location, it had a choice of employing its own personnel or employing personnel hired. Because the county chose to allow the private corporation to provide a nonbargaining unit staff for the new youth home, and because the new youth home's operation required essentially similar staff skills, the Commission had a rational basis for concluding that the county's decision primarily affected the county employees' wages, hours, or conditions of employment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1649 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Midwest Mut. Ins. Co. v. Nicolazzi


No. 86-0762


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


138 Wis. 2d 192; 405 N.W.2d 732; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3582


February 25, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
March 18, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Kenosha county: Bruce E. Schroeder, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insurer sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which entered judgment for plaintiffs, an individual and his insurer, in a property damage subrogation case. The judgment was entered on stipulations after the trial court struck defendant's defense that the insured vehicle was used without the owner's permission because defendant failed to comply with Wis. Stat. § 344.15(4) and (5) (1983-84).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs' action alleged that a vehicle insured by defendant struck the individual's vehicle. Defendant attempted to comply with Wis. Stat. § 344.15 (1983-84), which required it to advise the Department of Transportation if there was no coverage because the vehicle was driven without the owner's permission, by filing a statement signed by the vehicle's owner. The statement was rejected because the signature was not notarized. On appeal, the court held that the statute was mandatory and that the doctrine of substantial compliance was not applicable. The statute was mandatory because it was: (1) clear and unambiguous, (2) included a penalty for noncompliance, (3) was not a remedial statute, and (4) was directed to private individuals who controlled their own compliance with the statute. Because the deadline was part of the statute's substance, filing the notarized affidavit after the deadline was not substantial compliance. The court refused to address defendant's constitutional arguments because defendant failed to notify the state attorney general, a prerequisite to such a challenge, and failed to adequately brief the issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's determination that defendant was estopped from asserting the defense of non-permissive use in plaintiffs' action to recover property damage caused in a motor vehicle accident.

State v. Dennis


No. 86-1130-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


138 Wis. 2d 99; 405 N.W.2d 711; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3578


October 6, 1986, Submitted on briefs  
March 10, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment 1 of the circuit court for Barron county: James A. Wendland, Judge.


1 For purposes of appeal, the order is construed to be a final judgment. Section 808.03, Stats.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Barron County (Wisconsin), which dismissed a criminal complaint against defendant for bail jumping, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 946.49(1)(a), for driving without a valid license.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was twice charged with operating a motor vehicle after his driving privileges had been revoked. Defendant was granted bail, but a condition of bail was that he was not to drive without a valid license. Defendant violated that condition and was charged with bail jumping. Defendant contended that the restriction was unconstitutionally imposed. The trial court dismissed the complaint for bail jumping. The State sought review. The court reversed the dismissal, holding that the bond condition complied with Wis. Const. art. I, § 8(2), by serving to protect the community from serious bodily harm. Due to the danger to property and person, the public rightfully demanded freedom from reckless motor vehicle operators. No double jeopardy interests were implicated by the bail jumping charge.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the criminal complaint against defendant for bail jumping.

 

1651 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Brooks v. Labor & Industry Review Com.


No. 86-0314


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


138 Wis. 2d 106; 405 N.W.2d 705; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3535


September 15, 1986, Submitted on briefs  
March 10, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Forest county: James W. Karch, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Forest County (Wisconsin), which affirmed the decision of respondent, a state labor and industry review commission, to deny the employee's application for unemployment compensation benefits, on the ground that his physical limitations rendered him unavailable for work in his labor market area, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 108.04(2)(a) and Wis. Admin. Code ILHR § 128 (1984).


OVERVIEW: After 40 years of employment with respondent employer, the employee was laid off from his job. The employee sought unemployment compensation benefits, and an investigation revealed that he had a heart condition, which restricted the type of work he could do. At a hearing on the employee's application, a job counselor familiar with the employee's labor market testified that he was only physically able to perform about 10 percent of all available jobs in the area. For this reason, the commission denied the employee's request for benefits. On appeal from the circuit court's affirmance of the commission's decision, the employee contended that the compensation eligibility standard provided by Wis. Stat. § 108.04(2)(a) and Wis. Admin. Code ILHR § 128 (1984), which rendered persons ineligible for benefits if they were limited to less than 15 percent of the opportunities available in the area, violated the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. The court determined that the eligibility standard did not violate equal protection principles because the standard created a reasonable classification to ensure a solvent state compensation fund.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order.

In re Paternity of T.A.H.

OVERVIEW: The mother of a child, an unmarried woman, became pregnant and applied for AFDC. The State brought a paternity action against three men. The alleged progenitor failed to make an offer of proof regarding the mother's alleged other sexual encounter with a fourth man.

State v. Johnson

Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District One


137 Wis. 2d 650; 405 N.W.2d 84; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3464

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: ARLENE D. CONNORS, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which revoked his operating privileges for refusing to submit to a chemical test for intoxication under Wis. Stat. § 343.305.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for drunk driving. His operating privileges were revoked under Wis. Stat. § 343.305 for refusing to submit to a chemical test for intoxication. On appeal, the judgment was affirmed. The court held that defendant had no standing to raise the constitutionality of Wis. Const. art. In re Finding of Contempt in Interest of J.S.


Nos. 85-2172, 85-2379


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


137 Wis. 2d 217; 404 N.W.2d 79; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3425


December 12, 1986, Submitted on briefs  
February 11, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from orders of the circuit court for Racine county: Dennis J. Barry, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Orders reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parent challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin) finding the parent in contempt pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 48.25, and committing her for that contempt because she would not complete a residential rehabilitation program.


OVERVIEW: The parent had been committed for drug treatment in a residential rehabilitation program, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 48.45. However, she did not complete the program. Ultimately, the court found her in contempt and placed her in jail, except for the time she spent in the rehabilitation program. The parent contended that such commitments were governed exclusively by Wis. Stat. § 51.001 and that the trial court's actions deprived her of her constitutional rights. The county alleged that, under its inherent powers, it was authorized to take the action that it did, and that Wis. Stat. § 48.45 was the applicable statute. The court found that it was the legislature's intent to unify the system to combat drug and alcohol disorders by Wis. Stat. § 51.001. Further, no class of citizens was exempt from that statute's mandates. Thus, § 51.001 applied, and it preempted other legislation regarding involuntary commitments. Therefore, the trial court erred. Additionally, the inherent powers of the county did not apply because the commitment of the parent was not necessary in light of available alternatives.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the involuntary commitment order.

 

1655 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Petersen v. Dane County


No. 85-1340


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


136 Wis. 2d 501; 402 N.W.2d 376; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3337


September 4, 1986, Submitted on briefs  
January 27, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: Richard W. Bardwell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which affirmed defendant town's decision disapproving his petition for rezoning a two-acre parcel of land that was zoned for exclusive agricultural use to permit residential uses.


OVERVIEW: The landowner's lot was created by a predecessor in title's illegal split-off of two acres from a 10-acre parcel zoned for agriculture use. The landowner purchased the lot knowing that the predecessor had not complied with a county ordinance requiring an approved certified survey map. The circuit court found that the landowner was estopped from seeking rezoning because of the predecessor's failure to obtain an approved map. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment against the landowner despite the circuit court's erroneous conclusion that the town board could disapprove a rezoning application due to the absence of an approved map. The court upheld the town's decision to deny the rezoning request due to highway safety and erosion reasons and to limit residential development pursuant to the town's land use plan. By failing to prove that no profitable use could be made of lots less than 35 acres, the landowner was unable to challenge the constitutionality of the agricultural zoning classification. The landowner could not prematurely claim monetary damages for a regulatory taking because his hardship was self-created and he had not sought a variance or claimed inverse condemnation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment affirming the denial of the landowner's petition for rezoning.

State v. Dempsey


No. 86-0924-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Two


136 Wis. 2d 557; 402 N.W.2d 390; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3407



January 26, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Final Disposition by Denial of Reviews, March 10, 1987


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Walworth county: JAMES CARLSON, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Walworth County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a jury verdict finding him guilty of driving a motor vehicle without a driver's license in violation of Wis. Stats. § 343.05(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of driving a motor vehicle without a driver's license. On appeal, he contended that as a free white sovereign citizen, he could discriminately pick and choose which federal, state, and local laws to obey and could repudiate those that he disliked. He also argued that the trial court had no personal jurisdiction over him. In affirming, the court held that (1) the trial court had personal jurisdiction over defendant; (2) reasonable State regulation concerning the operation of motor vehicles on the highways, such as Wis. Stat. § 343.05(1)(a) that required a valid driver's license to operate a motor vehicle, was proper under the State's police power; (3) defendant was not exempt from the drivers' licensing requirements; and (4) defendant failed to prove that the licensing statutes violated either his due process or equal protection rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, which found defendant guilty of driving a motor vehicle without a driver's license.

Village of Shorewood v. Pleva


Nos. 86-0830, 86-0981-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District One


136 Wis. 2d 557; 402 N.W.2d 390; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3397



January 14, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: CHARLES B. SCHUDSON, Judge. Reversed and remanded. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Orders reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which dismissed a criminal complaint against defendant for operating a motor vehicle under the influence of an intoxicant, second offense, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1). Appellant village sought review of the order denying its motion to vacate a judgment convicting defendant of a first-offense violation of a similar municipal ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The State appealed an order dismissing its criminal complaint against defendant for operating a motor vehicle under the influence of an intoxicant, second offense, and the village appealed an order denying its motion to vacate its judgment convicting defendant of a first-offense violation of a similar municipal ordinance. The court held that the trial court was without subject matter jurisdiction in the municipal matter. Hence, the court held that the judgment of conviction was void and that the State's criminal prosecution could proceed. Defendant's constitutional protections against double jeopardy were not violated by the State's criminal prosecution, as the State, rather than the village, had the exclusive authority to prosecute second offenses for driving while intoxicated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

1658 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Whiting


No. 86-0269-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


136 Wis. 2d 400; 402 N.W.2d 723; 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3339


August 14, 1986, Submitted on briefs  
January 13, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review pending. This petition was not decided at the time the volume went to press. Its disposition will be reported in a later volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and orders of the circuit court for Brown county: Alexander Grant, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment entered in the Circuit Court for Brown County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of first-degree murder and imposed a life sentence. Defendant also sought review of orders that denied post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued on appeal that the trial court erred by giving the party-to-a-crime instruction. The court concluded that the jury had sufficient evidence to infer beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant had either committed the murder or had aided and abetted a third person in murdering the victim. As to defendant's argument that he was prejudiced because the State did not indicate that it would request a party-to-the-crime instruction until after defendant rested his case without calling witnesses, the court ruled that the State had no duty to notify defendant of its intent to rely on the party-to-a-crime instruction where the evidence supporting such an instruction came to light in the middle of a trial. The court further ruled that the trial court did not err by admitting preliminary examination testimony of a witness who invoked the Fifth Amendment to the United States Constitution at trial where the jury had a reasonable basis for judging the reliability of the witness's prior statements. Also, the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion for a new trial in the interests of justice where defendant failed to show that the real controversy had not been tried.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and orders denying post-conviction relief.

 

1659 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. SHEARS


No. 85-1064


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


135 Wis. 2d 545; 401 N.W.2d 182; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4074



December 18, 1986, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Final Disposition by Denial of Reviews, April 7, 1987


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: WILLIAM EICH, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Circuit Court, Dane County, Wisconsin. The order denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 974.06 from his convictions for first-degree murder and armed robbery. Defendant argued: (1) the trial court lacked jurisdiction because the judge did not honor his request for substitution; (2) ineffective assistance of counsel; and, (3) erroneous jury instruction on intent.


OVERVIEW: The trial judge did not honor defendant's substitution request under Wis. Stat. § 971.20 (1971). While the request deprived the judge of authority to act further, it did not deprive the trial court of jurisdiction. Failure to honor the request for substitution was not a cognizable claim under Wis. Stat. § 974.06. The judge's insistence that an accomplice testify against defendant pursuant to a plea bargain did not show a bias against defendant. Attorneys from the same agency represented defendant and codefendants. Defendant did not raise the ineffective assistance issue at trial or in prior postconviction motions. He did not meet his burden to show that his defense was prejudiced by the multiple representation. The jury instruction on intent was harmless error at most. Defendant was charged under Wis. Stat. § 939.05(1) (1971) as a party to first-degree murder. He was implicated as part of a conspiracy to rob a tavern and was identified as a robbery participant. His personal intention to kill the victims who were shot during the robbery was irrelevant. He was liable for the robbery he agreed to commit and the murders that resulted as a natural and probable consequence.


OUTCOME: The order that denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief was affirmed.

 

1660 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Vonesh


No. 86-0540-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


135 Wis. 2d 477; 401 N.W.2d 170; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4108


September 4, 1986, Submitted on briefs  
December 18, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Rock County: Gerald W. Jaeckle, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecution appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin) that admitted two sexually-oriented notes written by the minor complainant into evidence in defendant's trial for first-degree sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: The prosecution argued that the trial court's order derived from an errant application of the rape shield law, Wis. Stat. § 972.11(2). Defendant prevailed. Section 972.11(2) was ambiguous, in that it was capable of being construed in two different ways by reasonably well-informed persons as to whether a written or verbal communication or expression having a sexual basis or connotation could be, or described as, conduct or behavior relating to sexual activities. The ambiguity of Wis. Stat. § 972.11(2) compelled a determination of the legislature's intent from the language of the statute in relation to its scope, history, context, subject matter, and the object sought to be accomplished. Legislative history was extrinsic evidence to be used in divining the legislature's intent. The court reviewed these sources and concluded that: (1) the act of writing about sexual desires or activities was not itself prior sexual conduct; (2) acts of composing or copying notes of a sexual basis or connotation were not prior sexual conduct; and (3) written expressions of sexual desires were not conduct or behavior. The notes were therefore admissible under § 972.11(2).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

STATE v. HIBBLER


No. 86-0423-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District One


135 Wis. 2d 546; 401 N.W.2d 183; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4115



December 17, 1986, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION -- REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(3).


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Final Disposition by Denial of Reviews, April 7, 1987


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit courts for Milwaukee county: JOHN F. FOLEY and MARVIN C. HOLZ, Judges. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of second-degree murder, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 940.02, and from an order denying his motion for a new trial. Defendant claimed that the trial court's refusal to instruct the jury on self-defense manslaughter was error.


OVERVIEW: At his trial on a charge of first-degree murder defendant contended that he believed that the person he shot to death had a gun and was going to shoot him, and that his use of deadly force was necessary to defend himself. Defendant's attorney requested that the trial court give Wis. JI--Criminal 1141, entitled "First Degree Murder -- Self-Defense Manslaughter." The trial court declined to give Instruction 1141, but instead used Wis. JI--Criminal 1140, although the Committee Comment to Instruction 1141 stated that Instruction 1140 was withdrawn and should not be used. Defendant's attorney did not specifically object to the use of Instruction 1140. Although defendant's counsel waived any objection he might have had to Instruction 1140, the court addressed and rejected defendant's contention that the erroneous instructions were so prejudicial as to constitute plain error justifying a reversal of his conviction. The ailing instruction by itself did not result in a conviction that violated due process, because the error, if any, was rendered harmless by other parts of the instructions, and there was no reasonable possibility that absent the error the verdict would have been different.


OUTCOME: The judgment and order were affirmed.

 

1662 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mann


No. 86-0042-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


135 Wis. 2d 420; 400 N.W.2d 489; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4084


November 17, 1986, Submitted on briefs  
December 4, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Kenosha county: David M. Bastian, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court, Kenosha County, Wisconsin, that convicted him of leaving the scene of an accident in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.67(1)(a), (c). Defendant argued that § 346.67 was unconstitutionally vague, that jury instructions were erroneous, that evidence was admitted in error, and that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had a car accident in which the other driver was injured. Defendant left the scene to get help. When he returned, he saw a trooper aiding the driver. He denied any involvement in the crash and left. Under § 346.67(1)(a),(c), defendant was required to remain at the scene until he gave his name to the driver or the person attending the driver's vehicle and provided reasonable assistance. He argued that the term "attending" was ambiguous. He claimed that he could not leave his name with the trooper because the trooper was attending the driver, not the driver's car. The court found that the failure to define the word "attending" did not offend due process. The jury's determination of "reasonable assistance" did not render § 346.67(1)(c) unconstitutionally vague. Defendant waived objections to jury instructions. The trial court properly allowed expert medical witnesses to base their opinions on since-deceased doctor's autopsy report. Defendant's right to confrontation was not violated. The evidence was sufficient to support findings that the trooper was "attending" the driver's vehicle and that defendant's silent departure violated § 346.67(1)(a). There was no error.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for leaving the scene of an accident was affirmed.

 

1663 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hurd


No. 86-0558-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


135 Wis. 2d 266; 400 N.W.2d 42; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3959


August 1, 1986, Submitted on briefs  
November 18, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Trempealeau county: Robert W. Radcliffe, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order reversed and cause remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant school administrator appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Trempealeau County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of failing to report suspected child abuse and from an order denying his motion for postconviction relief. The administrator argued on appeal that the charging statute, Wis. Stat. § 48.981, was unconstitutionally vague, and that the trial court erred by failing to instruct the jury on the wilful element of the offense.


OVERVIEW: An adult at the administrator's school was convicted of sexually assaulting boys who resided there. At trial, a school counselor testified that he had informed the administrator several times that the adult was making "advances" toward the boys. On appeal, the administrator argued that there was insufficient evidence to convict him of failing to report suspected child abuse. He also claimed that § 48.981's phrase "reasonable cause to suspect" was ambiguous and vague. The court concluded that § 48.981 was constitutional and that there was sufficient evidence to convict. The phrase "reasonable cause to suspect" was a readily understandable standard. The court reversed, however, because the trial court's error in failing to instruct on the wilful element of the offense violated the administrator's constitutional right to due process. As a result, the jury was allowed to convict the administrator simply because he had failed to report suspected child abuse. The State was required to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that the administrator had not only failed to report, but that he had done so "wilfully," as set forth in Wis. Stat. § 48.981(b).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and the order and remanded the cause for a new trial.

 

1664 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


POLKA-DOT DAIRY-TOM THUMB MKTS. v. VILLAGE OF ELLSWORTH


No. 86-0406


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Three


135 Wis. 2d 543; 401 N.W.2d 28; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3964



November 11, 1986, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Pierce county: ROBERT W. WING, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff retailer sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Pierce County (Wisconsin), which declared that an ordinance promulgated by defendant village was valid. The ordinance, Ellsworth, Wis., Code § 12.06(3)(a) (1980), limited "Class A" retailers' licenses for the sale of fermented malt beverages to retailers who primarily sold groceries.


OVERVIEW: The village refused to renew the retailer's license to sell fermented malt beverages to be consumed off the premises because the retailer failed to establish that it was "primarily" a grocery store as required by a recently enacted ordinance. On appeal of a judgment declaring the ordinance valid, the court affirmed. The court rejected the retailer's argument that the ordinance was enacted without authority because Wis. Stat. ch. 125 had preempted the subject matter. The village was authorized to regulate its local affairs by the Home Rule amendment, Wis. Const. art. XI, § 3 and by Wis. Stat. § 62.11(5). Additionally, Wis. Stat. § 125.10 specifically authorized the village to incorporate state law governing the sale of alcohol and to prescribe additional regulations not in conflict with Wis. Stat. ch. 125. The ordinance did not deny equal protection of the laws. No fundamental right or suspect classification was involved. The ordinance's limitation of a Class A license to those retailers who primarily sold groceries rationally related to the legitimate public purpose of limiting the availability of alcohol. Nor was the ordinance unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1665 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Jones v. Gerhardstein


No. 85-1718


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


135 Wis. 2d 161; 400 N.W.2d 1; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4113


August 5, 1986, Submitted on briefs  
October 28, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: John E. McCormick, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied their motion for class certification and dismissed for mootness their petitions for a writ of habeas corpus and for a declaratory judgment. The state public defender appealed from that part of the same judgment that denied its motion to intervene on petitioners' behalf.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners challenged the constitutionality of the Wisconsin statutes that permitted the forcible administration of psychotropic drugs to individuals who had been involuntarily committed under the Mental Health Act, but who had not been adjudged incompetent. Citing the fact that both petitioners had been released, the State moved to dismiss their claims for mootness. The trial court adopted, without comment, the State's claim that petitioners had failed to establish that they shared a common interest with other members of the proposed class in obtaining a judicial determination that psychotropic drugs were being unconstitutionally administered to them. In light of the State's concession that it had used, and would continue to use, psychotropic drugs on involuntarily committed individuals, regardless of their competency, the court reversed and concluded that the putative class shared a common interest and that the trial court's finding in this matter were clearly erroneous. The court held that the unauthorized use of psychotropic drugs to treat mental illness not only infringed upon the right to bodily autonomy, but could also cause actual harm due to adverse side effects.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's discretionary judgment on the intervention issue. The court reversed on all other issues because petitioners' claim fell within a well-established exception to the mootness rule. The trial court misused its discretion in denying class certification, and the court found that involuntarily committed citizens retained the right to exercise informed consent before psychotropic drugs were administered.

 

1666 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re Conservatorship of G.S.


No. 85-1527


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


134 Wis. 2d 363; 397 N.W.2d 133; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4042


September 4, 1986, Submitted on briefs  
October 16, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Juneau county: Wallace A. Brady, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the conservator of a mentally ill individual, sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Juneau County (Wisconsin) holding the individual's estate liable for the expenses of his institutionalization. The trial court entered an order for payment that authorized the sale by respondent, the Wisconsin Department of Health and Social Services, of the individual's homestead to satisfy the expenses of hospitalization.


OVERVIEW: The conservator argued that Wis. Stat. § 46.10(2), which authorized the State to collect the costs of care from persons admitted or committed to state institutions, violated Wis. Const. art. I, § 17, and that the order should be vacated on equitable grounds. The court affirmed the order. It reasoned that there was no conflict with the homestead exemption statute, Wis. Stat. § 815.20(1), because by specifically authorizing sale of a homestead in Wis. Stat. § 46.10(2), the legislature had created an exemption as permitted by the homestead statute. The court held that by allowing a trial court to release all or a part of the homestead to accommodate those in necessitous circumstances, the statute neither abrogated the homestead exemption nor contradicted the underlying purpose of Wis. Const. art. I, § 17. It also held that where the conservator offered no evidence as to the individual's financial status or need, there was no evidence to support the argument that it would be inequitable for the Sate to seize his homestead or to apply the provisions of Wis. Stat. § 46.10(2),(3) that allowed the trial court to release all or part of the individual's property if necessary for his support.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

State v. Seyferth


No. 86-0252-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


134 Wis. 2d 354; 397 N.W.2d 666; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3928


August 15, 1986, Submitted on briefs  
October 15, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Racine county: Emmanuel Vuvunas, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the circuit court for Racine County, (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of unlawful possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver pursuant to Wis. Stat. §§ 161.41(1m) and 161.14 following its denial of defendant's motion to suppress evidence seized pursuant to the execution of a search warrant.


OVERVIEW: Police obtained a search warrant for the search of defendant's residence. The officers executed the warrant at approximately midnight. The officers were greeted by defendant's father who admitted the officers and directed them to defendant's room in the basement of the home. The officers found defendant asleep. They awakened him and read to him the search warrant and a constitutional rights form. The officers then searched defendant's room and discovered the incriminating evidence. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress the evidence seized pursuant to the execution of the warrant. Defendant appealed and claimed that the nighttime execution of the search warrant was not valid. The court affirmed and held that the execution of the search warrant was in compliance with statutory and constitutional standards. The court held that the execution of a search warrant in the nighttime was statutorily permitted and did not violate the Fourth Amendment. The court held that the midnight search was reasonable because defendant did not challenge that probable cause existed that contraband was likely to be on the property at the time in question.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for unlawful possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver.

ELIOPUL v. BOARD OF FIRE & POLICE COMMRS. for Milwaukee


No. 86-0108


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District One


134 Wis. 2d 453; 397 N.W.2d 157; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4048



October 8, 1986, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: RALPH ADAM FINE, Judge. Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, five police officers, appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied their petition for a writ of certiorari and affirmed a decision of respondent Milwaukee Board of Fire and Police Commissioners (Wisconsin).


OVERVIEW: The five officers were involved in the arrest of a man who died while in police custody. The man's mother filed a complaint alleging that the officers used excessive force and failed to render first aid. The Board found that one of the officers had used excessive force in the arrest, in violation of Milwaukee, Wis., Police Department Rules and Regulations, R. 4, § 98. The Board also found that each of the other four officers had failed to render first aid to the man, in violation of Rule 4, § 67. The Board discharged the first officer and suspended the other four officers. In challenging the Board decision, the officers raised several issues, including a claim that Rule 4, § 98 was impermissibly vague and that the Board's decision was not reasonable. The court affirmed in part the trial court's order, agreeing that Rule 4, § 98 was not unconstitutionally vague and that the first officer's actions fell within the zone of conduct prohibited by the regulation. However, because the trial court failed to address several issues presented by the officers in their petition, the court reversed the order in part and remanded the matter for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part the trial court's order, agreeing that a regulation of the Milwaukee Police Department was not unconstitutionally vague and that one of the officer's actions fell within the zone of conduct prohibited by the regulation. However, because the trial court failed to address several issues presented by the officers in their petition, the court reversed the order in part and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

1669 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thompson


No. 86-0592-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


134 Wis. 2d 330; 397 N.W.2d 121; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3925


September 9, 1986, Submitted on briefs  
October 8, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Racine county: Stephen A. Simanek, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin), which sentenced defendant as a second offender for an alcohol related driving offense even though he had been convicted but once of driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced as a second offender for an alcohol related driving offense despite being convicted only once of driving while intoxicated. The trial court based the enhanced sentence on the fact that defendant had a previous revocation of his license for failure to take a blood alcohol test on a prior occasion under Wis. Stat. § 343.05. Defendant appealed, claiming that Wis. Stat. § 346.65(2)(b), which provided that a person was a repeat offender and subject to harsher penalties if the total revocations under Wis. Stat. § 343.05 and convictions equaled two in a five year period, was unconstitutional because it denied him equal protection. The court ruled that defendant was not denied equal protection and the sentencing provision in Wis. Stat. § 346.65(2)(b) was not discriminatory where there was a reasonable basis to justify the different legislative treatment. By refusing the blood alcohol test, defendant deprived the State of relevant evidence to which it was legally entitled. Thus, the legislature had a legitimate public purpose in enacting § 346.65(2)(b) to provide incentives for taking the blood alcohol test by punishing those like defendant, who did not take it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1670 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kennedy


No. 85-2362-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


134 Wis. 2d 308; 396 N.W.2d 765; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4043


August 14, 1986, Submitted on briefs  
October 7, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Pierce county: Dennis Montabon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision from the Circuit Court for Pierce County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of vehicular homicide and causing injury by intoxicated use of a motor vehicle. Defendant challenged the statutory denial of the physician-patient privilege in homicide trials. In addition, defendant contended that the trial court committed numerous errors, including failing to suppress certain evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant caused a motor vehicle accident in which four people were killed and two children were seriously injured. Defendant was also injured and taken to a Minnesota facility. Blood samples drawn at the treating physician's request showed that defendant was intoxicated. Defendant was convicted of vehicular homicide and causing injury by intoxicated use of a motor vehicle. On appeal, the court held that: (1) a vodka bottle found in defendant's car during a search conducted pursuant to a defective search warrant was admissible where it inevitably would have been discovered during an inventory search of the car; (2) because Minnesota law governed the means by which the blood test evidence could be obtained, noncompliance with Wis. Stat. § 343.305 did not render the blood test evidence inadmissible; (3) because Wisconsin law governed the admissibility of the blood tests, and under Wisconsin law the physician-patient privilege did not apply in homicide trials, the tests were admissible; and (4) the policy choice to deny the doctor-patient privilege in homicide cases was rationally related to the state's compelling interest in detecting and punishing persons committing homicides.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision from the trial court, which convicted defendant of vehicular homicide and causing injury by intoxicated use of a motor vehicle.

Singer v. Medical Protective Co.


No. 85-0533


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Two


134 Wis. 2d 451; 397 N.W.2d 156; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4012



October 1, 1986, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Kenosha county: DAVID BASTIAN, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a physician, his insurer, and the Wisconsin Patient's Compensation Fund, appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which entered a jury verdict in favor of plaintiff parents in their medical malpractice action arising from the misdiagnosis of their son. The parents cross-appealed the constitutionality of the attorney's fee provisions of Wis. Stat. § 655.015.


OVERVIEW: After the parents' child suffered a permanent injury as a result of a misdiagnosis of meningitis, they filed a medical malpractice action against defendants. The child's claim was settled and at trial, the jury was presented with the issue parents' derivative damage claims. When the jury returned a verdict for the parents, defendants appealed. The court affirmed, holding that defendants had waived any objection to the verdict reference sheet by failing to make a specific objection as required by Wis. Stat. § 805.13(3). Further, defendants failed to object to the fact that the trial court did not submit written jury instructions. The trial court properly concluded that only the verdict awards concerning medical, therapy, rehabilitation, and skilled care were future medical expenses within the meaning of Wis. Stat. § 655.015 because the administrative code definition of medical expense eliminated any ambiguity in the phrase as used in § 655.015. Defendants were not entitled to a mistrial based on questionable argument from the parents attorney because they were unable to prove that prejudice resulted from the remarks.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the parents.

 

1672 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. DEMING


No. 86-0886-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


133 Wis. 2d 480; 395 N.W.2d 833; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3807



September 25, 1986, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: JAMES C. BOLL, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) convicting him of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant (OMVWI), contrary to Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a). Because this was defendant's second OMVWI conviction within a five-year period, the court sentenced him as a second offender pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 346.65(2)(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for OMVWI on June 7, 1982. A week later he was arrested in another Wisconsin jurisdiction for OMVWI. He was convicted of the second offense on June 1, 1983. Since that was his first recorded conviction for OMVWI, a civil forfeiture was imposed. Defendant was still awaiting trial on the June 7, 1982 charge when, on August 22, 1983, a summons and criminal complaint alleging a second OMVWI offense within a five-year period were issued. He was convicted and sentenced as a second offender pursuant to § 346.65(2)(b). The primary issue was whether § 346.65(2)(b) applied to defendant's June 7 offense. The statute manifested the legislature's intent that its sanctions be applied in a manner different from repeater penalties in general. The statute did not require a fine and imprisonment only where a second offense followed a first offense within a five-year period, it required a fine and imprisonment if the number of convictions equaled two in a five-year period regardless of the order in which the offenses were committed. Section 346.65(2)(b) mandated a fine and imprisonment for defendant when he was convicted of the June 7 OMVWI charge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction and defendant's sentence.

 

1673 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. ATKINSON


No. 86-0296-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


133 Wis. 2d 479; 395 N.W.2d 832; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3813



September 25, 1986, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and order of the circuit court for Columbia county: JOHN J. BYRNES, Reserve Judge. Reversed and remanded.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and order reversed and remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Columbia County (Wisconsin) convicting him of first-degree sexual assault and denying his postconviction motion. Defendant argued the trial court erred in admitting inculpatory statements he made to police while in custody, in refusing to allow him to inquire into an alleged prior false allegation of sexual assault by the victim, and in excluding evidence that the victim said she had herpes.


OVERVIEW: Defendant called his attorney after being arrested and was told not to make any statements. Defendant's wife and her friend testified that police told them the investigation was focused on other individuals and defendant would get probation if he cooperated. They also testified police told the wife to convince defendant to talk to them. Police denied these allegations. Defendant made inculpatory statements after talking with his wife. His motion to suppress was denied. He also could not introduce evidence that, while making out at a party, the victim started screaming and acting as though she had been sexually assaulted nor could he introduce alleged statements by the victim that she had herpes. The court reversed and remanded because the trial court did not consider the Lee factors in denying the motion to suppress. The court held there was no abuse of discretion in excluding the alleged prior false allegation of sexual assault because the proffer did not support a conclusion that the victim was alleging that she had been sexually assaulted. The court found the victim's alleged statement regarding herpes was properly excluded as defendant did not know how herpes was transmitted.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court convicting the defendant of first-degree sexual assault and denying his postconviction motion was reversed and the matter was remanded for the trial court to reconsider in light of the Lee factors defendant's motion to suppress inculpatory statements made to police.

 

1674 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


SCHULTZ v. KLOTH


No. 86-0085


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


133 Wis. 2d 479; 395 N.W.2d 832; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3888



September 12, 1986, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: CLARENCE R. PARRISH, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant cotenant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which, in plaintiff tenant's discrimination suit against the cotenant under the Wisconsin Open Housing Law, Wis. Stat. § 101.22, awarded the tenant compensatory and punitive damages.


OVERVIEW: The tenant sued the cotenant claiming that the cotenant discriminated against her in violation of the Wisconsin Open Housing Law, Wis. Stat. § 101.22 and federal law. The trial court awarded the tenant compensatory and punitive damages. The cotenant appealed arguing that because the trial court did not find that she segregated, separated, excluded, or treated the tenant unequally because of race, she could not be found in violation of § 101.22(2)(f). The court held that under § 101.22(2)(f), it was unlawful for any person to discriminate by refusing to renew a lease, causing the eviction of a tenant from rental housing or engaging in the harassment of the tenant. Pursuant to § 101.22(1m), "discriminate" and "discrimination" meant to segregate, separate, exclude or treat any person unequally because of race. Therefore, the trial court's finding that the cotenant engaged in racially motivated harassment and intimidation was a finding that the cotenant treated the tenant unequally because of her race. Further, because § 101.22(2) applied to any person, it created no impermissible classification.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the tenant was affirmed.

Rossie v. State/Department of Revenue


No. 85-0609


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


133 Wis. 2d 341; 395 N.W.2d 801; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3814; 65 A.L.R.4th 1191; 1 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1048; 105 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P55,658


June 3, 1986, Submitted on briefs  
September 12, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review pending. This petition was not decided at the time the volume went to press. Its disposition will be reported in a later volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal and Cross-Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: P. Charles Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Wisconsin Department of Revenue (DOR) challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court of Dane County (Wisconsin) that permanently enjoined the DOR from enforcing two DOR administrative directives through the DOR's internal discipline system that banned smoking in all DOR facilities. Respondent, a DOR employee, cross-appealed that portion of the judgment that declared the directives valid.


OVERVIEW: The employee initiated an action for declaratory and injunctive relief alleging that the DOR could not discipline him for smoking at work under administrative directives issued pursuant to the Wisconsin Clear Indoor Act, Wis. Stat. § 101.123. The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment that the DOR directives were valid, holding that the directives did not affect a private right or interest. Therefore, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 227.01(11)(a), the DOR did not have to follow statutory rule-making procedures in issuing the directives. The court reversed the circuit court's judgment enjoining the DOR from enforcing the directives through its internal disciplinary system. The Act did not limit the DOR's authority to issue internal work rules that regulated smoking. The court also rejected the employee's constitutional claims that the Act violated the employee's right to equal protection of the law and interfered with his right to contract.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that the administrative directives prohibiting smoking were valid. The court reversed the permanent injunction enjoining enforcement of the directives.

State v. Larson


No. 86-0253


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


133 Wis. 2d 320; 395 N.W.2d 608; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3884


July 16, 1986, Submitted on briefs  
September 3, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review pending. This petition was not decided at the time the volume went to press. Its disposition will be reported in a later volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Washington county: James B. Schwalbach, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant motorist appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Washington County (Wisconsin), which found him to be a habitual traffic offender and revoked his driving privileges for a period of five years, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 351.06.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to the effective date of Wis. Stat. § 351.02(1), the motorist accumulated three major violations contemplated under § 351.02(1)(a). Following the 1984 amendment to the statute, he accumulated one additional major violation. Based upon the total of four major violations, the county district attorney petitioned the circuit court to determine that the motorist was a habitual traffic offender and to revoke his license. On appeal, the motorist argued that the original statute required proof of not only the four major violations contemplated under subsection (1)(a) but also the 12 or more convictions contemplated under subsection (1)(b). He also argued that use of the three major violations prior to the amendment of the statute constituted an ex post facto application of the amended statute and was therefore a violation of Wis. Const. art. I, § 12, and U.S. Const. art. I, § 10. The court concluded that the 1984 amendment to the statute did not change the computation procedures but was only a clarification of the statute's original language. Therefore, the court concluded that statute was not unconstitutionally applied to the motorist and affirmed the circuit court's order.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

BANK OF ELROY v. SINKULE


No. 84-2473


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


133 Wis. 2d 473; 394 N.W.2d 919; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3765



August 22, 1986, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Vernon county: WALTER S. BLOCK, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a trust and trustees, filed an appeal from the decision of the Circuit Court for Vernon County (Wisconsin), which entered a summary foreclosure judgment in favor of plaintiff bank.


OVERVIEW: The trustee executed a mortgage to the bank as security for a note. Subsequently, the trustee quitclaimed the mortgaged property to the trust. The bank filed a foreclosure action, alleging that the trustee had defaulted on her note payments. The trust answered, admitting that the trustee executed the mortgage and note and that she had defaulted on her payments. Upon the bank's motion, the trial court granted summary judgment. The trust argued that summary judgment was improper because material facts were in controversy. According to the trust, the fact in dispute was a discrepancy in a valuable consideration. The bank supposedly created the money it loaned. The court held that the source of the money loaned to the trustee was irrelevant to the issue whether the trustee defaulted on the note. No genuine issue existed as to any material fact. The trial court correctly granted summary judgment to the bank.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

1678 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Frase


No. 86-0916


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


133 Wis. 2d 477; 394 N.W.2d 921; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3793



August 21, 1986, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Columbia county, LEWIS W. CHARLES, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Columbia County (Wisconsin) that revoked his operating privilege for five years pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 351, Wisconsin's Habitual Traffic Offenders Act. The driver had been convicted of reckless driving and of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: The driver argued that the 14-month delay in commencing the action denied him due process of law. In affirming the judgment, the court found that the driver was not denied due process by the delay and his conduct of his defense was not prejudiced. The State's burden in a habitual traffic offender case was simple. Under Wis. Stat. § 351.06, when the trial court found that appellant was the same person who committed the previous offenses, revocation was automatic. The only defense was that the driver was not the person who accumulated the prior convictions. That defense was not prejudiced by a 14-month delay in prosecution. Additionally, there was no showing that the State intentionally delayed to gain some tactical advantage over the driver. Further, Wis. Stat. § 351.04, did not provide a remedy for district attorneys' lethargy. The only requirement of § 351.04, was that the district attorney file the petition. He did. Though delay could eventually trigger a statute of limitation or deny due process, the latter did not happen and the driver did not assert the former. Section 351.04 did not require a dismissal of the order to show cause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that revoked the driver's operating privilege for five years.

 

1679 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


CITY OF JANESVILLE v. SIKER'S FURNITURE, INC.


No. 85-1479


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


133 Wis. 2d 473; 394 N.W.2d 919; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3755



August 14, 1986, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Rock county: MARK J. FARNUM, Judge. Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and cause remanded. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part, and cause remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant store sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin), which rendered summary judgment for respondent City in an action the City brought against the store for a number of unlicensed closing out sales in violation of City of Janesville ordinance § 5.32, adopting Wis. Stat. § 66.35(1). The City cross-appealed the dismissal of some claims and the amount of the forfeiture on each established claim.


OVERVIEW: The city made 16 claims against a store based on its advertisements. Under Wis. Stat. § 66.35, a store was required to obtain a special license to advertise a "closing out" sale. The city claimed the store did not obtain the required license when so advertising. The trial court found that seven of the claims by the City were unfounded, but rendered summary judgment for the City on the nine remaining claims. The court agreed with the trial court on all but one of the claims. The court held that such phrases as "has to vacate" and "must liquidate" told the reasonable reader that the company was forced to sell, and based on the impression the advertisement would leave with the reader, the company was required to obtain a closing out license. The intent of the owner of the business was not relevant because the statute looked to the advertiser's representation. Wis. Stat. § 66.35 provided fair notice of what was prohibited and permitted fair standards of enforcement. The statute and the ordinance adopting it were sufficiently definite.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in part, reversed it in part, and remanded the cause for further proceedings consistent with the opinion of the court.

STATE v. SALVA


No. 85-2239-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District One


133 Wis. 2d 475; 394 N.W.2d 920; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3749
