NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION -- REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(3)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: FRANCIS T. WASIELEWSKI, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which, after a jury trial, convicted him of resisting a police officer, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 946.41(1).


OVERVIEW: When defendant was asked by police to lower the volume on his radio, he refused, shouted obscenities, and resisted a police officer who tried to take him into custody. He was charged with resisting an officer and disorderly conduct. In the charging section of the complaint, it erroneously cited defendant for resisting the police officer who had accompanied the arresting officer, but the probable cause section correctly identified the arresting officer. The evidence introduced at trial concerned the arresting officer's confrontation with defendant. In initially instructing the jury, the trial court informed them that defendant was charged with resisting the accompanying officer rather than the arresting officer. However, in defining the elements of the resisting charge, the trial court used the correct name. The complaint was amended after the jury returned its verdict. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that defendant was not denied due process. He was not prejudiced by the technically incorrect complaint or by the amendment of the complaint. Furthermore, because any errors at trial were later corrected, he was not prejudiced by those errors.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1681 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. Elkhorn


No. 85-1952


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


132 Wis. 2d 394; 393 N.W.2d 95; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3659


May 21, 1986, Submitted on briefs  
July 2, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Walworth county: James L. Carlson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed in part; reversed in part, and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landlord appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Walworth County (Wisconsin), which dismissed the landlord's complaint and entered a judgment in favor of defendants, a city and a utility. The landlord had filed a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim for relief as well as other claims and a motion for default judgment.


OVERVIEW: The landlord brought an action against defendants after his tenant's delinquent electric bill was added to his property tax statement. Despite the fact that defendants were late in serving their answer and were in default, the trial court proceeded on the merits of the complaint. Further, the trial court spoke only to the § 1983 claim for relief and dismissed the whole action, despite the fact that there were other claims. The court affirmed the decision in part, holding that the trial court was correct in dismissing the § 1983 claim without first deciding whether there was excusable neglect for failure to timely serve the answer. Further, a § 1983 claim could only be maintained absent a state remedy, and the landlord's failure to allege the non-existence of such a remedy rendered the complaint insufficient. The defect was fatal to the motion for a default judgment. The court concluded, however, that there was much more to the landlord's complaint than a § 1983 action and held that the trial court erred in dismissing the whole complaint on the same basis as the § 1983 claim. The trial court was to consider the merits of the other issues that were raised.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the § 1983 claim, reversed the dismissal of all the other claims, and remanded to the trial court to decide the other issues on the merits.

COUNTY OF JEFFERSON v. KLASS


No. 85-2388


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


132 Wis. 2d 476; 392 N.W.2d 131; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3563



June 19, 1986; Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Jefferson county: JOHN B. DANFORTH, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Jefferson County (Wisconsin), by which he was found guilty of illegally passing a school bus in violation of a county ordinance that adopted Wis. Stat. §§ 346.485, 346.48(1). Defendant claimed that the bus was not a school bus under the applicable statutes, the trial court improperly directed a verdict against him, and that Wis. Stat. § 346.48 was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant passed a school bus that was stopped in an oncoming lane after waiting children had entered the bus but before the driver turned of the flashing lights and retracted the stop sign. Defendant claimed that he had not violated Wis. Stat. §§ 346.485, 346.48(1) because the bus was not a school bus. Defendant reasoned that words "school bus" were not painted on the front and back of the bus as provided by Wis. Stat. § 347.44 and it was thus not equipped within the meaning of Wis. Stat. § 347.25(2). On appeal, the court held that the bus was in fact a school bus, reasoning that Wis. Stat. § 347.25(2) required a school bus to be equipped with flashing lights. Because defendant had passed the bus while it was stopped and displaying flashing lights, the court held that defendant violated Wis. Stat. § 346.48(1) regardless of whether the words "school bus" were painted on the front and back of the bus. The court held that the statute was constitutional and that the directed verdict was proper because defendant's claim that the driver should have extinguished the lights after the children boarded was not a cognizable defense to the illegal passing charge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment by which defendant was found guilty of illegally passing a stopped school bus.

STATE v. FERGUSON


No. 86-0227


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District One


132 Wis. 2d 477; 392 N.W.2d 131; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3593



June 12, 1986, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: RUSSELL W. STAMPER, .Judge. Reversed and remanded.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Order reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which dismissed the State's case against defendant for possession of controlled substances after granting defendant's motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that defendant tossed a bag of cocaine away after police stopped their vehicle near him and got out. The trial court held that because the police lacked reasonable suspicion to detain defendant, the cocaine was not admissible in evidence. In reversing the order, the court held that the trial court erred in determining that the police had detained or seized defendant. Regardless of whether police had reason to stop defendant pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 968.24, the court held that by simply stopping their vehicle and getting out of the car near defendant, the police had not detained defendant. The court held that the test to determine whether a seizure had occurred was objective, so the fact that police had decided to detain defendant was irrelevant, because there was no evidence that defendant knew this. Accordingly defendant abandoned the property before any seizure occurred, and neither U.S. Const. amend. IV nor Wis. Const. art. I, § 11, was implicated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that suppressed the evidence, and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

1684 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Jacobs v. Major


No. 85-0341


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


132 Wis. 2d 82; 390 N.W.2d 86; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3486


December 17, 1985, Argued  
May 15, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal and Cross-Appeal from a judgment and order of the circuit court for Dane county: William D. Byrne, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, who were members of a partnership that owned two shopping malls, sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) that permanently enjoined respondents, a dance troupe and its founder, from performing on partnership properties, but denied damages. Respondents filed a cross-appeal, alleging infringement of their rights of free expression under Wis. Const. art. I, § 3.


OVERVIEW: Respondents distributed letters to the mall merchants soliciting support, after their request to conduct a performance of a dance, which depicted the results of nuclear warfare, was denied. Appellants filed an action seeking damages and injunctive relief. Respondents filed a counterclaim. Several respondents violated a pretrial temporary injunction by leafleting and by performing the dance. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment that permanently enjoined respondents from performing but denied appellants' request for damages. The majority of the court held that the state constitution secured the right to free expression against both private infringements and state action. Appellants' property and free speech interests under the federal constitution were adequately protected by balancing them against respondents' competing expressional interest. Respondents' dance activities were properly enjoined because they had, on balance, interfered with the use of and diminished the value of appellants' property. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by limiting the injunctive relief to the dance activities or by refusing to hold a leafleting participant in contempt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1685 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. JOHNSON


No. 85-0295-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


131 Wis. 2d 590; 393 N.W.2d 797; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3457



April 24, 1986, filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for La Crosse county: MICHAEL J. MULROY, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of second-degree murder under Wis. Stat. § 940.02(1) as a lesser-included offense of first-degree murder. The key issue was whether defendant's Fifth Amendment right against self-incrimination had been violated after sheriff's interrogators failed to honor his Sixth Amendment request for counsel.


OVERVIEW: The victim was bludgeoned to death with a stick. After the body was found, defendant accompanied officers to town for questioning and admitted that he and another man had been with the victim the night he was killed. During interrogation, he was Mirandized and later asked for an attorney, but none was provided. He said the second man had killed the victim but admitted helping hide the body. His oral and taped statements were admitted at trial. On appeal, the court upheld defendant 's conviction for second-degree murder. The trial court correctly refused to suppress any statements given after defendant requested counsel because he was not in custody, having been told he was free to leave the station at any time. Defendant's statements were voluntary; he was not psychologically "coerced" when officers asked him to "narc" on his accomplice out of deference to the victim's family. Because he was not subjected to custodial interrogation after he invoked his Sixth Amendment right to counsel, his Fifth Amendment right against self-incrimination was not violated A homicide by reckless conduct instruction was properly refused because the victim's injuries were intentional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1686 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Laskaris v. Wisconsin Dells, Inc.


No. 84-2160


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


131 Wis. 2d 525; 389 N.W.2d 67; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3463


November 22, 1985, Submitted on briefs  
April 24, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Columbia county: Earl J. McMahon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Columbia County (Wisconsin), which dismissed their complaint against respondent city.


OVERVIEW: The landlords owned residential and commercial rental property in the city. Their tenants had separate utility meters. The city bought electric power from a supplier and resold it to customers within the city. Wisconsin Dells, Wis., Ordinance § 7.0.2(7), provided that special assessments for delinquent electric bills could be levied against the real estate served to become a lien on the property and placed on the tax roll with the same effect as other city taxes. The city assessed delinquent tenants' bills against the landowners' rental properties. The landowners sought a declaration that § 7.02(7) was invalid and an injunction. They claimed that the ordinance exceeded the city's statutory powers, deprived them of property without due process, and impaired the obligation of contracts, contrary to the state and federal constitution. The trial court dismissed the landowners' compliant. On appeal, the court rejected their contentions and affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that Wis. Stat. § 66.60(16) authorized a city to impose special charges for delinquent electric bills due a municipal utility and found no constitutional deprivation of rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which denied the landowners' request for an injunction.

 

1687 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


NAU v. HUSSLEIN


No. 85-1839


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


131 Wis. 2d 592; 393 N.W.2d 798; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3372



April 16, 1986, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county. GEORGE A. BURNS, JR., Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant tenants appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which evicted them from a mobile home lot owned by plaintiff landlord and awarded the landlord double rental damages pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 704.27. On appeal, the tenants asserted that the double rental damage provision of § 704.27 violated their due process rights and the Equal Protection Clause.


OVERVIEW: The parties' lease, which was a month-to-month tenancy, contained a provision allowing the landlord to terminate the lease if the tenants breached it, but required the tenants have been given five days to remedy the breach. The landlord served the tenants with a 28-day notice terminating the tenancy due to the tenants continuous noise, arguments, profanity, and disorderly conduct. When the tenants refused to vacate, the landlord filed an eviction action and was awarded double rental damages pursuant to § 704.27. On appeal, the tenants asserted that the lease required they have been given five days to cure and that § 704.27 was unconstitutional. The court held that the 28-day notice for termination of month-to-month tenancies in Wis. Stat. § 704.19(3) applied and superseded the 5-day notice provision because the lease provision only applied to terminations based upon a breach. Section 704.27 was constitutional because it did not deny the tenants access to the courts and there was a compelling governmental justification to establish minimum damages for the cost and inconvenience of a landlord's lawsuit and the difficulty of proving loss of rental opportunity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1688 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. ADAMS


No. 85-1270-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District One


131 Wis. 2d 591; 393 N.W.2d 798; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3440



April 16, 1986, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county. VICTOR MANIAN, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of first-degree sexual assault in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.225(1)(b), second-degree sexual assault in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.225(2)(a), and armed robbery in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 943.32(1)(b), (2). Defendant also appealed from the trial court's order denying his postconviction motions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with sexually assaulting three victims, who had all identified him as their assailant during pre-trial line-ups. After defense counsel impeached one victim's identification by asking her if she had seen defendant after the lineup but before trial, and she said she had not, the State cross-examined defendant, who admitted that his attorney had advised him not to appear at a preliminary hearing. On appeal, the court held that the State's cross-examining defendant about his waiver of his right to be present at the pretrial hearing did not violate his Sixth Amendment right to be present at trial or his attorney-client privilege. Under Wis. Stat. § 906.11(2), the State was entitled to cross-examine defendant on his waiver of his right to be present at a pretrial hearing, which was not analogous to commenting on defendant's exercise of his right against self-incrimination. The cross-examination was necessary to show that defendant's absence at the pretrial was not caused by the State and to mitigate defendant's attack on the witness's ability to identify defendant. Also, the State did not delve into the details of defendant's conversation with his attorney.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

 

1689 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Smith v. Oak Creek


No. 85-1470


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


131 Wis. 2d 451; 389 N.W.2d 366; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3427


February 4, 1986, Submitted on briefs  
April 16, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review pending. This petition was not decided at the time the volume went to press. Its disposition will be reported in a later volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Rudolph T. Randa, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner applicant appealed an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), dismissing his request for injunctions and a writ of certiorari regarding respondent city's refusal of his application to renew his alcoholic beverage license, due to the applicant's status as a habitual law offender under Wis. Stat. § 125.04(5)(b). The applicant contended that the city's action was arbitrary, capricious and discriminatory.


OVERVIEW: The applicant had testified under immunity from prosecution in a criminal case that he had illegally possessed and sold controlled substances in his tavern. Subsequently, the applicant requested a renewal of his alcoholic beverage license from the city. The city council held a hearing, at which the testimony from the criminal proceeding was read. The city refused to renew the applicant's license because he was a habitual law offender under Wis. Stat. § 125.04(5)(b). The applicant petitioned the trial court for a writ of certiorari and contended that the city's action was arbitrary, capricious and discriminatory. He also sought a permanent injunction ordering the city to renew his license. The trial court denied the petition and injunction. The applicant appealed. The court held that nothing in the language of the statute mandated a conclusion that the applicant had to be convicted of a law violation in order to be classified as an habitual offender. The statute prohibited the issuance of an alcoholic beverage license to habitual law offenders and convicted felons. The record contained the applicant's own testimony regarding his habitual violations of the controlled substances law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

In re M.J.


No. 85-1444


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


131 Wis. 2d 591; 393 N.W.2d 798; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3434



April 1, 1986 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: ROBERT J. MIECH, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county board sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which dismissed with prejudice its petition to extend the involuntary mental commitment of respondent, an adult female, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 51.20(13)(g)2.


OVERVIEW: Respondent was committed to the custody of the board pursuant to a finding that she was dangerous to herself under Wis. Stat. § 51.20(1)(a)2.d. In 1984 respondent's commitment was extended for one year pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 51.20(13(g)2. Subsequently, respondent was transferred to outpatient care, but she was then arrested for battery. The criminal court initiated competency proceedings under Wis. Stat. § 971.14 and discharged her to the board for civil commitment. In 1985 the board petitioned the trial court to extend the commitment for one year; the trial court dismissed the petition on the ground that respondent received no notice of her rights upon return from her conditional transfer under Wis. Stat. § 51.35(1)(e) and any violation of the 1984 agreement was a result of the intervening criminal proceedings. On appeal the court affirmed for a different reason, holding that respondent's due process rights were violated when she was not given timely notice of the 1985 petition to extend the commitment as required by Wis. Stat. § 51.20.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal order entered by the trial court.

JOHNSON v. CEGIELSKI


No. 84-2538


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


130 Wis. 2d 540; 393 N.W.2d 547; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3361



March 5, 1986 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: PATRICIA S. CURLEY, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) enjoining him from harassing respondent, his former wife.


OVERVIEW: At the injunction hearing, the husband admitted that he had called his wife 23 times at work one day. The trial court found that the husband had called his wife 75 times at work during a period of one month and, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 813.125, ordered him to stay away from her. The husband contended on appeal that § 813.125, which authorized the entry of harassment restraining orders and injunctions, was unconstitutional. The husband also contended that the trial court abused its discretion by failing to consider seriously his motions and objections at the injunction hearing. The court rejected the constitutionality argument because the husband failed to support his allegations by any argument or citation to authority. The court also found no support for the contention that the motions and objections were not seriously considered on the merits. The court cautioned the husband that the appeal appeared to be frivolous under Wis. Stat. § 809.25(3)(c) in light of his inappropriate request for relief, including vacation of the divorce judgment and prosecution of his wife.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that the husband's claims were meritless and affirmed the trial court's order.

SINCLAIR v. CEGIELSKI


No. 84-2493


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


130 Wis. 2d 540; 393 N.W.2d 547; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3364



March 5, 1986 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: MICHAEL P. SULLIVAN, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review pro se from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) enjoining him from harassing respondents, a husband and wife.


OVERVIEW: Appellant had repeatedly called respondents' home late at night demanding his ex-wife's unlisted telephone number. Appellant's ex-wife was the daughter of one of the respondents. The trial court enjoined appellant from calling or contacting respondents for one year. The issue on appeal was the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 813.125, which authorized the entry of harassment restraining orders and injunctions. In his brief, appellant stated, without further elaboration or citation to any precedent, that § 813.125 was "massively unconstitutional." The court held that appellant's arguments were wholly inadequate and that he had failed to meet the heavy burden placed on a challenger to a statute's constitutionality. The court added that the appeal appeared to be frivolous under Wis. Stat. § 809.25(3)(c) and admonished appellant that it would carefully scrutinize any future actions filed by him in the matter.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

STATE v. ELLEFSON


No. 84-2472-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


129 Wis. 2d 545; 394 N.W.2d 317; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3256



February 20, 1986 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for La Crosse county: PETER G. PAPPAS, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of homicide by operation of a motor vehicle while intoxicated in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.09(1)(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in a head-on collision with a vehicle driven by the victim. The victim was killed in the collision, and defendant was seriously injured. Blood tests revealed that both defendant and the victim had blood alcohol levels in excess of the legal limit. Defendant was convicted of homicide by operation of a motor vehicle while intoxicated pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 940.09(1)(a). On review, defendant's major assertion was that the standard jury instruction Wis. Jury Instructions Crim. No. 1185 on the elements of the offense under Wis. Stat. § 940.09(1)(a) violated substantive due process, was fundamentally unfair, or stated an improper burden of proof for the statutory defense. The court affirmed. The court held that neither 940.09(1)(a) nor Wis. Jury Instructions Crim. No. 1185 violated procedural or substantive due process rights where Wis. Stat. § 940.09(1)(a) was reasonably related to its desired end. The court held that placing the burden of persuasion on defendant to establish the statutory defense under Wis. Stat. § 940.09(2) did not violated due process and Wis. Jury Instructions Crim. No. 1185 accurately stated the burden of proof under Wis. Stat. § 940.09(2).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1694 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re Paternity of S.M.S.


No. 85-0707


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


129 Wis. 2d 310; 384 N.W.2d 709; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3200


December 12, 1985, Oral argument  
February 5, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Waukesha county: John P. Buckley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a paternity case, appellant disputed a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin). The issues included whether the jury selection method used in that county's courts complied with Wis. Stat. § 756.04(3), and, if so, whether the method was unconstitutional because it compartmentalized prospective jurors into specialized panels, e.g., civil, juvenile, and criminal court and the like for their whole tour of duty.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued that the procedure was contrary to the plain meaning of § 756.04(3). On appeal, the court recognized the rule of statutory construction that clear and unambiguous language should be given its ordinary and accepted meaning but pointed out that courts could construe a statute whose meaning was clear if literal application would lead to an absurd or unreasonable result. The court noted that the words "sitting" and "term" were used interchangeably in Wis. Rev. Stat. ch. 97, §§ 8, 9 (1949), the former of which was the forerunner of Wis. Stat. § 756.04(3). Thus, the term "sitting of any court" in § 756.04(3) meant the same as "term of any court" and the county's practice of drawing panels four or five times per year conformed, as nearly as possible, with the law. Substantial compliance with the jury selection law was all that was required. The court rejected appellant's argument, for which he offered no legal authority, that selecting panels for various branches of the circuit court was unconstitutional if those branches were confined to specialized areas of the law. The Supreme Court of Wisconsin had rejected a similar argument. Nor had appellant shown prejudice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and the order.

 

1695 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re C.J.


No. 84-2541


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


128 Wis. 2d 560; 384 N.W.2d 367; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3144



January 28, 1986 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Rock county: J. BYRNES, Judge. Reversed and cause remanded. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, department of social services and a guardian ad litem, sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin) that dismissed the county's petition filed under Wis. Stat. § 48.415(2) to terminate respondent parents' parental rights to their children.


OVERVIEW: The county's termination of parental rights petition alleged that the parents' children were in continuing need of protection or services. At the fact-finding hearing, the trial court permitted the guardian ad litem to question prospective jurors at voir dire, make preemptory strikes, and make an opening statement to the jury. However, the trial court precluded the guardian from making a summation to the jury. In lieu of a closing statement, the trial court permitted the guardian to indicate how she wanted the jury to answer each question of a special verdict. The jury failed to find that the county made a diligent effort to provide required services. The court reversed and remanded and agreed with the guardian that the trial court unduly restricted her participation at the fact-finding hearing. The court noted the limitation of Wis. Stat. § 805.10 to two attorneys per side, but noted that because the county had only one attorney argue to the jury the guardian the trial court erred in not giving the guardian the opportunity to make her summation. The guardian's summation may have persuaded the jury that the county made diligent efforts to provide services.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded.

 

1696 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. SCHAITEL


No. 84-2433-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


128 Wis. 2d 559; 384 N.W.2d 367; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3177



January 28, 1986 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and order of the circuit court for Monroe county: JAMES W. RICE, Judge. Affirmed in part, vacated in part and remanded. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed, sentences under sec. 125.66(1), Stats., vacated, and cause remanded solely for resentencing under sec. 125.66(1).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an amended judgment of the Circuit Court for Monroe County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of violating the repeat offender provision of Wis. Stat. § 125.66(1), and Monroe County, Wis., Zoning Ordinance, art. III, § 32(11) for illegal sales of alcohol on his property. Defendant also appealed from an order that denied his post-conviction motions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant unlawfully operated a private club that served alcohol on his property without a license. He was convicted of violations of the Monroe County, Wis., Zoning Ordinance, art. III, § 32(11), and the trial court convicted and sentenced him under the repeat offender provision of Wis. Stat. 125.66(1). On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions and concluded that the sales of liquor on three separate occasions gave rise to separate violations of the ordinances because the legality of the land use during each transaction must have been determined separately. The court rejected defendant's claims that § 125.66(1) was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad, and affirmed the convictions under that statute. However, the state conceded that the trial court erred in concluding that the multiple convictions were second or subsequent convictions under the repeat offender provision of § 125.66(1). Thus, the court vacated the sentences and remanded for resentencing under § 125.66(1).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction for unlawful alcohol sales in violation of the zoning ordinance. However, the court vacated the sentences under the statutory repeat offender provision and remanded solely for resentencing.

 

1697 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. McBOUNDS


Nos. 84-1951-CR, 84-1952-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


128 Wis. 2d 559; 384 N.W.2d 366; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3127



January 22, 1986 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Kenosha county: EMMANUEL J. VUVUNAS, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of first-degree murder and armed burglary. Defendant specifically challenged the trial court's disqualification of his attorney on conflict of interest grounds.


OVERVIEW: The trial court disqualified defendant's attorney because his law firm was representing a potential prosecution witness. Defendant challenged the trial court's finding that an actual conflict had existed. On appeal, the court held that the simultaneous representation by defense counsel's firm of a prosecution witness constituted an actual conflict of interest. The court found that the trial court based its decision to disqualify on the reports of both defense counsel and the district attorney. The court rejected defendant's argument that even if an actual conflict had existed, he should have been permitted to waive the conflict. The court held that defendant had not sufficiently objected to the disqualification. The court found that the record merely indicated a willingness to continue the attorney-client relationship. The court found nothing in the record to indicate that defendant was objecting to the disqualification, that defendant could waive the conflict, that defendant wanted to waive the conflict, or that defendant wanted a waiver proceeding. Moreover, the court found that by pleading guilty, defendant had waived his right to raise the conflict of interest issue on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first-degree murder and armed burglary. The court affirmed the trial court's finding that a conflict of interest had existed.

 

1698 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


GILBERT v. BOARD OF POLICE & FIRE COMMRS. OF MADISON


No. 84-769


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


128 Wis. 2d 558; 384 N.W.2d 366; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3155



January 14, 1986 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: ANGELA B. BARTELL, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff fireman appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which had affirmed a decision of defendant board reprimanding and suspending him for one week without pay for violation of an administrative directive. The fireman contended that he was not a "supervisor" within the meaning of the directive, that the directive was overbroad, vague, selectively enforced against him, and violated his First Amendment rights.


OVERVIEW: The mayor issued a directive charging supervisors with the duty to take affirmative steps to insure a harassment-free environment for city employees. The fireman was a lieutenant. He made a vulgar statement in the presence of a woman firefighter indicating that women did not belong in the fire department. He contended that the directive did not apply to him because he was not considered a supervisor under the National Labor Relations Act. The court held that under the plain meaning of the term he was a supervisor. He had control over the other firefighters within his company. The court held that the directive was neither overbroad nor vague. The fact that the fireman was the only city employee disciplined for violation of the directive did not indicate selective enforcement because it had only been in effect for six months. Abridgement of the fireman's free speech rights was justified because he was in a policymaking position and did not make the comment in private, but in the presence of firefighters under his direct supervision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

 

1699 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


NCR Corp. v. Department of Revenue


No. 84-2010


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


128 Wis. 2d 442; 384 N.W.2d 355; 1986 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3118


November 7, 1985, Submitted on briefs  
January 10, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: Moria Krueger, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a Wisconsin Tax Appeals Commission decision denying the corporation a deduction on its state corporate franchise tax return for federal income taxes paid for the stated years. The corporation claimed that the Commission's interpretation of Wis. Stat. § 71.04(3) (1975), to disallow the deduction was erroneous.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the conclusions of the Commission were based on extensive findings of fact. The court's independent review of the record confirmed that there was substantial and credible evidence to support the Commission's findings and, therefore, its conclusions of law. In particular, the court concurred with the Commission's conclusion that adoption of the corporation's interpretation would lead to an absurd and unreasonable result. It was uncontroverted that legislators believed they were enacting a revenue-enhancing amendment, yet the corporation acknowledged that its interpretation of the amendment would have entailed a revenue loss to the state of a substantial amount of money. The court was required to look to the common sense meaning of a statute to avoid unreasonable and absurd results. To adopt the corporation's argument the court would have had to adopt a statutory construction in derogation of common sense. The requisite rational basis existed for the Commission's interpretation of the statute, and thus the court rejected the corporation's "plain meaning" argument and affirmed both the Commission and the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed both the Commission's interpretation and affirmed the trial court's as well, rejecting the corporation's "plain meaning" suggestion.

 

1700 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. PERRY PRINTING Corp.


No. 84-1308


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


128 Wis. 2d 554; 381 N.W.2d 619; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4026



December 26, 1985 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL and CROSS APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Jefferson county: ARNOLD K. SCHUMANN, Judge. Affirmed in part, reversed in part and cause remanded. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court: -- Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Jefferson County (Wisconsin) that dismissed its claims that appellee corporation violated Wis. Admin. Code § 154.11(6) by emitting solvent emission from its plant presses, and that denied injunctive relief against future violations. The corporation cross-appealed challenging the constitutionality of § 154.11(6).


OVERVIEW: Wis. Admin. Code § 154.11(6) limited the opacity of emission plumes. However, it did not specify if it pertained to particulate matter emissions. The court resolved that ambiguity by considering the position of § 154.11(6) within Wis. Admin. Code § 154.11, and because the entire regulation dealt with particulate matter and how to control its emissions, § 154.11(6) encompassed particulate matter. Next, the only presses that released particulate matter for purposes of § 154.11(6) were "new direct sources" under Wis. Admin. Code § 154.01(137)(b) because at standard conditions the solvent emissions were liquid. Further, because liquids were included in the definition of particulate matter subject to opacity limits on July 1, 1975, only those presses installed after that date were within § 154.01(137)(b). The court overruled the corporation's constitutional challenges to § 154.11(6) because a reasonable relationship existed between opacity limits and air pollution control, and the regulation was not vague. The court affirmed the denial of the State's injunction request because even if the emissions were a public nuisance Wis. Stat. § 144.98 gave the trial court discretion in the matter.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of the judgment that denied the State's request for injunctive relief against the corporation. The court reversed a part of the judgment that held certain of the corporation's presses emitted emissions that violated the State's regulation. The court also denied the corporation's constitutional challenge. Finally, the court remanded for recalculation of the forfeitures imposed in light of its decision.

 

1701 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Chappy v. Labor & Industry Review Com.


No. 84-2320


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


128 Wis. 2d 318; 381 N.W.2d 552; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3956


October 10, 1985, Oral argument  
December 26, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Washington county: James B. Schwalbach, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Washington County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision by the Labor and Industry Review Commission (LIRC) determining the rate at which appellee employee was to receive temporary total disability benefits (TTD) under the Worker's Compensation Act (Act).


OVERVIEW: The employee was injured during her employment in 1967 and received TTD benefits from the insurer. In 1980, the employee suffered another period of disability related to the original injury. The LIRC determined that the employee should be paid at the rate prescribed in Wis. Stat. § 102.43(7)(b), which was enacted after the employee's original injury and was intended to deal with the effects of inflation upon compensation rates. The court rejected the insurer's argument that the statute was not intended to be applied retroactively. The Act was remedial in nature and the statute itself reflected a legislative intent that it be applied retroactively. Even assuming the insurer was correct that retroactive application of § 102.43(7), resulted in an impairment of the insurer's contract obligations, the court concluded that the impairment was not unconstitutional. Wis. Stat. § 102.43(7) has a significant and legitimate public purpose and the statute is reasonable and appropriate, given its purpose. Retroactive application did not deprive the insurer of property without due process of law because the statute used a rational means to achieve a legitimate end.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1702 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


G. HEILEMAN BREWING CO. v. CITY OF LA CROSSE


No. 84-1315


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


128 Wis. 2d 554; 381 N.W.2d 619; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4025



December 23, 1985 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for La Crosse county: GARY B. SCHLOSSTEIN, Judge. Reversed and remanded. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court: - Judgment reversed and remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant brewing company sought review of a judgment rendered by the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin), which held that the external structures of its tank cellars were buildings and thus not exempt from property taxation as "manufacturing machinery and specific processing equipment" used exclusively and directly in manufacturing tangible personal property within the meaning of Wis. Stat. § 70.11(27).


OVERVIEW: The brewing company filed suit, seeking refunds of property taxes, against respondents, the State Department of Revenue, the county, and city, seeking a declaration that certain structural components of its beer cellars were "manufacturing machinery" and thus exempt from property taxation under Wis. Stat. § 70.11(27). The trial court found against the company and it appealed, claiming that the trial court erred. The court held that the Department did not have sovereign immunity because the suit was not against the State, but one against the officers of the Department for acting beyond their authority. The court also held that the company had standing to file because it paid the taxes under protest and notice was given in advance. Finally, the court determined that the structural components of the beer cellars were manufacturing machinery and exempt from property taxation under § 70.11(27) because the cellars contained and stabilized the precise environments required for the mass production of beer. The court concluded that the cellar's other uses were merely incidental to that primary and principal function and did not effects its exemption.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1703 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


BIEL v. BIEL


No. 84-925


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


128 Wis. 2d 553; 381 N.W.2d 619; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4002



December 17, 1985 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dodge county: HENRY G. GERGEN, JR., Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of that part of a divorce judgment of the Circuit Court for Dodge County (Wisconsin), which awarded respondent mother custody of their children.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from the award of custody of the children to the mother, the father argued that the trial court abused its discretion and denied him equal protection under the Fourteenth Amendment by applying the "tender years" doctrine, a gender based preference. He also argued that Wis. Stat. § 767.24(1)(b) was unconstitutional. Affirming the judgment, the court concluded that the record did not support the father's contention that the trial court used a gender-based preference. The court held further that the issue of the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 767.24(1)(b) was not properly before the court because the attorney general was not given an opportunity to appear before the court and defend the law as constitutionally proper. The court then concluded that the trial court properly relied on the interaction and interrelationship of the children with his parents and other siblings in determining the children's best interests, according to Wis. Stat. § 767.24(2)(b). The court determined that, based on the record, the findings of the trial court could be reasonably construed as a finding that these children, at the present time, had a greater need to be near their mother.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment awarding custody of the children to the mother.

CITY OF OSHKOSH v. ANDERSON


Nos. 85-1304, 85-1305, 85-1306


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


128 Wis. 2d 557; 381 N.W.2d 621; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3974



December 4, 1985 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Winnebago County: THOMAS S. WILLIAMS, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant City of Oshkosh, Wisconsin, disputed orders of the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin), which dismissed citations issued to respondent property owner for alleged violations of an ordinance that regulated the use and storage of flammable and combustible liquids. The issues included whether the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague and whether the City's motion to vacate the judgment was improperly denied.


OVERVIEW: The City's ordinance adopted Wis. Admin. Code § Ind. 8, which regulated the use and storage of flammable and combustible liquids. The City did not dispute the property owner's statement in his affidavit filed with respect to the parties' cross-motions for summary judgment that he continued to use the tanks for private purposes. On appeal, as to the denial of its motion to vacate, the City argued that it should have been given an opportunity to brief the constitutional issue upon which the citations were dismissed. But, pointing out that the trial court had the power to sua sponte consider legal issues not raised by the parties, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the motion. Further, given the nature of the owner's argument, the City should have been aware that he was raising the constitutional issue of vagueness. The court also agreed with the trial court that the terms "out of service" and "abandoned" were indefinite and vague such that an ordinary person would not be made aware that converting the tanks from commercial to private use would constitute taking the tanks "out of service" and, after 90 days, an abandonment of the tanks.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders.

 

1705 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. KERRIGAN


No. 85-0667


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


128 Wis. 2d 556; 381 N.W.2d 620; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4051



December 4, 1985, RELEASED  
December 4, 1985, FILED


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)(5), STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha county: ROGER P. MURPHY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of operating an automobile with a blood alcohol content in excess of .10 percent pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(b) was unconstitutionally vague because it failed to give individuals adequate notice of the conduct which it prohibited because it was based upon a measured blood alcohol level rather than on an identifiable act. Defendant also contended that the trial court erred by excluding from evidence a blood alcohol chart he offered at trial and that the trial court erred by giving a falsus in uno instruction to the jury which allowed the jury to completely disregard testimony which it did not find credible. The court held that (1) a person of normal intelligence was able to reason that if he drank a substantial amount of alcohol he would run a serious risk of violating § 346.63(1)(b) and thus, § 346.63(1)(b) was not unconstitutionally vague; (2) the trial court properly excluded the blood alcohol chart because defendant did not provide the jury with sufficient evidence to allow it to use the chart without engaging in speculation; and (3) it was not error for the trial court to give jurors the falsus in uno instruction because it had a reasonable basis to conclude that the jury could find that one of the witnesses was lying.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1706 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thomas


No. 84-838-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


128 Wis. 2d 93; 381 N.W.2d 567; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3918


April 18, 1985, Oral argument  
December 4, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Kenosha county: Robert V. Baker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin) that convicted him of three counts of kidnapping and three counts of first-degree sexual assault. An issue presented on appeal was whether or not Wis. Stat. § 940.225(1)(c), which made first-degree sexual assault with the aid of one or more persons a crime, was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Four men, including defendant, abducted and raped three female hitchhikers, aged 16 to 19. On appeal, the court held that a challenge to the constitutionality of a statute on the basis of vagueness went to the subject matter jurisdiction of the trial court and could not be waived. Defendant argued that the words "aided or abetted" in Wis. Stat. § 940.225(1)(c) were so unclear that a reasonable person could not determine whether he was committing first-degree or second-degree sexual assault. The court held that § 940.225(1)(c) was not unconstitutional. Due process did not require a statute to be so definite as to inform a defendant in advance of exactly what the consequences of his act would be, other than to make it patent that his act would be criminal. The legislature intended the phrase "aided or abetted" in Wis. Stat. § 940.225(1)(c) to have the same meaning as the phrase "aids and abets" in Wis. Stat. § 939.05. The trial court did not err by refusing to instruct on the lesser-included offense of second-degree sexual assault because defendant's conduct, at the very least, aided and abetted the other men in sexually attacking the women.


OUTCOME: Ruling against defendant, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment and order.

 

1707 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Olson


No. 84-1537-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


127 Wis. 2d 412; 380 N.W.2d 375; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3850


May 13, 1985, Submitted on briefs  
November 21, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review pending. This petition was not decided at the time the volume went to press. Its disposition will be reported in a later volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Grant county: John R. Wagner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Grant County (Wisconsin) convicting him of delivering a controlled substance, tetrahydrocannabinol (THC), a violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 161.14(4)(t), 161.41(1)(b). An issue presented on appeal was whether or not § 161.14(4)(t) denied defendant equal protection by irrationally classifying THCs, including those in marijuana, as Schedule I controlled substances.


OVERVIEW: Under the Uniform Controlled Substances Act, Wis. Stat. ch. 161, a drug was classified as Schedule I if it had a high potential for abuse and either no accepted medical use in treatment in the United States or lacked accepted safety for use in treatment under medical supervision. A preliminary issue was whether or not, by pleading guilty, defendant had waived the right to attack § 161.14(4)(t) on equal protection grounds. On appeal, the court ruled that § 161.14(4)(t) was not facially invalid; ergo, the equal protection challenge was nonjurisdictional. Defendant's guilty plea did not waive his right to his appellate equal protection attack on § 161.14(4)(t), even though the statute was facially valid. However, it was rational for the legislature to classify THC as schedule I as long as its acceptance for medical use was an unsettled medical question. Defendant failed to establish an accepted medical use and conceded that debate continued in the scientific community about the effects of marijuana. Regarding sentencing, the court ruled that defendant's refusal to name his supplier was a proper factor to consider.


OUTCOME: Ruling against defendant, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1708 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mahone


No. 84-1533-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


127 Wis. 2d 364; 379 N.W.2d 878; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3859


August 15, 1985, Argued  
November 20, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Racine county: Dennis D. Costello, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin) that recommitted him pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 971.17(3) after conditional release had been granted pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 971.17(2). Defendant had been committed to a state hospital after he was, under a plea agreement, found not guilty of burglary by reason of mental disease or defect and was found to be a present danger to others.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had petitioned the trial court for an absolute discharge under Wis. Stat. § 971.17(2), but the trial court ordered defendant recommitted after receiving information that, while babysitting, he had hung a seven-year-old child with a rope. Defendant asserted, inter alia, that Wis. Stat. § 971.17(3) was invalid because it provided no due process. On appeal, the court found that, on its face, § 971.17(3) did not provide for procedural due process. The same preexisting procedural due process rules that applied to probationers and parolees in revocation proceedings applied to insanity acquittees in recommitment proceedings. The court held that § 971.17(3) was not unconstitutionally vague. Regarding the standard for recommitment under § 971.17(3), which spoke in terms of the safety of defendant or the safety of others, the court held that there was no requirement of a finding of mental illness for recommitment of a conditionally released insanity acquittee. The proper standard for recommitment for those found not guilty by reason of a mental disease or defect was "dangerousness."


OUTCOME: Ruling against defendant, the court affirmed the trial court's order.

 

1709 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


City of Madison v. Town of Madison


No. 85-0029


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


127 Wis. 2d 96; 377 N.W.2d 221; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3835


September 23, 1985, Argued  
October 28, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review pending. This petition was not decided at the time the volume went to press. Its disposition will be reported in a later volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dane county: Robert R. Pekowsky, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant town appealed from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which invalidated the town's efforts to incorporate as a city pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 60.81.


OVERVIEW: Wis. Stat. § 60.81 provided a procedure whereby a town adjacent to "a city of the first class" could incorporate as a city if its resident population exceeded 5,000 and its equalized valuation exceeded $ 20,000,000. There was no question that the town met the population and valuation requirements. The question was whether the neighboring city of Madison was a city of the first class. Although Madison met the population requirements for being a first class city, it had not proclaimed itself to be a first class city, and had not made required changes in government. Wis. Stat. § 990.001(15), passed after the town submitted its petition for incorporation, stated that meeting the population requirements for first class city status was not enough without the other required changes being met. The court rejected the town's argument that § 990.001(15) could not be applied retroactively. The statute was procedural in nature. It related solely to Wis. Stat. § 62.05, which specified the procedures by which a city, having reached the required population, may move up the classification ladder; it did not create, abolish, or otherwise regulate the ability of a city to so move.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1710 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fisher


No. 84-1408


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


127 Wis. 2d 560; 378 N.W.2d 295; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3776



October 10, 1985 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waupaca county: NATHAN E. WIESE, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court: -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Waupaca County (Wisconsin), which found he was a habitual traffic offender under Wis. Stat. § 351.02 and revoked his driving privileges.


OVERVIEW: The driver was served with an order to show cause why his driving privileges should not be revoked pursuant to the Habitual Traffic Offender Law, Wis. Stat. ch. 351. The order was based on a petition alleging that over two years the driver was convicted of 15 moving violations or traffic regulations in eight states. The State introduced his certified driving record showing 15 convictions. The driver admitted some of the convictions and denied others. He contended that most of the convictions were based on no-contest pleas. The trial court nevertheless found that he was a habitual traffic offender and revoked his driving privileges. On appeal the court affirmed. The court held that there was no right to a jury trial under ch. 351 proceedings and that the certified driving record was a self-authenticating public record, and so was not inadmissible hearsay. The court also noted that the ch. 351 proceeding was not a criminal proceeding and that due process did not require that the state bear the burden of proof. The court held that the driver's due process rights were not violated by imposing on him the burden of disproving facts contained in the certified driving record.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the driver was a habitual traffic offender and revoking his driving privileges.

 

1711 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE ex rel. GROBARCHIK v. REIVITZ


No. 85-0388


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


126 Wis. 2d 515; 376 N.W.2d 869; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3732



September 17, 1985 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Dodge county: JAMES W. KARCH, Reserve Judge. Reversed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Orders reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate and respondents, Secretary of Department of Health and Social Services (Department), Administrator of Department of Corrections, and superintendent of a correctional institution, all challenged orders from the Circuit Court for Dodge County (Wisconsin), which ruled that the Department could not deny good time credit to mandatory release parole violators.


OVERVIEW: While the inmate was paroled on mandatory release, he committed a robbery, and his parole was revoked. At the revocation hearing, the examiner ruled that most of his good time credit was forfeited. The Department held a hearing and concluded that the inmate should not be allowed to earn good time on previously-earned good time that had been forfeited during parole revocation. The trial court concluded that the Department's ruling operated as an unconstitutional ex post facto law. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the Department had the authority under Wis. Stat. § 53.11(7)(b) to deny good time credit to the inmate and that the proceedings were not unconstitutional. The court concluded that § 53.11(7)(b) gave the Department the right to deny credit to the inmate, as one who returned to prison as a mandatory release violator. The inmate did not have the right to call witnesses at a good time eligibility hearing. The Department could refuse to allow witnesses if their testimony would be irrelevant or unnecessary. The inmate failed to show how the delay between the revocation hearing and the good time eligibility hearing was unreasonable or prejudicial to his interests.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order.

 

1712 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


TOWN OF VERNON v. WAUKESHA CTY.


No. 84-1676


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


126 Wis. 2d 510; 375 N.W.2d 220; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3629



August 21, 1985 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Waukesha county: HAROLD J. WOLLENZIEN, Judge. Affirmed in part; reversed in part. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed; order affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a town and several individuals, sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which dismissed their complaint seeking declaratory relief to prevent respondents, a county and related entities, from using a site within the town as a sanitary landfill. The town also appealed an order holding that the State of Wisconsin was not a necessary party and that the motion to add the State was frivolous.


OVERVIEW: The town and the individuals brought suit seeking declaratory relief to prevent the county's use of a site within the town as a sanitary landfill. The town later filed a motion to join the State of Wisconsin as a necessary party. The trial court found that the motion was frivolous, denied the motion, and imposed costs against the town. The trial court later granted the county's motion to dismiss the complaint on the ground that it was not ripe because the town had not exhausted its administrative remedies. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's determination that the town's claims were premature and therefore not ripe for disposition and that part of the trial court's order denying the motion to join the State as a party. The court held that, considering that the entire matter had yet to proceed through administrative channels and therefore could not have been acted upon with any certainty, neither the question of prospective injunctive relief nor that of the propriety of expenditures was properly before the courts. The court reversed that part of the trial court's order granting costs for frivolousness because the costs were not requested by the county in writing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment affirmed. The court affirmed the portion of the trial court's order denying the motion to join the State of Wisconsin as a party but reversed the portion of the order that awarded costs in favor of the county.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which affirmed appellee Kenosha County Board of Review's decision regarding a tax assessment on an apartment complex owned by the taxpayer.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer objected to the county assessor's tax on its apartment complex. In re Paternity of C.B.


Nos. 84-1593 & 84-1752


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


125 Wis. 2d 576; 373 N.W.2d 88; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3545



July 24, 1985 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Manitowoc county: FRED H. HAZLEWOOD, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner husband appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Manitowoc County (Wisconsin), which found that he was the father born to respondent wife after the parties separated, and which ordered him to pay child support.


OVERVIEW: The child was born eight and one half months after the parties separated. The wife alleged in her answer to the husband's divorce petition that he was the child's father, and testified that she and the husband had intercourse during the conceptive period. The husband denied both paternity and intercourse. Blood test results favored the husband's paternity. The court held that: (1) the presumption of paternity arising from marriage contained in Wis. Stat. § 891.41(1) did not violate equal protection because it could be asserted against a woman who denied her husband's paternity as well as against a husband who denied paternity; (2) the presumption was gender-based only to the extent that only women can become pregnant and only men can father children; (3) the presumption did not offend due process because Wis. Stat. § 767.47(1) provided it could be rebutted, and because there was a rational connection between the fact of marriage and the presumption of paternity; (4) the mother's sexual behavior outside of the conceptive period was not relevant to the issue of the child's paternity; and (5) the trial court considered the appropriate factors when it determined child support.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

In re Paternity of A.S.D.


No. 84-1771


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


125 Wis. 2d 529; 372 N.W.2d 921; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3591


June 17, 1985, Submitted on briefs  
July 18, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: Angela B. Bartell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed in part, reversed in part, and cause remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mother challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which directed respondent father to pay support, claiming that the trial court erred in applying the percentage of income standards specified in Wis. Stat. § 767.51(5m) to the particular circumstances of the case and determining the father's gross income.


OVERVIEW: In a paternity case, the mother applied for an order requiring the father to pay child support. The court found that application of the one-child percentage to serial children living in separate households could render unreasonable results with a father of five such children required to pay 85 percent of his gross income in support. The court determined that (1) avoidance of financial hardship for the children of divorced or separated parents was the basic purpose of the child support laws; (2) the percentage guidelines established under Wis. Stat. § 767.395(3) were developed by the Department of Health and Social Services on the assumption of intact, not serial, families; (3) in situations of successive children living in separate households a court could not use the guidelines but must hear the evidence and proceed to establish support by applying relevant criteria under Wis. Stat. § 767.51(5). The court ruled that the trial court's determination of the father's income was not unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of the trial court's order that determined the father's income. The court reversed that part of the order that applied the statutory guidelines to determine the amount of child support and remanded the case for further proceedings.

State v. Steckel


No. 84-2014-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


125 Wis. 2d 577; 373 N.W.2d 88; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3541



July 17, 1985 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments and an order of the circuit court for Walworth county: ROBERT D. READ, JOHN J. BYRNES, JOHN R. RACE, Judges. 1 Modified and as modified, affirmed. 


1 Judge Read presided at the trial and the initial sentencing. Judge Byrnes presided at the sentencing following revocation of probation. Judge Race presided at the post-conviction proceedings.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgments and order modified and as modified, affirmed. 7 



7 Upon remittitur, the clerk is directed to prepare a modified judgment, reciting the correct statute, for the trial court's signature.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of judgments and an order of the circuit court for Walworth county (Wisconsin), which convicted him of defrauding an innkeeper, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 943.21(1)(a). He further sought review from a subsequent judgment committing him to prison and from an order denying his post-conviction motions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stayed at a hotel and at the beginning of his stay, he paid on a daily basis. At a later point, the hotel manager agreed to allow defendant to pay his bill once a week or once every ten days. When he terminated his stay at the hotel he failed to pay the balance due at that time. He did not return to the hotel to collect his property and did not pay the balance due. After several unsuccessful attempts to collect payment, the hotel manager sought criminal prosecution. Initially, he was charged with violating Wis. Stat. § 943.21(1)(b). After the preliminary hearing, however, the district attorney changed the charge to a violation of Wis. Stat. § 943.21(1)(a). Defendant was convicted following a bench trial. The trial court withheld sentence and placed him on probation for two years. Subsequently, defendant's probation was revoked and he was sentenced to two years' imprisonment and ordered to pay a fine. He sought review. On appeal, the court upheld defendant's conviction and sentence. The court ruled that there was sufficient evidence to convict defendant, under Wis. Stat. § 943.21(1)(a), because the hotel did not extend credit to defendant beyond the date of departure.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgments and order and as modified, affirmed them. The court modified the judgment to reflect the proper statutory charge as recited in the information.

Milwaukee v. Wakefield


No. 84-2450


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


125 Wis. 2d 578; 373 N.W.2d 89; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3531



July 15, 1985 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: ROBERT W. LANDRY, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) that affirmed a judgment of the Municipal Court of the City of Milwaukee that adjudicated him guilty of violating a parking-meter ordinance of the City of Milwaukee, which was Milwaukee, Wis., Code § 101-32(6) (1972). Defendant argued that § 101-32(6) was an unauthorized attempt by the State, via the City, to burden or tax the federal government.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was an army employee, and his argument regarding unauthorized attempt to burden was based on the requirement of § 101-32(6) that he feed a meter for on-the-street parking. Elaborated further, he asserted that where the citation was not issued to a person but was against the license number, were he not to pay the ticket, probably the registration of the vehicle that he drove would have been suspended together with all other vehicles in Wisconsin owned by the army. He argued further, based on Wis. Stat. § 341.04(1), that every person operating an army vehicle after such suspensions were imposed would be subject to a penalty for operating an unregistered vehicle as well as other possible legal penalties. The court was not convinced by this argument. It had not been established that the vehicle at issue was registered in Wisconsin under state law or that it or other vehicles owned by the army were required to be registered. Without such a showing, the court was unable to find a burden or interruption imposed on the federal government by a state government through a local municipality. The court rejected defendant's tax argument regarding § 101-32(6).


OUTCOME: Ruling against defendant, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment.
