Kleiman v. Wisconsin Dep't of Revenue


Nos. 84-902, 85-0327


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


125 Wis. 2d 576; 373 N.W.2d 88; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3561



July 11, 1985 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court of Dane county: ANGELA B. BARTELL, Judge. Affirmed. 

APPEAL from an order of the circuit court of Dane county: MARK A. FRANKEL, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Dane County (Wisconsin). The trial court affirmed decisions of respondent, the Wisconsin Tax Appeals Commission, which had granted summary judgment to respondent, the Wisconsin Department of Revenue, in the taxpayer's appeals of the Department's denial of his petitions for redetermination.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer filed his petitions for redetermination with the Department after it notified him that it was voiding his withholding exemption certificate and assessing him additional income tax for 1980 and 1981. The taxpayer's petitions raised the issues whether wages were income that the State could tax, whether the income tax unconstitutionally infringed on the fundamental right to work, and whether the State's power to tax could be so exercised as to make it a potential instrument of enslavement. The court held that: (1) pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 71.02(2)(e), Wisconsin based its definition of income subject to taxation on the federal definition; (2) wages were taxable income because 26 U.S.C.S. § 61(a) defined income to include compensation for services, which included wages; (3) both the federal and state constitutions granted Congress and the state legislature the power to tax income; (4) the imposition of a tax on the taxpayer's income was not "enslavement"; and (5) the taxpayer failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that the State's tax on wages was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's orders.

 

1719 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kath


No. 85-0023-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


125 Wis. 2d 578; 373 N.W.2d 89; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3589



July 11, 1985 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Jefferson county: HAROLD EBERHARDT, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction entered by the Circuit Court for Jefferson County (Wisconsin), for carrying a concealed weapon in violation of Wis. Stat. § 941.23. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in refusing to admit the content of defendant's telephone calls to law enforcement agencies in support of his claim that the manner in which he carried the weapon was legal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped by a sheriff's deputy for a traffic violation. Defendant's driver's license was under suspension, and he was arrested. The deputy discovered bullets in defendant's pocket during a routine search and found a gun wrapped in a pair of jeans buckled to the saddlebag of defendant's motorcycle. Defendant was convicted for carrying a concealed weapon in violation of Wis. Stat. § 941.23. Defendant appealed and contended that the trial court erred in refusing to admit his telephone conversations with unnamed employees of law enforcement agencies who told him that transporting a gun the way he did was legal. The calls were made after his arrest. The court affirmed. There was no indication in the record that the persons defendant talked to were authorized or required to give such legal advice. The court rejected the argument of mistake of law or fact under Wis. Stat. § 939.43(1) because the only element of intent under Wis. Stat. § 941.23 was that defendant had to be aware of the gun's existence. The court found the statute constitutional and that the weapon was within his immediate reach. There was no evidence that the gun was encased in the manner required by law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1720 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. HAASE


Nos. 85-0089, 85-0090, 85-0092, 85-0093, 85-0094, 85-0095


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


125 Wis. 2d 578; 373 N.W.2d 89; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3553



July 3, 1985 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments of the circuit court for Winnebago county: ROBERT A. HAWLEY and WILLIAM E. CRANE, Judges. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, defendant motorist disputed convictions in the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin) for operating a motor vehicle without a valid driver's license, Wis. Stat. § 343.05(1), and operating an unregistered vehicle, Wis. Stat. § 341.04(1). On appeal, the issues included whether the use of a uniform traffic citation violated the separation of powers doctrine and whether defendant was denied his right to a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: The motorist received copies of the uniform traffic citations for each violation. On appeal, the court held that the circuit court had subject matter jurisdiction pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 345.30 and the filing of the citations with the circuit court was sufficient to confer personal jurisdiction. The use of a citation did not violate the separation of powers doctrine. Wis. Stat. § 345.11(1), (5) were presumed constitutional and the officer issuing a uniform traffic citation fulfilled only the law enforcement obligations of the executive branch. The requirement of a neutral and detached magistrate was limited to civil and criminal cases involving the issuance of search or arrest warrants. Defendant was not entitled to be represented by someone not licensed to practice law in Wisconsin. Also, because the charges were prosecuted as civil forfeiture actions, the right to counsel under U.S. Const. amend. VI had not attached. Because defendant's jury trial demand was not accompanied by the required fee, he had waived his right to a jury trial. The requirements of a driver's license and the registration of a vehicle were reasonable exercises of the State's police power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments.

 

1721 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Slatter


No. 85-0397-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


125 Wis. 2d 575; 373 N.W.2d 87; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3528



June 25, 1985 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Rock county: GERALD W. JAECKLE, Judge. Reversed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Order reversed and cause remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin), which suppressed the results of a breathalyzer test give to defendant after he was stopped for squealing his tires and denied the State's motion to reconsider the suppression order.


OVERVIEW: An officer stopped defendant and noted the smell of intoxicants. Defendant was cited for driving while intoxicated after submitting to a breathalyzer test. Defendant entered a not guilty plea and filed a motion for suppression of the test results, claiming that the test was the result of physical force and coercion. The circuit court granted the motion and denied the State's motion to reconsider that was based on its failure to appear at the suppression hearing. The circuit court denied the State's motion and the State appealed. The court reversed the circuit court's decision. The court found that because probable cause to arrest was not disputed, the request that defendant submit to the chemical test, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 343.305(2)(b), was proper. Further, the officer was justified in promptly seeking to subject defendant to a chemical test of his blood, because an exigent situation, the body's rapidly metabolizing alcohol, existed. The officer was warranted in telling defendant that if he didn't consent to the breathalyzer test, he would be taken for blood to be drawn, as there was no proof that anything other than a proper blood test was suggested to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's decision.

 

1722 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Wisconsin Tel. Co. v. Wisconsin Dep't of Revenue


No. 84-243


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


125 Wis. 2d 339; 371 N.W.2d 825; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3447


April 3, 1985, Submitted on briefs  
June 25, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review pending. This petition was not decided at the time the volume went to press. Its disposition will be reported in a later volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: Angela B. Bartell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayers, mostly telephone companies, appealed the decision from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which entered summary judgment in favor of respondents, the Wisconsin Department of Revenue and the departmental secretary, in the taxpayers' suit challenging a sales tax under Wis. Stat. § 77.52(2)(a)4 as an unconstitutional burden on interstate commerce.


OVERVIEW: The tax was imposed on telephone calls originating in Wisconsin and billed in the State. The taxpayers contended that there was insufficient evidence that the calls had a sufficient nexus with Wisconsin, that the tax created multiple taxation, that it discriminated against interstate commerce, and that the tax was not fairly related to services provided by the State. The court affirmed the judgment. The court began with the rule that taxing statutes were presumed constitutional. The tax was not a midstream tax that lacked a sufficient nexus to Wisconsin. Rather, it taxed calls at the point of origin. The fact that the tax was unapportioned did not render it unconstitutional. The fact that there was a potential for multiple taxation did not establish in fact that it was multiple. The existence of a gross receipts tax along with the sales tax did not create multiple taxation. Because the tax equally taxed both interstate and intrastate calls, the tax did not discriminate against interstate commerce. The taxpayers, as Wisconsin residents, received the benefits of the tax, particularly police and fire protection. A use tax was also constitutional under the same rules.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment against the taxpayers was affirmed on appeal.

Cain v. Brennan


No. 84-1147


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


125 Wis. 2d 572; 373 N.W.2d 85; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3456



June 21, 1985 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: MARVIN C. HOLZ, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient filed a submission of controversy with the patients compensation panel, alleging that defendants, doctors and a hospital, negligently rendered medical services to her. After the panel dismissed her action for failure to comply with discovery rules, the patient filed a negligence action in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin). She appealed from the trial court's judgment of dismissal.


OVERVIEW: Defendants first sought dismissal by the panel when the patient failed to answer their interrogatories or to provide medical releases. The panel ordered her to comply with such requests or face dismissal. She complied but then ignored their later requests that she submit to a deposition. The panel cited the patient's uncooperative conduct in granting defendants' motion to dismiss her cause of action. When the patient filed her action in the trial court, defendants moved for dismissal again. The court upheld the judgment below. Pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 655.04(1)(b), a medical malpractice claim could not be commenced in a circuit court unless it had been heard on the merits and findings and an order had been made by the panel. As to the patient's contention that the panels' order of dismissal was an order within the meaning of § 655.04(1)(b), the court explained that the patient was not entitled to pursue a claim in a circuit court if the dismissal order was intended as a sanction for failure to comply with discovery rules. The panel's order was clearly intended as such. Finally, the court noted that Wis. Stat. § 655 had been previously upheld as a constitutional provision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Dane County Hospital & Home v. Labor & Industry Review Com.


No. 84-983


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


125 Wis. 2d 308; 371 N.W.2d 815; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3445


May 3, 1985, Submitted on briefs  
June 20, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county; Robert R. Pekowsky, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) that affirmed a decision of respondent Labor and Industry Review Commission (LIRC) awarding workers' compensation benefits to respondent employee that included permanent partial disability benefits, temporary total disability benefits during vocational rehabilitation training, and travel expenses for the training period pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 102.61.


OVERVIEW: The employee's award included eligibility for additional benefits and travel compensation, subject to continued progress and periodic review. The employer objected to the rehabilitation award and to the procedure followed by the Department of Industry, Labor, and Human Relations (DILHR). The court affirmed the award. The employee was not required to submit to an additional medical examination because the examination permitted to the employer by Wis. Stat. § 102.13(1) had taken place. DILHR did not abuse its discretion in denying a continuance because the need arose from the employer's lack of preparation. DILHR was presumed to be impartial and there was no probability of prejudice from an ex parte communication. The employer was not denied a meaningful opportunity to be heard on the eligibility issue and there was no misrepresentation of facts in the eligibility determination. Amendments in the federal Vocational Rehabilitation Act (Act) were incorporated into Wis. Stat. § 102.61 and the reference to the Act in § 102.61 did not unconstitutionally delegate legislative authority. Wis. Admin. Code § 80.49(3) did not apply because the record was compiled before its effective date.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court judgment that affirmed the LIRC decision awarding workers' compensation benefits to the employee.

 

1725 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Milwaukee Brewers v. Dep't of Health & Social Services


No. 85-0164


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


126 Wis. 2d 512; 375 N.W.2d 220; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3669



June 18, 1985 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: ANGELA B. BARTELL, Judge. Reversed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment reversed. Section 46.05(10)(a), Stats., is declared unconstitutional and void.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff baseball club brought a declaratory relief and injunctive action against defendants, a corporation and related individuals and alleged that Wis. Stat. § 46.05(10)(a), which designated a proposed prison site was unconstitutional. The Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) ruled that § 46.05(10)(a) was constitutional and entered judgment in favor of defendants.


OVERVIEW: The proposed prison was to be built near the site where the baseball club played their professional baseball games. The baseball club claimed that the statute designating the proposed prison site, § 46.05(10)(a), was enacted in violation of Wis. Const. art. IV, § 18. The circuit court held that Wis. Stat. § 46.05(10)(a) was neither private nor local and therefore was not subject to Wis. Const. art. IV, § 18. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that § 46.05(10)(a) was a local bill and that its enactment violated Wis. Const. art. IV, § 18. Accordingly, the court declared § 46.05(10)(a) unconstitutional. Under Wis. Const. art. IV, § 18 no private or local bill passed by the legislature could embrace more than one subject, which had to be expressed in the title. Wis. Stat. § 46.05(10)(a) originated as part of a budget bill. The budget bill embraced many subjects, and its title gave no indication that it contained legislation that would designate the proposed prison site. Thus, § 46.05(10)(a) was enacted in violation of Wis. Const. art. IV, § 18.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment and declared the challenged statute unconstitutional.

Link Farms v. Labor & Industry Review Com.


No. 84-1179


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


125 Wis. 2d 572; 373 N.W.2d 85; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3515



June 13, 1985 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: WILLIAM F. EICH, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court:--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which confirmed an order of respondent, the Wisconsin Labor and Industry Review Commission (LIRC), entered without a hearing, that an employee had sustained an injury arising out of his employment while performing service growing out of and incidental to that employment.


OVERVIEW: The employee was injured at work. He sought compensation and, at a prehearing, the examiner discussed the necessity for filing an answer. The employer gave no reason for not filing an answer and the examiner ruled in favor of the employee without notice. The LIRC affirmed and the employer sought review, alleging that Wis. Stat. § 102.18(1)(a) did not confer authority on the LIRC to order payment without a hearing. This argument was premised on the assertion that § 102.18(1)(a) was ambiguous. The court affirmed. The court held that the employer's argument that § 102.18(1)(a) was ambiguous was without merit as it did not limit the making of findings to instances in which a hearing had been held. Because the examiner had examined the relevant facts of record, applied a proper legal standard and, using a rational process, reached a conclusion that a reasonable factfinder could have reached, he did not abuse his discretion. The employer's argument that entry of the order without notice violated its due process rights was without merit because the warning that a default could issues, coupled with the discretion of Wis. Admin. Code § Ind. 80.05(2), provided adequate notice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's decision.

In re B.W.S.


No. 84-2547


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


125 Wis. 2d 212; 371 N.W.2d 379; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3437


March 18, 1985, Submitted on briefs  
June 4, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Brown county: Charles E. Kuehn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father appealed from the order of the Circuit Court for Brown County (Wisconsin), which required him to pay child support for petitioner child, his illegitimate son. The father claimed that a prior judgment of a Michigan court approving a lump sum settlement was owed full faith and credit in Wisconsin.


OVERVIEW: The child was the illegitimate son of the father. Settlement of a paternity action was by an agreement approved by the Michigan circuit court in which the father was to pay medical expenses for the mother and a lump sum payment on the child's 18th birthday. The mother, via a guardian ad litem petitioned for support for the child. The father was unable to convince the trial court to honor the Michigan agreement. The father stipulated to a finding of paternity, and the trial court ordered monthly support payments. The court affirmed the order of the trial court. The court concluded that the Michigan statute was unconstitutional because it disadvantaged illegitimate children. The classification failed to bear an evident and substantial relation to a state interest. It invidiously discriminated against illegitimate children by denying them substantial benefits accorded children generally. Because the Michigan judgment and the statute on which it was based violated the equal protection clause of the federal constitution, the Michigan judgment was not entitled to full faith and credit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

State v. Knies


No. 84-1455-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


125 Wis. 2d 569; 371 N.W.2d 430; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3336



May 1, 1985 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha county: MARK S. GEMPELER, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of carrying a concealed weapon, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 941.23.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was pulled over in his vehicle for having expired registration plates. When defendant opened his door, the police officer saw a pair of metal nunchakus on the floor of the vehicle. Defendant was arrested and later convicted of carrying a concealed weapon, contrary to § 941.23. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that § 941.23 did not violate the defendant's constitutional right to keep and bear arms under the Second Amendment to the United States Constitution. The court also held that while § 941.23 may have, when it was originally enacted, reflected the intent of the legislators of that era to require proof of intent to cause harm, that version of the statute was no longer binding on the court. Finding that defendant was found carrying a concealed weapon within the State of Wisconsin, the court held that he was therefore subject to prosecution and punishment under the criminal law of Wisconsin in the trial court. The court held that as a result, the trial court properly denied defendant's motions to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

SPIC & SPAN, INC. v. STATE


No. 84-707


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


124 Wis. 2d 776; 370 N.W.2d 293; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3258



April 19, 1985 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: MARVIN C. HOLZ, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a selling corporation and a buying corporation, sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision issued by respondent Wisconsin Department of Natural Resources (DNR) that reduced the corporations' emission reduction credits.


OVERVIEW: The selling corporation operated a dry cleaning business in Milwaukee. In 1982, the corporation installed machines that would reduce its air pollution emissions. It applied for and received emission reduction credits. It sold some of these credits to the buying corporation. In 1983, the DNR told appellants that it intended to adopt "reasonably available control technology III" (RACT III) rules. Under these rules, the DNR said, any unused credits would be reduced because the RACT III rules required emission controls similar to those voluntarily adopted by the selling corporation. Thus, the DNR said, the emission reductions for which credits were awarded did not constitute a surplus under the RACT III rules. Appellants sought judicial review and the trial court affirmed. Appellants again sought review and the court affirmed. The court held that the DNR's decision to reduce the credits was not inconsistent with anything it told either of appellants and did not violate a rule or established agency policy or practice. The court also held that the DNR's decision was neither arbitrary nor capricious or inconsistent with the federal Environmental Protection Agency's credit-trading policy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's confirmation of a decision by the DNR reducing the number of emission reduction credits allotted to the corporations.

STATE v. DENSON


No. 84-1759-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


124 Wis. 2d 778; 370 N.W.2d 294; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3299

NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Rock county: J. RICHARD LONG, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of disorderly conduct contrary to Wis. Stat. § 947.01, and that denied his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The complaint stated that defendant harassed two young girls. He pleaded no contest to disorderly conduct under Wis. Stat. § 947.01. Defendant contended that his no contest plea was taken by a court commissioner at his initial appearance, that the commissioner did not have the authority to accept the plea, and, therefore, that the plea was void. The court commissioner informed defendant of the charge against him at his initial appearance and ascertained, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 757.69(1)(a), that defendant made an intelligent waiver of his rights and that he understood the consequences of his decision. The commissioner then directed the case to the trial judge who adjudged defendant guilty. The court concluded that the commissioner merely informed defendant of his rights; the trial court actually accepted defendant's plea. While defendant's comments to the girls asking them if they used drugs, drank alcohol, and would go out with him did not constitute a crime, the statements carried sexual overtones and his repeated approaches, given the girls' ages, were sufficient to offend the senses and sensibilities of the average person.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and the order.

VOIGHT'S MARINE SERV. v. TRANSPORTATION COMMN.


No. 84-1597


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District III


124 Wis. 2d 777; 370 N.W.2d 294; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3278



April 9, 1985 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Door county: EDWIN C. STEPHAN, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant common carrier sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Door County (Wisconsin), which approved respondent Wisconsin Transportation Commission's decision to deny the carrier's application for a certificate of convenience to operate a second tour boat.


OVERVIEW: Seeking to operate a second boat that would transport vacationers to an island during the summer tourist season, the carrier applied for a certificate of convenience under Wis. Stat. § 195.45. The Commission found that the island community depended on the carrier's competitor for transportation services in the winter and that the competitor could provide essential year-round ferry service only if its summer profits subsidized its winter losses. On appeal, the court held that there was substantial evidence supporting the Commission's conclusion that the carrier failed to establish that its proposed service was in the public interest. Wis. Stat. § 195.45 did not violate the forever free clause of Wis. Const. art. IX, § 1, because the application process was a reasonable means to accomplishing the legitimate goal of ensuring that common water carriers acted in the public interest. The court concluded that Wis. Stat. § 195.45's delegation of legislative power to the Commission was constitutional because the review proceedings set forth in Wis. Stat. ch. 227 provided procedural safeguards to ensure that the Commission acted to serve the public interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

American Standard Ins. Co. v. Cleveland


No. 84-1437


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


124 Wis. 2d 258; 369 N.W.2d 168; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3241


March 16, 1985, Argued  
April 9, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Pierce county: Richard Galstad, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of the Circuit Court for Pierce County (Wisconsin) judgment that imposed liability upon appellants for damages caused to plaintiff victim in an automobile accident.


OVERVIEW: Appellant driver negligently caused an automobile accident that injured plaintiff victim. Although the accident occurred in Minnesota, both appellant driver and plaintiff victim were Wisconsin residents and were insured by Wisconsin insurance policies. Respondent, plaintiff victim's insurer, paid plaintiff victim for past medical expenses and for lost wages. The trial court applied Wisconsin law and imposed liability for damages against appellants. The appellate court held that Wisconsin's collateral source rule applied to the case. Therefore, plaintiff victim was entitled to recover payments made by respondent. Furthermore, the appellate court held that Wisconsin's subrogation law applied to allow respondent to recover payments made to plaintiff victim. Therefore, judgment in favor of respondent was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed judgment for respondent for payments made to plaintiff victim for damages caused by an automobile accident because Wisconsin's collateral source rule and subrogation law applied to allow respondent's recovery.

Steel v. Bach


No. 84-1395


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


124 Wis. 2d 250; 369 N.W.2d 174; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3244


March 5, 1985, Submitted on briefs  
April 9, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order 1 of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: William J. Shaughnessy, Judge.


1 The trial court issued a memorandum decision. We are construing the memorandum decision as an appealable order because it is apparent that the trial court intended the memorandum decision to be the last document in the litigation and that it disposed of the controversy between the parties. See Radoff v. Red Owl Stores, Inc., 109 Wis. 2d 490, 493, 326 N.W.2d 240, 241 (1982).



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged the order of the Circuit Court of Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which dismissed their motion for a declaratory judgment that the actions of respondent City of Wauwatosa (Wisconsin) in creating a pedestrian mall and in making streets dead-end were illegal and exceeded the City's statutory authority.


OVERVIEW: Over several years, the City altered the use of various streets by creating a pedestrian mall and making some streets into dead-ends or cul-de-sacs. The property owners brought the action for a declaratory judgment. The trial court dismissed their action. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that under Wis. Stat. § 349.03(1), a local authority could enact traffic regulations if they were not inconsistent with chapters in the motor vehicle code or if they were expressly authorized by statute. The court found that the creation of dead-end streets was not contrary to the motor vehicle code because it was not addressed in it. The court found that the dead-ends did not interfere with the free use of the streets, which was prohibited by Wis. Stat. § 349.03(2). The court found that Wis. Stat. § 62.11(5) was an express statutory authorization for local traffic regulations that fit within the strict conformity test of Wis. Stat. § 349.06(1). The court found that Wis. Stat. § 66.298 and Wauwatosa, Wis., Ordinance 12.44, authorizing the pedestrian mall, did not violate due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1735 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. GEORGE


No. 83-2292


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


123 Wis. 2d 544; 368 N.W.2d 846; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3171



March 26, 1985 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Crawford county: MICHAEL KIRCHMAN, Judge. Modified and, as modified, affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment modified and, as modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Crawford County (Wisconsin) convicting defendant under the Uniform Controlled Substances Act of possession of a controlled substance with intent to manufacture and deliver, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 161.41(1m).


OVERVIEW: Police seized 132 well-tended marijuana plants from a padlocked basement room in defendant's home. Defendant claimed that his farmhand rented the room but admitted to owning milk cans used as potting containers and heat lamps found in the room. On appeal, the court modified the judgment to state that defendant was convicted of being a party to the crime of possession of a controlled substance with intent to manufacture in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 939.05(1) and 161.41(1m) and affirmed. The court held that disjunctive jury instructions, although error, were harmless. Possession of a controlled substance with intent to manufacture and possession with intent to deliver were distinct crimes; intent to deliver was not an element of the crime of possession of marijuana with intent to manufacture. The distinction between possession of marijuana, § 161.41(3), and possession with intent to manufacture, § 161.41(1m), was not unconstitutionally vague. Defendant lacked standing to make an equal protection challenge to the personal use exception in Wis. Stat. 161.01(13) because it strained credulity to argue that 132 plants were grown solely for personal use.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment to state that defendant was found guilty of being party to the crime of possession of a controlled substance with intent to manufacture, and affirmed the judgment as modified.

Thorpe v. Thorpe


No. 83-501


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


123 Wis. 2d 424; 367 N.W.2d 233; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3198

March 5, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Rock county: Patrick J. Rude, Judge.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin), which required him to pay 25 percent of his military pension proceeds to respondent ex-wife under the 1982 Uniform Services Former Spouses Protection Act (Act), 10 U.S.C.S. § 1408(c)(1).


OVERVIEW: The husband argued that the circuit court lacked authority to modify the property portion of the divorce judgment. The court held that the circuit court had authority to modify the property division under Wis. Stat. § 806.07. The court held that the wife was entitled to 25 percent of the husband's monthly pension payment, including periodic increases. The husband also argued that the retroactive application of the Act unconstitutionally deprived him of vested property rights in his military retirement pay. The court held that the Act permitted state courts to remedy a harsh result to former spouses and, as a remedial statute, it was properly retroactively applied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of a percentage of the husband's pension to the wife and the retroactive application of the Act.

Prentice v. Transportation Com. of Wisconsin


No. 84-240


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


123 Wis. 2d 113; 365 N.W.2d 899; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3099


August 27, 1984, Submitted on briefs  
February 5, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal and Cross-Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Price county: Gary L. Carlson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant department of transportation challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Price County (Wisconsin), which vacated an order by the Transportation Commission of Wisconsin rescinding a previous order that required a divided crossing where a state highway crossed the tracks of a railroad near respondent village. The village filed a cross-appeal challenging a ruling that res judicata did not prohibit the rescission of a previous order.


OVERVIEW: After the commission rescinded its previous order directing a divided crossing at the intersection of a state highway and railroad tracks and ordered, instead, an at-grade crossing, the village and the railroad commenced separate review proceedings. The trial court reversed the commission's order. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court and reinstated the commission's order. The court held that res judicata did not prohibit the commission from rescinding the previous order because res judicata was inapplicable to commission orders. Moreover, permitting rescission did not interfere with judicial authority because persons adversely affected by the rescission of a previous order were entitled to judicial review. The court also held that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to decide whether the commission properly granted a rehearing.The court further held that a substantial change of circumstances was not necessary to justify rescission in a reopened proceeding. The commission's decision was supported by substantial evidence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order and reinstated the commission's order.

State v. Cissell


No. 84-891-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


124 Wis. 2d 776; 370 N.W.2d 293; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3269



February 1, 1985 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: JANINE P. GESKE, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which dismissed a felony charge of abandonment under Wis. Stat. § 52.05(1) and directed that the charge be reduced to failure to support, a misdemeanor, under Wis. Stat. § 52.055(1).


OVERVIEW: A minor child's mother signed a criminal complaint charging defendant with intentionally and willfully neglecting to provide for the support and maintenance of the child, leaving her in destitute and necessitous circumstances. Defendant was arrested and filed a motion seeking to reduce the felony charge to a misdemeanor charge. The trial court granted the motion and dismissed the felony charge, holding that the felony abandonment statute was a violation of equal protection as applied to defendant. The State sought review. On appeal, the court upheld the order. A conviction under the felony abandonment statute violated the equal protection provisions of Wis. Const. art. I, § 1, and the Fourteenth Amendment. The court ruled that the elements needed to support the charge were identical to those constituting the offense of failure to support under Wis. Stat. § 52.055(1) and that there was no rational basis for the classification of those elements as a felony under Wis. Stat. § 52.05(1). Under the entire felony abandonment statute, the required mental state was simply that of intent, not malice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that dismissed the charge of felony abandonment against defendant.

In re Estate of Trainer


No. 84-825


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


123 Wis. 2d 102; 365 N.W.2d 893; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3095


December 10, 1984, Submitted on briefs  
February 1, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: William J. Shaughnessy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the State Department of Revenue, challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) favoring respondents, the personal representative and the trustees of an estate, which held that a portion of Wis. Stat. § 72.01(5) (1969) was unconstitutional and that a power of appointment possessed by the testator's daughter was not includable in her taxable estate.


OVERVIEW: The testator executed a trust agreement wherein he granted his daughter a power of appointment over certain trust assets. The daughter died without exercising the power of appointment either by will or any other written instrument during her lifetime. After the daughter's death, the State sought to apply Wis. Stat. § 72.01(5) (1969) to the power of appointment that the daughter held at the time of her death. The trial court found that the statute was unconstitutional because the daughter was not provided with the same protection or opportunity possessed by donees of powers created before October 21, 1942. The language of the statute allowed certain exemptions for powers created before October 21, 1942 and after July 22, 1951, but not for the years in between. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that application of the statute to the facts presented would violate the estate's right to equal protection. The court emphasized that its ruling was limited solely to that part of the statute that created an inability to utilize the procedural exception for modification to a tax-exempt class; the substantive portion of the statute creating the tax-exempt class remained valid.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Nyborg


No. 84-226-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


122 Wis. 2d 765; 364 N.W.2d 553; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3076


December 6, 1984, Submitted on briefs  
January 28, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Rock county: Edwin C. Dahlberg, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a postconviction order of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin) that denied him more than 50 days credit on his sentence for endangering safety by conduct regardless of life, a violation of Wis. Stat. § 941.30. An issue on appeal was whether or not he should have been given credit by the trial court for time that he had spent in the county jail of LaFayette County, Wisconsin, on an unrelated matter.


OVERVIEW: Regarding endangering safety and resisting, defendant was released on bail from the jail of Rock County. Later, he was jailed in LaFayette County, during which time a detainer was filed for Rock County, and, when his probation was revoked on the endangering safety conviction, he sought to have credit on the sentencing for that charge credited with time served in Lafayette County. Wis. Stat. § 973.155(1)(a) gave credit toward the service of a sentence for all days spent in custody in connection with the course of conduct for which sentence was imposed. The court rejected the argument that, because a detainer had been filed for Rock County while he was in the jail of LaFayette County, defendant was entitled to sentencing credit for his time in the jail in LaFayette County. Where a county filed a detainer in another county in which a defendant was confined, that defendant was not in custody in connection with the course of conduct for which sentence was imposed in the demanding county until his custody was surrendered to that county. The court rejected the argument that Wis. Stat. § 53.12(1) violated the equal protection of the laws.


OUTCOME: Ruling against defendant, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Hengel v. Hengel


No. 82-2138


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


122 Wis. 2d 737; 365 N.W.2d 16; 1985 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3037; 53 A.L.R.4th 75


April 6, 1984, Argued  
January 24, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for La Crosse county: Dennis G. Montabon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed. No costs to either party.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent husband brought an action against appellant wife, seeking a judgment of divorce. The Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin) entered judgment divorcing the parties and dividing the marital property in accordance with a prenuptial agreement. The wife sought review of the property division.


OVERVIEW: Before their marriage, the husband and the wife entered into an agreement providing the wife with certain personal property in lieu of alimony in the event of a divorce. The trial court found at the time of the parties' marriage, the husband had a net worth of $ 340,000, while the wife had a car, some furniture and her clothing. At the time of the divorce approximately eight years later, the husband's net worth had increased almost ten-fold. Notwithstanding the increase in wealth, the trial court held Wis. Stat. § 767.255(11) applied to the parties' prenuptial agreement and the circumstances of its signing were equitable. Accordingly, the trial court ordered the distribution of the parties' property in accordance with the agreement. On appeal, the wife challenged the conclusion that § 767.255(11) validated the prenuptial agreement entered before § 767.255(11) was effective. She also argued the agreement was inequitable if it was enforceable. The court affirmed the division of marital property because the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it pronounced the prenuptial agreement between the husband and the wife to be equitable as to her.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the part of the judgment that divided the marital property according to the prenuptial agreement between the husband and the wife.

 

1742 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. ANDERSON


No. 84-899-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


122 Wis. 2d 776; 362 N.W.2d 447; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4548



December 26, 1984 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha county: HARRY G. SNYDER, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgement affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant and while having a blood alcohol concentration (BAC) of .10 percent or more, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a) and (b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was pulled over for speeding. The officer asked defendant to submit to a preliminary breath screening test (PBT). The result indicated that defendant had a .10 percent BAC. A breathalyzer test was administered that showed defendant had a .12 percent BAC. Defendant was precluded from asking the officer at trial about the PBT. The court rejected defendant's contention that Wis. Stat. § 343.303 was unconstitutional. The State's interest in protecting its citizens provided a reasonable basis for allowing a police officer to administer a PBT. Defendant's due process rights were not violated when he was precluded from asking about the PBT test at trial. The legislature determined that PBT tests were reliable enough to allow an officer to determine whether to arrest defendant, but not reliable enough to allow admission of the test at trial. The tests were therefore not relevant. Defendant was not prevented from pursuing his chosen line of defense. The exclusion of the PBT test did not render an unfair advantage to the state because the evidence was not admissible by either party at trial. There was no Brady violation because the state did not withhold the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

 

1743 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re T.L.R.


No. 83-1586-LV


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


122 Wis. 2d 774; 362 N.W.2d 446; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4630



December 6, 1984 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court of Dane county: ANGELA B. BARTELL, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Dane County (Wisconsin) waiving juvenile court jurisdiction and referring the case to the district attorney for the institution of criminal proceedings. Appellant contended, among other things, that simultaneously charging her with violations of Wis. Stat. §§ 940.09(1)(a) and (b) placed her in double jeopardy, and that charging under both statutes deprived her of due process of law.


OVERVIEW: Appellant allegedly caused the death of another person by driving while intoxicated. She was 17 years old at the time. She claimed that she was being charged twice for one offense stemming from a single incident, and that this violated double jeopardy. The court found that, because there could be only one conviction under §§ 940.09(a) and (b), charging under both paragraphs did not place appellant in double jeopardy. Appellant contended that the amended § 940.09 was an attempt by the Legislature to permit the State to convict an individual for homicide by driving while intoxicated without having to prove a key element of the crime: that the individual was intoxicated. She contended that § 940.09(1)(b) had the effect of creating a conclusive presumption that someone with a blood alcohol content (BAC) of 0.1 percent or more was under the influence of an intoxicant, and that this was a violation of due process. The court disagreed. In a prosecution under § 940.09(1)(b), whether defendant was under the influence of an intoxicant was irrelevant because § 940.09(1)(b) created a separate offense, that of causing a death by operating a vehicle while having a BAC of 0.1 percent or more.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the juvenile court waiving jurisdiction and referring the case for criminal proceedings.

STATE v. ALEXANDER


No. 83-1933-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


121 Wis. 2d 699; 361 N.W.2d 310; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4480



November 21, 1984 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and order of the circuit court for Richland County: WALTER S. BLOCK, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment and order of the Circuit Court for Richland County (Wisconsin), which convicted her of first-degree murder. Her motion for post-conviction relief was denied.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was guilty of killing her husband. The conviction was affirmed. The court held that the trial court properly reconsidered its original suppression order of the knife. The court ruled that the ownership factor was outweighed by defendant's absence from the property for months, its occupation of tenants, and the fact that the searched area was a septic tank located in the backyard. Thus, defendant had no reasonable expectation of privacy in the contents of the septic tank and the consent of the tenants validated the search. The court determined that defendant had no reasonable expectation of privacy in the loan documents admitted into evidence. The fact that defendant repeatedly forged her husband's name to obtain loans had some probative value as to her motive, but did not demonstrate conduct that the court could reasonably conclude would have inflamed the jury to convict on a first degree murder charge. Thus, the evidence was properly admitted. The court held that based on the State's evidence, the jury disbelieved defendant's version of the events on the day in question. And the jury could have inferred that defendant failed to provide her husband with any assistance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first degree murder.

Mikaelian v. Woyak


No. 83-2385


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


121 Wis. 2d 581; 360 N.W.2d 706; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4513


September 17, 1984, Submitted on briefs  
November 21, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal and Cross Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Racine county: John C. Ahlgrimm, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin) entered judgment in favor of plaintiffs, the administrators of two estates and other victims, against defendant drivers in an action arising out of an automobile accident. Plaintiffs appealed a judgment in favor of defendant passenger and defendants cross-appealed the finding that the vicarious liability statute for sponsors of minor drivers, Wis. Stat. § 343.15(2), was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Several plaintiffs were injured and the decedents were killed when their van was struck by the drivers while the drivers were illegally racing. Plaintiffs argued that the passenger should have been jointly liable for their injuries. The parents of one driver also argued that they should not have been found vicariously liable for the driver, who was a minor. The court affirmed the judgment for plaintiffs. The trial court properly denied plaintiffs' motion for a new trial on the ground of newly discovered evidence. The statement was not independently probative but was corroborative of testimony already in the record and would not result in a different verdict. The court held that the passenger was not required to share responsibility for the injuries because his acquiescence did not make him a participant in the race. The court rejected the parents' argument that the vicarious liability statute was unconstitutional. There was a rational connection between imposing liability on parents and the conduct upon which the liability was predicated because juveniles did not possess mental discretion to the same degree as an adult and lacked the finances to cover any damage they might cause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of plaintiffs and the order holding the vicarious liability statute constitutional.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court for Clark County (Wisconsin), which waived juvenile court jurisdiction in a matter in which appellant was alleged to have conspired to commit armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Appellant claimed that the State failed to show probable cause that appellant had conspired to commit armed robbery. He also argued that Wis. Stat. § 939.31 was unconstitutionally vague. On appeal, the court noted that the trial court's finding of probable cause was based on the petitions. The court decided that appellant did not meet his burden of proving beyond a reasonable doubt that § 939.31 was unconstitutional. The court found that the statute was sufficiently definite to give a person of ordinary intelligence who sought to avoid its penalties fair notice of conduct required or prohibited.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

KLEINSCHMIT v. ROYSTON


No. 83-2278


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


121 Wis. 2d 699; 361 N.W.2d 310; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4485



November 14, 1984 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Winnebago county: ROBERT A. HAASE, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff filed an action against defendants, deputy sheriffs, a county, and the county's insurer, alleging the use of excessive force during an arrest. The Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin) dismissed plaintiff's complaint, which alleged negligence and a strict liability theory premised on the claimed unconstitutional entry into his house. Plaintiff sought review of the trial court's judgment.


OVERVIEW: The trial court jury found that plaintiff was more causally negligent than defendants and dismissed his complaint. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that plaintiff had expressly disavowed any civil rights or constitutional cause of action and that the trial court properly refused to instruct the jury on those matters. The court found that a statement by plaintiff's attorney that plaintiff's strict liability claim did not involve a violation of civil rights or federal law constituted an abandonment of any civil rights claim at trial. The court determined that the trial court properly refused to instruct on strict liability theory because plaintiff had conceded at trial that no case law supported his position that strict liability should have flowed from an unconstitutional entry. The court concluded that the only theory of recovery which was pleaded and put to the jury was whether defendants were negligent. The court found that the evidence supported the jury verdict on that question and that no new trial was warranted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of defendants.

State v. Weisman


No. 84-958


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


121 Wis. 2d 701; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4539



November 14, 1984 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: W. L. JACKMAN, Reserve Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction under Wis. Stat. § 341.63(3) by the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) for failure to return his vehicle license plates to the Wisconsin Department of Transportation. The appeal challenged the constitutionality of the registration suspension procedure, Wis. Stat. § 345.28.


OVERVIEW: Wis. Stat. § 345.28 provided for the suspension of a vehicle's registration if, after two notices were sent to the owner's last known address, a nonmoving traffic violation remained unpaid, or the owner did not appear in court. Defendant received a parking ticket and two notices that, in order to avoid further action, he was required to pay or contest the citation. When defendant did not pay the fine or contest the ticket, his vehicle registration was suspended. He was then convicted of failing to return his license plates. On appeal, the court found that defendant had an opportunity for a fair hearing and was repeatedly notified of this fact so that he was not denied due process. The statute did not deny defendant substantive due process because the right to have one's vehicle registered was not a fundamental constitutional right and the statute was rationally related to the state's legitimate objective of controlling and sanctioning parking law violators. Finally, the statute did not violate the equal protection of the laws guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. XIV, Wis. Const. art. 1, § 1 simply because other municipalities used a different procedure.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for failure to return his license plates to the Department of Transportation.

 

1749 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Hennekins v. River Falls


No. 83-1894


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District III


121 Wis. 2d 699; 361 N.W.2d 310; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4474



November 6, 1984 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Pierce county: WILLIAM E. McEWEN, Judge. Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and cause remanded with directions. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part, and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Pierce County (Wisconsin), which quashed his petition for a writ of certiorari to review respondent employer's decision to terminate his employment.


OVERVIEW: The employee was terminated from his job as a policeman for conduct unbecoming an officer. He contended that the rules were unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. Moreover, he alleged that his due process rights were violated because he did not receive adequate notice of the charges against him. After the trial court quashed his petition for a writ of certiorari, the employee sought review. The court determined that the rule prohibited continuous association with certain persons. The rule was not vague because both actual and constructive knowledge of a person's criminal behavior triggered the rule's prohibition. Moreover, the rule was not overbroad because it contained detailed exceptions for relationships that existed in the performance of official duties or associations that were unavoidable. The court determined that the employee was allowed to confront and cross-examine witnesses. In addition, the hearing was held before an impartial and detached decisionmaker. However, the court held that the employee's due process rights were violated because one of the charges was devoid of necessary facts to apprise the employee of his alleged violation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision with regard to one charge against the employee. The decision to quash the petition for a writ of certiorari on the rest of the charges against the employee was affirmed. The case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

1750 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. IVEY


No. 84-702-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


121 Wis. 2d 698; 359 N.W.2d 181; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4465



October 25, 1984 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: MARK FRANKEL, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court, Dane County, Wisconsin, that convicted him of failing to file State income tax returns for 1979, 1980, and 1981 in violation of Wis. Stat. § 71.11(41).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was required to file the returns because he was under 65 and received more than $ 5,200 income in each of the three years. He was prohibited under the motion in limine from addressing in any way the substantive merits of his belief that the State had no authority to tax him pursuant to federal law. Defendant argued that he was denied a fair trial because he was precluded from presenting a "good faith" defense. The court disagreed. Under Wis. Stat. § 939.43(1), reliance on a mistaken view of the criminal law was no defense unless it negated the existence of the state of mind essential to the crime. The "willfulness" instruction was proper, and no showing of bad purpose of evil motive was required. Defendant waived his right to counsel and could not complain that his own representation was ineffective. The court noted that U. S. Const. art. I, § 10, did not limit Congress's power to declare what was legal tender for all debts. Under 12 U.S.C.S. § 411 (1982), federal reserve notes were redeemable in lawful money and were taxable dollars. Defendant received federal reserve notes measured in dollars in excess of $ 5,200. There was no error.


OUTCOME: The judgment that convicted defendant of failing to file State income tax returns for three years was affirmed.

STATE v. WADUSKY


No. 84-1204-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


121 Wis. 2d 698; 359 N.W.2d 181; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4452



October 24, 1984 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Fond du Lac county: HENRY B. BUSLEE, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Fond du Lac County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of misdemeanor theft in violation of Wis. Stat. § 943.20(1)(a) and (3)(b) as a repeater pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 939.62.


OVERVIEW: A battery was stolen from a parked car. Defendant experienced battery problems on the same night and in the same area. Defendant had a working battery within hours after his car broke down and he bragged about how easy it was to steal a battery. Two witnesses testified that defendant made admissions of guilt. One of the admissions specifically linked the stolen battery to the area where the crime took place. Defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction. He also argued that the trial court committed plain error when it gave a jury instruction that characterized a car battery as movable property without an affirmative showing by the State that the battery was movable property. The court held that: (1) the circumstantial evidence and testimony regarding two admissions of guilt by defendant were sufficient to support his conviction; (2) the trial court's jury instruction did not create a conclusive presumption regarding an element of the charged offense because the jury was still required to find that defendant took and carried away the property; and (3) the act of taking and carrying away an object necessarily implied that it was movable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1752 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


WEBSTER v. MEYER


No. 83-1628


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District III


121 Wis. 2d 694; 359 N.W.2d 179; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4353



October 16, 1984 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Burnett county: DOUGLAS S. MOODIE, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an assured and his insurer, appealed the take-nothing judgment that the Circuit Court for Burnett County (Wisconsin) entered on a jury verdict in favor of defendants, a timber company and individuals, in plaintiffs' action for damages arising from a forest fire that originated upon defendants' property.


OVERVIEW: A fire started during a timber harvest on defendants' property. The blaze spread to the assured's property and damaged it. Plaintiffs sued in tort. After they lost at trial, plaintiffs appealed, asserting myriad errors. Defendants prevailed. Plaintiffs were not entitled to a negligence per se instruction under Wis. Stat. § 26.12(6)(b) (repealed 1984) because its requirements on timber harvest remnants were not intended to apply in cases where parties other than a state or municipality sought recovery. Instead, the controlling statute was Wis. Stat. § 26.21, and plaintiffs were not entitled to a jury instruction thereunder. Under Wis. R. Civ. P., Wis. Stat. § 805.12(1), the trial court's instruction on one defendant's duty as a landowner was proper because it was correct and fully and fairly instructed as to its application regarding the facts. No instruction on principal contractor liability was in order because the timber harvest remnants were not a peculiar unreasonable risk of harm to others. Under Wis. R. Civ. P., Wis. Stat. § 805.08(3), the trial court properly limited plaintiffs' number of peremptory strikes, and the statute survived attack on equal protection grounds.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Menard, Inc.


No. 84-474


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


121 Wis. 2d 199; 358 N.W.2d 813; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4397


September 4, 1984, Submitted on briefs  
October 9, 1984, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal and Cross-Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Eau Claire county: William D. O'Brien, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part, and cause remanded. No costs to either party.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Eau Claire County (Wisconsin) that entered judgment imposing forfeitures on respondent corporation for eight violations of Wis. Admin. Code ch. Ag. 124, that regulated price comparison advertising. The corporation cross-appealed the judgment on the basis that summary judgment should not have been granted finding it guilty of improper price comparisons.


OVERVIEW: The lower court entered judgment against the corporation and imposed forfeitures for eight violations of Wis. Admin. Code ch. Ag. 124, that regulated price comparison advertising. The corporation affirmed the summary judgment because the corporation was guilty of improper price comparisons. The court reversed and remanded for further consideration of the number of violations the corporation committed because each publication of an advertisement had to comply with Wis. Admin. Code ch. Ag. 124. The court found that a violation occurred each time an improper advertisement was published and that each newspaper edition constituted a separate publication. The court found that treating each publication as a separate violation was not a denial of due process because the audience size exposed was not intended to define a violation. The court found no discriminatory classification existed because advertisers in small newspapers were not treated differently from advertisers in large newspapers. The court found Wis. Admin. Code ch. Ag. 124 was not unconstitutionally vague because it clearly defined the conduct prohibited and the trier of fact did not have to apply its own standards of guilt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding that the corporation had violated the state regulation that prohibited improper price comparisons in advertising but reversed and remanded for further consideration of how many forfeitures should be imposed.

Benefit Claim of Erwin N. Sobczyk v. Milwaukee Emples. Retirement Sys.


No. 84-153


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: JOSEPH P. CALLAN, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) quashing his writ of certiorari of his appeal of respondent Annuity and Pension Board's denial of his duty disability pension pursuant to Milwaukee, Wis., Charter Ord. ch. 36.


OVERVIEW: The employee contended that there were insufficient facts to warrant a finding that his knee injury was not compensable and that the hearing board system under the city charter ordinance violated the separation of powers doctrine, making it unconstitutional. The employee filed a petition for a writ of certiorari. On appeal, the court held that his challenge to the constitutionality of the ordinance was required to be accompanied by service of the papers on the attorney general under Wis. Stat. § 806.04(11) and that the his claim was one for declaratory relief, requiring service on the attorney general. The court then considered the merits of his claim, noting that certiorari review under Wis. Stat. § 68.13 was limited to whether the board had acted according arbitrarily, oppressively, or unreasonably and whether the evidence supported the decision. The court held that, because the trial court found that the physician who testified that the employee's condition was the result of degenerative osteoarthritis in the knee was more credible than those who testified to the employee's injury, the decision was supported by substantial evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

In re Budish


No. 84-058


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT II


121 Wis. 2d 696; 359 N.W.2d 181; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4422



October 3, 1984 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Racine county: DENNIS J. FLYNN, Judge. Reversed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant board of police and fire commissioners challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin) that set aside its order imposing a 10-day suspension upon appellee police officer. The board contended that the trial court exceeded its authority under Wis. Stat. § 62.13(5)(I) when it reviewed the jurisdictional issue of whether the board had authority to impose a greater sanction than originally imposed by the police chief.


OVERVIEW: The police officer responded to a complaint and, during a subsequent investigation, found marijuana cigarettes and a small bag of marijuana. Neither the cigarettes nor the bag was safeguarded as evidence. The chief of police imposed a 5-day suspension on the officer for violation of police department rules, regarding the preservation of evidence. The officer requested a hearing before the board, and the chief filed formal charges under Wis. Stat. § 62.13(5)(b). The board found that the charges were sustained and imposed a 10-day suspension. The officer appealed under § 62.13(5) (i) and the trial court set aside the order of the board, concluding that it did not have the authority to increase the penalty originally imposed by the police chief. The board appealed and argued that the trial court exceeded its authority under § 62.13(5)(i) when it reviewed the jurisdictional issue of whether the board could impose a greater sanction. The court reversed and held that the trial court's review was limited to a determination of whether the order of the board was reasonable. The court held that the appeal was specifically brought pursuant to the statute and not by a writ of certiorari.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Leahan


No. 84-717


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


120 Wis. 2d 683; 357 N.W.2d 566; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4154

DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Rock County (Wisconsin) of the offense of operating a motor vehicle with a blood-alcohol concentration of .10 percent or more in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(b). Defendant appealed his conviction and the trial court's denial of his post-trial motions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped after a state trooper observed defendant driving erratically. The trooper smelled a strong odor of intoxicants on defendant, noticed his manner of speech and movement, and arrested defendant for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of alcohol. After being taken to the sheriff's department, defendant performed poorly in the field sobriety tests, and registered a .15 percent blood-alcohol concentration in a breathalyzer test. The trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss on the ground that he lacked notice or knowledge that his conduct fell within the scope of § 346.63(1)(b), and denied defendant's request to admit the department of transportation's blood-alcohol concentration computation wheel into evidence. Defendant was convicted and the court affirmed. The court rejected defendant's assertion of error in the admission of his breathalyzer tests into evidence and held that they emanated from an agency charged with maintaining the records, and were certified and therefore self-authenticated. The court held that the wheel was properly excluded because defendant's intent was not relevant to the charged offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

State ex rel. Lowery v. Civil Service Com.


No. 83-1223


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


120 Wis. 2d 680; 357 N.W.2d 564; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4216



September 25, 1984 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: WILLIAM EICH, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former deputy sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which affirmed an order of respondent Dane County Civil Service Commission affirming the termination of the deputy's employment. The deputy asserted several errors on appeal.


OVERVIEW: The deputy was accused of making many unauthorized telephone calls at county expense. After an investigation, he was fired. The Commission affirmed the sheriff department's decision to fire the deputy. The trial court affirmed. On appeal, the issue before the court was whether the deputy was statutorily or constitutionally entitled to a pre-termination hearing to determine the proper discipline for his acts, and whether the Commission acted arbitrarily when it failed to address his constitutional argument. The court affirmed. Specifically, the court held that because the deputy did not raise his argument that a pre-termination hearing was required by statute, it would not consider the issue on appeal. Furthermore, the court found that where the deputy contested the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 63.01, but he failed to make service, as required by Wis. Stat. § 806.04(11), the trial court could not have considered the issue and, therefore, the court could not consider the issue on appeal. Finally, the ordinance permitting a post-termination hearing was not unconstitutional where a meaningful hearing was provided and the Commission was authorized to reinstate the deputy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.
