In re C.D.


No. 84-358


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


120 Wis. 2d 683; 357 N.W.2d 566; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4135



September 12, 1984 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a non-final order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: LEANDER J. FOLEY, JR., Judge. Reversed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which entered a non-final order requiring the State to post a bond before the circuit court would order an arrest of respondent putative father in a paternity action.


OVERVIEW: A paternity action was commenced by the State. The father appeared before the court commissioner below and denied paternity. The commissioner ordered a blood test. The mother and father admitted to being served with an order to appear for a pretrial hearing, but neither appeared for the blood test, and both appeared for the hearing. When the same thing occurred at a subsequent hearing, the commissioner issued a capias for the mother and order for the arrest of the father, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 767.465(2). The father moved to stay the order because the State had not posted the bond arguably prescribed by Wis. Stat. § 818.05, the statute setting forth the bond requirement for arrests in civil actions. The commissioner held that § 818.05 did not apply to paternity actions, and the father filed an emergency motion to quash the arrest warrant. The circuit court ruled that no order for arrest could issue before the State posted the bond. The State appealed and the court reversed. The court found that § 818.05 did not apply to actions in which the State was the petitioner, or to an order for arrest in a paternity action, pursuant to 1983 Wis. Laws 447, § 53.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's order.

1760 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Jadofsky v. Iowa Kemper Ins. Co.


No. 84-029


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


120 Wis. 2d 494; 355 N.W.2d 550; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4126


July 10, 1984, Submitted on briefs  
August 22, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: William J. Haese, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee filed a tort action seeking damages for the bad faith termination of his worker's compensation benefits by defendant insurance company. The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) granted the insurance company's motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction because the Worker's Compensation Act, Wis. Stat. § 102.18(1)(bp) was the employee's exclusive remedy, and the employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee was injured in the course of his employment on August 3, 1981. His employer's insurance company began paying him temporary total disability benefits, but starting in June, 1982, the insurance company, allegedly in bad faith, unreasonably suspended and terminated his benefits and refused to pay all the benefits subsequently awarded by the Department of Industry, Labor, and Human Relations. The main dispute on appeal was which date the employee was injured. Wis. Stat. § 102.18(1)(bp) provided the exclusive remedy for bad faith claims, but a judicial holding that bad faith constituted a separate injury remained in force. The law in effect at the time of the injuries determined the employee's right to compensation for any alleged bad faith denial of benefits. The bad faith injuries began to occur in June, 1982 and § 102.18(1)(bp), which was effective at that time, was the employee's sole remedy. Because he had no vested right in his cause of action for bad faith termination prior to June, 1982, and because § 102.18(1)(bp) was applied prospectively, not retroactively, the court rejected the employee's argument that his rights were unconstitutionally impaired.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the employee's tort action against the insurance company for the alleged bad faith termination of his worker's compensation benefits.

State v. Martin


No. 83-1984-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


120 Wis. 2d 678; 356 N.W.2d 496; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4102



August 16, 1984 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: MICHAEL B. TORPHY, Jr., Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which sentenced him as a repeat offender under Wis. Stat. § 343.44(2)(b). Defendant claimed § 343.44(2) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued his equal protection rights were violated when the increased penalties of § 343.44(2)(b) was determined by the use of the conviction dates rather than violation dates. Defendant was cited May 2, 1978 for operating a motor vehicle after revocation and convicted January 19, 1981. He was again cited for the same violation on June 18, 1983 and convicted September 13, 1983. More than five years had elapsed between his first and second violations, bur defendant was sentenced as a repeat offender because his convictions were less than five years apart. The court held that a rational basis existed for specifying the date of conviction as the beginning of the five-year period in § 343.44(2) as that was when the punishment was imposed which failed to deter a person from committing the crime a second time. The court concluded § 343.44 was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The trial court judgment was affirmed.

 

1762 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Schwarze


No. 83-1791-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


120 Wis. 2d 453; 355 N.W.2d 842; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4132


March 9, 1984, Submitted on briefs  
August 16, 1984, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Jefferson county, Harold H. Eberhardt, Judge, and an order of the circuit court for Jefferson county, John B. Danforth, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant public employee challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Jefferson County (Wisconsin), which convicted her of misconduct in public office in violation of Wis. Stat. § 946.12(3) and denied her post-conviction motion for a new trial. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in instructing the jury that she had a duty to disclose shortages of money to her employer.


OVERVIEW: Defendant served as an accounts receivable clerk for a school district. Her brother admitted to her that he had taken money from her office. She told her supervisor 11 weeks after she noticed the money was missing. She claimed that if she had a duty it was mandatory, and the real controversy was not tried. On appeal, the court held that as a matter of law an employee had a duty to disclose shortages of money to her supervisor, and therefore the trial court properly instructed the jury that the duty existed. The court found that defendant had a duty to disclose shortages to her employer, but how she did so was within her discretion. The court ruled that because defendant's power to determine the manner in which she exercised her duty was discretionary, the jury reasonably could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that her failure to exercise that discretionary power was a violation of Wis. Stat. § 946.12(3). The court concluded that because defendant's duty was discretionary and the trial court correctly instructed the jury that a public employe had a duty to report shortages to her employer, the real controversy was tried.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for misconduct in public office.

 

1763 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Quinn v. Dodgeville


No. 82-1932


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


120 Wis. 2d 304; 354 N.W.2d 747; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4035


December 15, 1983, Argued  
July 19, 1984, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Iowa county: James P. Fiedler, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Iowa County (Wisconsin), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee town in an action that sought a judgment declaring unconstitutional Wis. Stat. Ann. § 59.97(5(e)(6), which allowed the town board to veto a county zoning ordinance amendment.


OVERVIEW: A landowner petitioned a town to rezone certain land. The town denied his request and the landowner brought an action that sought a judgment declaring unconstitutional Wis. Stat. Ann. § 59.97(5(e)(6), which allowed the town board to veto a county zoning ordinance amendment. The circuit court granted summary judgment in favor of the town and the court affirmed. The court held that the power to prevent a change in the permitted uses to which land could be put was the power to preserve an existing zoning. The court found that the town's power to veto a county zoning ordinance amendment was as legislative as the power to zone. The court held that the state's constitution did not prevent the legislature from authorizing a town to veto a county zoning ordinance. The court concluded that the delegated power shared by the town and the county was not unconstitutional. The court found that the town's veto had not violated a constitutional or statutory requirement that zoning conform to a comprehensive plan.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the landowner's suit.

 

1764 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Messner v. Briggs & Stratton Corp.


No. 83-2002


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


120 Wis. 2d 127; 353 N.W.2d 363; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4056


May 16, 1984, Submitted on briefs  
June 20, 1984, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Patrick J. Madden, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an injured employee and her husband, sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which dismissed their action against defendant employer for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and granted summary judgment to the employer. The injured employee and her husband challenged the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 102.18(1)(bp), part of the Worker's Compensation Act.


OVERVIEW: The controversy stemmed from the employer's refusal to pay the injured employee temporary total disability benefits for the period that she did not work while she was recuperating from her injury. The injured employee filed a lawsuit against the employer, alleging various physical and emotional injuries caused by the company's action. The trial court dismissed the action and granted summary judgment to the employer on the ground that because the injured employee's exclusive remedy was under the Worker's Compensation Act, the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction. On appeal, the court determined that the Worker's Compensation Act precluded an employee from bring a tort action against her or his employer for a work-connected injury. The court found that the injured employee's claims had their origin in events that occurred because of the employment relationship between the injured employee and her employer. Thus, the court concluded that the claims were work related and were barred by the exclusivity provisions of the Worker's Compensation Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which dismissed the action of the injured employee and her husband and granted summary judgment to the employer.

 

1765 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Jacobson v. Commissioner of Ins.


No. 83-379


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


120 Wis. 2d 669; 353 N.W.2d 842; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3896



June 13, 1984 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: PATRICK J. MADDEN, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Order affirmed. The stay previously granted by this court is vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner insurance intermediary sought a Wis. Stat. § 227.15 review of the suspension of his insurance intermediary license and the imposition of a fine against him by the Commissioner of Insurance (Wisconsin). The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) remanded the matter to the Commissioner for more explicit findings, and the intermediary appealed. The court granted a stay.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner found that the intermediary had committed various unfair and deceptive insurance marketing practices, suspended his license for 30 days, and imposed a fine against him. On review under § 227.15, the trial court found that the rules under which the intermediary had been disciplined and the procedures followed by the Commissioner were valid. The trial court also concluded that the Commissioner's findings were insufficient and remanded the matter to the Commissioner for more definite findings. On appeal, the court held that: (1) the intermediary was precluded from challenging the validity of the rules under which he was disciplined where he did not challenge their validity before the Commissioner; (2) the intermediary's challenges to the Commissioner's findings were not appealable where he was not aggrieved by the trial court's disposition of those issues; and (3) the trial court properly ruled that Wis. Stat. § 628.34, prohibiting false or misleading information in communications on insurance matters, was not unconstitutionally vague where it sufficiently identified the prohibited conduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order and vacated the stay previously granted by the court.

 

1766 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Miller v. Green


No. 83-2263


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


120 Wis. 2d 672; 353 N.W.2d 843; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3942



June 13, 1984 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: RUDOLPH T. RANDA, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tenants sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), finding that the tenants breached a lease, evicting them from respondent landlord's premises, ordering them to pay double daily rent pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 704.27, and dismissing the claims of retaliation and unconstitutionality of the double rent statute.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that it was uncontradicted that the tenants failed to cure the lawn maintenance and security defects within the five days required under Wis. Stat. § 704.17(2). On appeal, the court held that these findings were not clearly erroneous and upheld them pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 805.17(2); it held that the trial court was correct in finding that the tenants materially breached the lease and that the landlord was entitled to eviction. It also held that the tenants failed to meet the beyond a reasonable doubt standard of proof in regard to Wis. Stat. § 704.27, as since they did not prove they were part of a class denied access to the court system, and it further held that they had not proved that they were denied either equal protection or due process where the eviction law required trial on the return date of the summons, the same as any other small claims action, and allowed the tenants any legitimate defenses. The court further held that because the tenants did not give notice to the attorney general as required by Wis. Stat. § 806.04(11), their challenge to the constitutionality of the double rent statute should not have been heard by the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1767 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Strassburg


No. 83-1857


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


120 Wis. 2d 30; 352 N.W.2d 215; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4044


May 17, 1984, Submitted on briefs  
June 6, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Sheboygan county: John G. Buchen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County (Wisconsin), which found him to be a habitual traffic offender under Wis. Stat. ch. 351, thereby revoking his operating privileges for five years.


OVERVIEW: Between August 1, 1980 and February 22, 1983, defendant incurred 12 moving traffic violations. Nine of these violations took place in California, while the remaining three violations occurred in Wisconsin. Upon the revocation of defendant's driving privileges, he contended that the Department of Transportation was estopped from bringing a proceeding under Wis. Stat. ch. 351 on the facts of this case, that the trial court abused its discretion by failing to exercise any discretion, that the State's delay in bringing the petition was a violation of due process, and that the habitual traffic offender statute was unconstitutional. The court affirmed, holding that it was not reasonable for defendant to assume that because he had obtained reinstatement, he would be immune from a habitual traffic offender action if subsequently convicted of an earlier offense. The court stated that courts were permitted no discretion in the administration of Wis. Stat. ch. 351. The court found that the delay in bringing the habitual offender proceeding was not unreasonable and that defendant was not prejudiced by the delay. The court found the habitual offender statute to be constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

 

1768 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


CITY OF MADISON v. CHRITTON


No. 83-159


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


119 Wis. 2d 899; 350 N.W.2d 741; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3887



May 25, 1984 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: MARK A. FRANKEL, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment rendered by the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which found him guilty of operating a motor vehicle while having a blood-alcohol concentration of 0.1 percent or more by weight of alcohol in his blood, claiming that he was denied a fair trial.


OVERVIEW: A police officer pulled defendant over after he observed his vehicle speeding and drifting partially into the adjacent lane. The officer observed defendant stumble somewhat when he got out of his car, noted an odor of intoxicants on his breath and bloodshot eyes, and noted that he slurred his speech. After defendant failed his field sobriety tests, he was arrested for driving while under the influence of intoxicants. Defendant was administrated a breathalyzer test, showing a .12 percent blood-alcohol level. Defendant was found guilty and appealed his conviction. The court held that Wis. Stat. § 885.235 created a rebuttable presumption that defendant's blood-alcohol level was 0.1 percent or more at the time of operating a vehicle if, within three hours thereafter, his blood-alcohol level was tested to be 0.1 percent or more. The court also stated that the presumption, standing alone, was sufficient in the absence of scientific rebuttal evidence by the defendant to sustain a directed verdict under the clear and convincing burden of proof. The court concluded that defendant failed to present evidence to overcome the presumption and therefore defendant's conviction was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Monroe v. Funeral Directors & Embalmers Examining Bd.


No. 83-1122


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


119 Wis. 2d 385; 349 N.W.2d 746; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3803


February 28, 1984, Submitted on briefs  
May 23, 1984, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Walworth county: John J. Byrnes, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Funeral Directors and Embalmers Examining Board (Wisconsin) challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Walworth County (Wisconsin), which vacated the Board's decision to suspend respondent funeral director's license to practice as a funeral director and embalmer.


OVERVIEW: The funeral director received a call to take charge of the deceased's body. He was notified that an autopsy was to be performed, so he should only do an arterial embalming. The funeral director instead did a cavitary embalming, which made the autopsy impractical. When the family asked the funeral director about this, he made crass remarks about the autopsy procedure. The Board charged him with violating Wis. Admin. Code § FDE 3.01(5), (2) and suspended his license. The trial court vacated the decision. On appeal, the court reversed. The court reviewed the Board's legal conclusions to determine if they were reasonable. The court found that substantial evidence supported the conclusion that the funeral director's conduct in embalming the body as he did was a wanton or reckless disregard of his duties. The court found that the Board's interpretation of its own regulation was entitled to controlling weight. The court found that the Board's finding that the funeral director's statements to the family were offensive was not clearly erroneous. The court found that the language in Wis. Admin. Code § FDE 3.01(2), (5) was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court, which vacated the Board's suspension of the funeral director.

 

1770 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. JAQUA


No. 83-1498


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT II


119 Wis. 2d 900; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3854



May 19, 1984 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Racine county: RICHARD ORTON, Reserve Judge, presiding. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of operating a motor vehicle with a blood alcohol concentration in excess of .10 percent, a violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(b).


OVERVIEW: A police officer stopped defendant after defendant attempted to enter southbound expressway traffic from a northerly direction. The arresting officer testified that defendant had trouble walking in the snow, her eyes were bloodshot, and there was an odor of alcohol on her breath. A breathalyzer test indicated that her blood alcohol concentration was .11 percent. Defendant testified that she had consumed some alcohol at her daughter's home prior to driving. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. Contrary to defendant's contention, Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(b) was not constitutionally invalid due to vagueness. A similar argument had been raised in a prior case. The court dismissed the constitutional challenge in the prior case upon finding that a person of common intelligence could, with a fair degree of definiteness, believe himself or herself to be in jeopardy of violating the statute if a significant quantity of alcohol had been consumed. Any person with common sense would know when consumption approached a meaningful amount. At that point, the person was on notice or had "clear warning" that if they drove they did so at their own risk.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

STATE v. PARK


No. 83-1563


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


119 Wis. 2d 901; 350 N.W.2d 742; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3859



May 9, 1984 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Waukesha county: MARK S. GEMPELER, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment and order of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of operating a motor vehicle with a blood alcohol concentration of .10 percent or more contrary to Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(b).


OVERVIEW: A state trooper observed defendant drifting back and forth using the full width of the lane. Defendant claimed that he was weaving because of his poor suspension. Defendant performed well on field sobriety tests, but the trooper later detected the smell of alcohol on defendant's breath. Defendant was arrested, and a breathalyzer test showed his blood alcohol concentration (BAC) was .15 percent. Defendant appealed from his conviction under Wis. The court affirmed his conviction. Defendant essentially argued that the statute was unconstitutionally vague because it was not possible for a person to determine by his own senses whether his BAC was legal or illegal. The court had dismissed that argument in a prior case. A person of common intelligence could, within a fairly definitive degree, believe himself to be in jeopardy of violating the statute if a significant amount of alcohol was consumed. Any person with common sense would know when consumption approached a meaningful amount.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and order.

HABERMANN v. CITY OF SUN PRAIRIE


No. 83-598


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


119 Wis. 2d 896; 350 N.W.2d 739; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3802



April 19, 1984 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: W. L. JACKMAN, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed a declaratory judgment entered by the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which upheld the validity of defendant city's 1969 zoning ordinance. The ordinance designated the property owners' property R-3, or two-family residence.


OVERVIEW: The property was located between multiple apartments that bordered a commercial area and single family residences. The property owners had a three-unit apartment building on part of their property. The city's 1969 ordinance zoned the property as a buffer between the higher and lower density uses surrounding it, restricting construction on a vacant portion to one- or two-family dwellings. The property owners alleged that the ordinance constituted illegal spot zoning and that it was arbitrary. The court upheld the trial court's judgment. The court held that the property owners were not denied equal protection of the laws because the different land use classification of the surrounding properties and the property owners' property was justified by the city's desire to buffer residential areas from commercial zones. Further, the property owners' property was not spot zoned because it shared the same land use privileges and restrictions as other properties in the vicinity. Finally, because the benefits of orderly land use planning and the use of buffer zones were great, and because the economic burden to the property owners was slight, the property owners were not denied due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1776 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. SEIY


No. 83-2056


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


119 Wis. 2d 898; 350 N.W.2d 740; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3763



April 18, 1984 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha county: MARK GEMPELER, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which revoked his driver's license privileges for his refusal to submit to a breathalyzer test upon his arrest for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicants.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicants. He refused to submit to a breathalyzer test, and the trial court eventually revoked his driver's license privileges. He appealed, noting that the statute allowed up to three hours for taking the test. He therefore reasoned that the officer's conduct in demanding that he take the test promptly was contrary to statutory intent and was also a deprivation of due process. He claimed that there was no probable cause to arrest, so the breath sample was an unlawful seizure. The court affirmed the judgment and held that once defendant was arrested, and a citation was given for operation of a vehicle under the influence of intoxicants, custodial authorities had the duty to immediately warn him of the obligations and consequences of refusal. Defendant's obligation was to take the test promptly or refuse it promptly. The constitutionality issue was not considered because it was not presented at the trial court level. Ample probable cause existed to place defendant under arrest because the officer saw defendant's vehicle weaving in traffic, and defendant failed the field tests.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1777 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Muehlenberg


No. 83-1598


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


118 Wis. 2d 502; 347 N.W.2d 914; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3640


February 9, 1984, Submitted on briefs  
March 27, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Washington county: James B. Schwalbach, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with operating a motor vehicle with a blood alcohol concentration of 0.10 percent or more in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(b). The Circuit Court for Washington County (Wisconsin) found the statute unconstitutionally vague. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that § 346.63(1)(b) was void for vagueness because it was not possible for a person to determine by his or her own senses whether his or her blood alcohol concentration of a "legal" 0.09 percent or an "illegal" 0.10 percent. The trial court agreed and found statute unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed. Defendant conceded that the statute satisfied the second prong of the "void-for-vagueness" test, as it provided a precise standard of law enforcement. With respect to the second prong, the court held that absolute precision was not required to prevent the statute from being declared vague. While a driver might not be able to determine that his or her blood alcohol content was 0.10 percent rather than 0.09 percent, a person of average intelligence could, with a fair degree of definiteness, believe himself or herself to be in jeopardy of violating the statute if a significant quantity of alcohol had been consumed. The court also took judicial notice of the fact that it required more than a small amount of alcohol to produce a 0.10 percent blood alcohol content.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

STATE v. NETZ


No. 83-793-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


118 Wis. 2d 824; 349 N.W.2d 110; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3709

OVERVIEW: After skating, defendant, the victim, his friend, and another girl had drinks in defendant's car. After taking the other girl home, defendant parked the car. Defendant jumped on top of the victim and tried to kiss her and feel her breast. She repelled him by pulling his hair and biting his cheekbone. The friend was in the back seat pretending to be asleep. After driving a short distance defendant again stopped the car. He told the victim that if she took her clothes off he would not hurt her. She took off her clothes and they had intercourse. Defendant again wanted to have intercourse. The victim complied because she was afraid. When defendant attempted intercourse a third time, defendant's friend told the victim to knock it off. The victim fled to a nearby house and asked for help. Defendant pled not guilty and not guilty by reason of mental disease or defect. Defendant was found guilty on three counts of second-degree sexual assault and his motion for postconviction relief was denied. On review, the court affirmed. The court held that defendant's statement that he would not hurt the victim if she took her clothes off could be construed as a threat of force if she did not comply.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions on three counts of second-degree sexual assault and the denial of his motion for postconviction relief.

 

1779 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brown


No. 83-820-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


118 Wis. 2d 377; 348 N.W.2d 593; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3633


January 19, 1984, Submitted on briefs  
March 9, 1984, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: John F. Foley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order reversed and cause remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of first degree murder and armed robbery, and from an order denying post conviction relief. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in refusing to give lesser-included offense instructions to the jury, and that the trial court erred in refusing to give the jury written instructions on all applicable substantive law.


OVERVIEW: The trial court instructed the jury on first degree murder and the intoxication defense but refused to submit a second degree murder instruction. Defendant testified that, on the night before the murder, he smoked a PCP cigarette, took two amphetamines, and drank a pint of whiskey. While this may not have been overwhelming evidence of intoxication at the time of the offense, the court could not conclude that the trial court abused its discretion in giving the intoxication instruction. The court also found that evidence of intoxication sufficient to merit an intoxication defense instruction could lead a reasonable jury to convict on either first or second degree murder. It therefore was error to instruct on intoxication but refuse to permit the lesser-included offense question to go to the jury. Finally, the court concluded that it was error for the trial court not to have submitted the intoxication instruction to the jury in writing. Such an instruction set forth a defense to a first degree murder charge. Given the gravity of the instruction's role in the case, the court could not reasonably say that, had the error not been committed, the verdict might probably have been different.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for first degree murder and armed robbery, and remanded the cause for a new trial.

State v. Minniecheske


No. 83-1503-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


118 Wis. 2d 357; 347 N.W.2d 610; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3622


January 9, 1984, Submitted on briefs  
March 6, 1984, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Shawano county: Gary L. Carlson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Shawano County (Wisconsin), which convicted him for criminal slander of title, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 943.60(1), and imposed a sentence of two years.


OVERVIEW: Charges arose out of defendant's attempt to record a lis pendens that purported to effect title to all of the real property in a town. On appeal, the court held that (1) the refusal of the register to record the lis pendens was irrelevant because the statute prohibited an attempt; (2) the scope of the lis pendens, filed in connection with a lawsuit that was barred by a statute of limitations and that challenged the establishment of the town, and defendant's history of filing similar documents unsuccessfully, supported a jury's finding that defendant knew the lis pendens was a sham; (3) defendant's vagueness challenge failed because his conduct was obviously prohibited by Wis. Stat. § 943.60(1); (4) defendants pattern of harassing those who disagreed with him was not protected by the First Amendment because he claimed he was making a political statement; (5) the fact that defendant was the first person prosecuted under the statute did not demonstrate vindictiveness because someone had to be the first person prosecuted and the facts supported the prosecution; and (6) the maximum sentence was not disproportionate or shocking even though it was for a first offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Wickstrom


No. 83-1500-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


118 Wis. 2d 339; 348 N.W.2d 183; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3623


January 16, 1984, Submitted on briefs  
March 6, 1984, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Shawano county: Earl W. Schmidt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Shawano County (Wisconsin), which, after a jury trial, convicted him of two counts of violating Wis. Stat. § 946.69(1) for assuming to act as a town clerk and as a municipal judge and imposed consecutive sentences of nine months for each conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of falsely assuming to act as a town clerk and as a municipal judge after he purported to create a new township and took a number of actions indicating that he assumed to act as a public officer. The court affirmed his conviction and sentence. There was no error in the failure to appoint defendant counsel for an indigency proceeding because it was not a critical stage and, thus, he had no right to counsel at the proceeding. There was no prejudice in allowing the State to amend the complaint against defendant to charge additional counts supported by the original complaint without allowing defendant 10 days to challenge the amended complaint because defendant received sufficient notice of the nature and cause of the accusations. The fact that defendant assumed the offices of a nonexistent township did not make his actions outside of Wis. Stat. § 946.69(1). Section 946.69(1) was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad. Finally, the trial court considered factors that were proper in sentencing defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence.

 

1782 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


VIVID, INC. v. CITY OF JANESVILLE


Nos. 82-1952, 82-1953


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


118 Wis. 2d 819; 346 N.W.2d 469; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3618



February 24, 1984 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Rock county: GERALD W. JAECKLE, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a sign corporation and its president, appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin) in favor of defendant City of Janesville in the plaintiffs' action brought to obtain moving and other expenses as displaced persons under Wis. Stat. § 32.19(2)(c) (1969) on account of condemnation of realty by the City.


OVERVIEW: Under Wis. Stat. § 32.19(2)(c) (1969), "displaced person" meant any person that moved from realty on or after July 1, 1970, as a result of the acquisition of the realty for public purposes or reasonable expectation of acquisition of the realty subsequently acquired for public purposes. An amendment codified at Wis. Stat. § 32.19(2)(c)(1971) removed the "reasonable expectation" language from the statute. The 1971 version was made retroactive to January 2, 1971. The trial court found that plaintiffs did not begin their move until January 2, 1971. Plaintiffs claimed that they moved in reasonable expectation of the acquisition of realty during the period of January 2, 1971, to January 2, 1972, and that they acquired vested rights under the 1969 version of the statute. On appeal, the court ruled that, because the amendment occurred before the property had been taken by the City in 1973, causes of action did not accrue to plaintiffs, who had no vested rights until the property was acquired by the City. A statutory cause of action could be taken away by the legislature before it vested. The retroactive application of § 32.19(2)(c) (1971) was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Ruling in favor of the City, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1783 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brady


No. 83-474-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


118 Wis. 2d 154; 345 N.W.2d 533; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3542


October 3, 1983, Submitted on briefs  
February 24, 1984, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Rock county: J. Richard Long, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Wisconsin sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Rock County (Wisconsin), which suppressed evidence that resulted from defendant's arrest to secure his presence as a witness in a John Doe proceeding. The trial court held that the evidence could not be used against defendant in the criminal proceedings brought against him.


OVERVIEW: The John Doe judge issued a warrant for defendant's arrest, which required him to appear as a material witness. While in custody during the weekend, and after waiving his Miranda rights, defendant gave statements to the police and consented to a search of his business premises. The statements and evidence obtained from the search inculpated defendant. The pending charge resulted. A material witness arrest warrant under Wis. Stat. § 969.01(3) could only be issued in a "felony criminal proceeding." A John Doe judge was required to determine if any crime had been committed. The John Doe judge was not able to predict that a specific crime had been committed or that it was felonious. Accordingly, the court held that a John Doe proceeding was not a "felony criminal proceeding." It followed that a John Doe judge was not allowed to issue a material witness warrant under § 969.01(3). Therefore, the warrant authorizing defendant's arrest was invalid. The court held that defendant's arrest was unconstitutional under the Fourth Amendment. It was undisputed that the evidence sought to be suppressed was obtained as a result of defendant's arrest and was inadmissible against him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1784 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE ex rel. HASSAN ABOZEID v. CIRCUIT COURT FOR DANE CTY.


No. 84-248-W


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


118 Wis. 2d 822; 346 N.W.2d 471; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3619



February 15, 1984 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: HABEAS CORPUS proceedings instituted in this court upon leave granted pursuant to a petition. Writ granted. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Writ of habeas corpus is granted. The Dane County Sheriff, Jerome D. Lacke, is ordered to release petitioner from custody forthwith.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a writ of habeas corpus to require the trial court and both the Dane County District Attorney and Sheriff to release him from the county jail, where he had been incarcerated for failure to post cash bail on two misdemeanor charges. An issue presented was whether or not the $ 1,500 cash bail set by the trial court was excessive.


OVERVIEW: The criminal complaint for which bail was set alleged that petitioner had knowingly violated an injunction issued under Wis. Stat. § 813.025(2), which misdemeanor was a violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.33. A second charge against him was bail jumping. Apparently in contravention of the injunction, petitioner had contact with his wife, during which he stated to her that she looked good and that he still did not agree with what she was doing. The court ordered petitioner released on a writ of habeas corpus because of excessive bail. U.S. Const. amend. VIII and Wis. Const. art. 1, § 6 prohibited excessive bail; claims of constitutional error could be heard by an application for habeas corpus. Bail set higher than necessary to adequately assure appearance at trial was excessive under the Eighth Amendment. In finding that bail was excessive in the instant case, the court focused on the fact that defendant's oral statements during the subject contact were made at a public place and conveyed no threat of violence. The court made other rulings, including one that the merits of the habeas petition had been properly decided by a single appellate judge.


OUTCOME: Ruling in favor of petitioner, the court granted the writ of habeas corpus and directed the county sheriff to release petitioner from custody.

 

1785 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re B.L.P.


No. 83-911


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


118 Wis. 2d 33; 345 N.W.2d 510; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3554


November 22, 1983, Submitted on briefs  
February 1, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Racine county: Jon B. Skow, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin), which found her in contempt of a dispositional order and sentenced her to 30 days of confinement.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile was adjudicated delinquent for shoplifting. As part of the dispositional order she was required to attend school regularly without any unexplained absences or tardiness. Subsequently, the juvenile was found in contempt on three occasions. On the fourth occasion, the juvenile was ordered to spend 30 days in secure detention following an informal hearing in which a representative of the district attorney's office was not present and in which there was no order of proof or sworn testimony. On appeal, the court reversed finding that there was no sworn testimony and no proper order of proof was undertaken and therefore the procedures for executing contempt actions under Wis. Stat. § 785 were not followed. The court rejected the county's argument that the juvenile court did not have to follow the procedures of § 785. The court further rejected the argument that the juvenile court had discretion to apply whatever procedures it wanted, finding that such a contention was unworkable and contrary to the principles of due process. The fact that the case involved a juvenile did not require less due process than an equivalent adult proceeding.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed and remanded.

 

1786 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wilks


No. 83-737-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


117 Wis. 2d 495; 345 N.W.2d 498; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3534


December 14, 1983, Submitted on briefs  
January 24, 1984, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from judgments of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Robert W. Landry, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgments of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) convicting defendant of attempted robbery and attempted burglary, contrary to Wis. Stat. §§ 943.32(1)(a) and 939.32, and 943.10(1)(a) and 939.32, respectively, after defendant pleaded guilty to both offenses.


OVERVIEW: While defendant was being detained after being arrested for loitering in violation of Milwaukee, Wis., Ordinance § 106-31(1)(a) (1981), he was placed in a lineup that involved criminal offenses. After two witnesses identified him he was charged with criminal trespass, attempted robbery, and attempted burglary. Defendant pleaded guilty to attempted robbery and attempted burglary and was convicted. Defendant appealed, claiming that his constitutional rights to be free from unreasonable seizures were violated when he was forced to submit to a lineup following his arrest for an ordinance violation. In affirming the judgments, the court held that there was no distinction between an arrest for a civil violation and an arrest for a criminal violation where a lineup was concerned. As long as defendant was lawfully in custody and his constitutional rights were observed, he could be required to submit to a lineup for an unrelated criminal offense. In defendant's case, the police officers clearly had probable cause to arrest defendant for violating the loitering ordinance. Therefore, forcing defendant to submit to the lineup did not violate his constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments.

 

1787 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Milwaukee Mut. Ins. Co. v. Priewe


No. 82-2238


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


118 Wis. 2d 318; 348 N.W.2d 585; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3645


October 13, 1983, Submitted on briefs  
January 18, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Rock county: Gerald W. Jaeckle, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed and claim remanded for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant first insurer challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin), which granted respondent second insurer's motion for summary judgment and which dismissed the first insurer's alternative claims for contribution and indemnification.


OVERVIEW: The first insurer's insured and his wife were injured in a collision with the second insurer's insured. The first insurer paid the medical expenses of its insured's wife on August 20, 1979. It commenced the instant action on August 13, 1981 to recover the medical expenses. The first insurer's claim for contribution accrued when it made the payment. Thus, the contribution action was barred under Wis. Stat. § 893.92, which required the first insurer to commence its contribution action within one year of accrual. The first insurer was not entitled to a three-year limitation under Wis. Stat. § 893.12 on its contribution action because the first insurer's payment was a final settlement, not an advance payment. The trial court improperly rejected the indemnification claim because factual issues existed. The first insurer made payment pursuant to an insurance policy. Thus, it was not voluntary, but compelled by law. Therefore, the indemnification claim was proper. The first insurer's claim was not barred by the statute of limitations if it was one for indemnity; an apportionment of negligence would have determined whether the claim was for indemnity or contribution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment on the first insurer's contribution claim. The court reversed that part of the order that granted summary judgment on the first insurer's indemnification claim and remanded the indemnification claim for trial.

 

1788 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


ATLANTIC MUT. INS. CO. v. STEINPERIS


No. 82-1201


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


117 Wis. 2d 783; 345 N.W.2d 79; 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3517



January 10, 1984 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Portage county: ROBERT C. JENKINS, Judge. Judgment modified and affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment modified to $1,932.60, plus costs and disbursements, and, as modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant driver appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Portage County (Wisconsin), which awarded plaintiff subrogated insurer damages, plus costs and disbursements, after a jury found that the driver was 60 percent negligent in causing an accident and that the insured was 40 percent negligent.


OVERVIEW: The driver's car struck the insured's car. The insurer paid the car loss to its insured, subrogated to the insured's claim, and filed an action against the driver. The trial court's judgment against the driver was reversed and remanded for a jury trial. In the second trial, a jury apportioned negligence but the trial court answered the damages issue. The driver appealed. The court held that the driver had no right to challenge the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 806.09(1) because he failed to give the attorney general notice of his challenge. Section 806.09(1) did not deprive the driver of due process because he received a full jury trial before the second judgment was entered. The court held that the trial court properly refused to instruct on subrogation, which was determined on the prior appeal, and properly decided the damages issue as a matter of law. The court held the verdict was supported by sufficient evidence that the driver proceeded into the intersection when the insured had the right of way. The court reduced the judgment by the amount of the insured's negligence and the salvage value the insurer received for the car as offset against the towing and storage charges.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for the insurer and against the driver but modified the amount of damages.

State v. Fonk's Mobile Home Park & Sales, Inc.


No. 82-2319


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


117 Wis. 2d 94; 343 N.W.2d 820; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4146


November 2, 1983, Submitted on briefs  
December 27, 1983, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Racine county: James Wilbershide, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin), which dismissed its case against defendant mobile home park in an action that alleged the mobile home park had placed unreasonable contractual restrictions on owners residing in its park.


OVERVIEW: A mobile home park required that owners in the park who wanted to sell their homes had to sell the home to the park or the mobile home had to be immediately removed from the park. The State alleged this restriction placed unreasonable contractual restrictions on owners residing in the park in violation of Wis. Admin. Code § Ag. 125.07(1). The mobile home park discontinued the practice and the trial court dismissed the case because the mobile home park had discontinued using the restriction so no threat of future harm, a necessary element of proof in injunction actions, could be shown. The court reversed and remanded and held that threat of future harm needed only be alleged and proven in common law actions for injunctions. It was not necessary where the authority for the injunction was found in a statute that did not make threat of future harm a prerequisite to relief. The court found that the statute at issue here specifically provided the court with the authority to issue an injunction if an order had been violated. .


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment that dismissed the action against the mobile home park.

Eastman v. Madison


No. 82-2392


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


117 Wis. 2d 106; 342 N.W.2d 764; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4153


October 13, 1983, Submitted on briefs  
December 27, 1983, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review dismissed.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: Angela B. Bartell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former employees appealed a ruling from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which denied the employees' request for declaratory relief ordering their reinstatement as employees of defendant former employer, the City of Madison.


OVERVIEW: The employees had worked as police officers for the City. At the time that they entered employment, they resided in the City in compliance with Madison, Wis., General Ordinance 3.27, but they later moved to the suburbs. The employees maintained apartments in town and registered to vote there. The employees continued living in the suburbs even after City officials circulated a memorandum that advised that the ordinance in question would be strictly enforced. After due warning, the employees' positions were vacated. One of the employees filed a grievance, which was dismissed. Upon appeal of the denial of declaratory relief, the court concluded that the employees were not City residents as defined by the ordinance in question. The City was not estopped by alleged assurances that had been made to the employees by superior officers. Madison, Wis., General Ordinance 3.27 was constitutional facially and in its application to the employees. The availability of the grievance procedure culminating in a full evidentiary hearing satisfied due process requirements. The employees were not denied due process through a deprivation of an impartial decision-maker.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which denied declaratory relief to the former employees.

 

1791 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re Infant Boy S.


No. 83-981


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


117 Wis. 2d 782; 343 N.W.2d 830; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4163



December 7, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: ROBERT J. MIECH, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the mother of a child, sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied her petition to terminate the parental rights of respondent, the father of the child. On appeal, the mother asserted that the trial court erred in reserving the question of unfitness to the dispositional phase of the action and erred in excluding the testimony of police officers regarding the father's violent conduct.


OVERVIEW: Upon learning of the pregnancy, the mother's relationship with the father deteriorated to the point that he drove the mother's car into ditch, pushed her down, and had threatened to kill her. Throughout the pregnancy, the mother kept the father at a distance, generally refusing contact with her, and then with the baby after its birth. She filed an action seeking the termination of the father's parental rights after she decided to place the baby for adoption. Pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 48.242(3), the trial court reserved the issue of the father's fitness for the dispositional phase, allowing the jury to only find whether any grounds for termination existed. On appeal, the mother challenged the constitutionality of § 48.242(3) by asserting that it was error for the trial court to reserve the question of unfitness to the dispositional phase. She also asserted that the testimony of two police officers regarding the father's violent nature should have been admitted. The court held that the mother failed to meet the high burden of proving the unconstitutionality of § 48.242(3). The proposed evidence, while relevant and admissible, was cumulative, making its exclusion harmless error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1792 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re J. B.


No. 83-802


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


117 Wis. 2d 781; 343 N.W.2d 830; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4211



December 7, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: LEANDER J. FOLEY, JR., Judge. Reversed and cause remanded. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Orders reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of orders of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) that respectively adjudicated him delinquent and denied his motion for a new trial. An issue on appeal was whether or not there was a violation of a constitutional right by the disclosure without appellant's consent of his school photograph for use by the victim to identify him such that her out-of-court identification of him should have been suppressed.


OVERVIEW: The victim had been assaulted sexually by three assailants while she was departing from a high school. She had seen one assailant. A school principal allowed the victim to identify the assailant from about 1,200 photograph-identification cards. The victim also identified the assailant through glass from inside a school office. The court found that the show-up procedure was not impermissibly suggestive but that if it were given the circumstances in toto of the procedure the identification was reliable. However, the court ruled that testimony about the out-of-court identification should have been suppressed on account of the Fourth Amendment as far as the photograph identification had been procured by an illegal search of appellant's school records. Appellant had a reasonable expectation of privacy via Wis. Stat. § 118.125(2), which required the confidentiality of school records; notwithstanding the trial court's opinion, a pupil's photograph was indubitably a pupil record under Wis. Stat. § 118.125(1)(d). The court could not say that the erroneous admission of the inadmissible evidence was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: Ruling in favor of appellant, the court reversed the trial court's orders and remanded the case to the trial court for a new trial.

 

1793 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


K.J. K.J. v. BROWN CTY. DEPT. OF SOC. SERVS.


No. 83-1056


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District III


117 Wis. 2d 782; 343 N.W.2d 830; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4178



December 6, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Brown county: WILLIAM J. DUFFY, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a mentally disabled patient, challenged two orders from the Circuit Court for Brown County (Wisconsin), which ordered his continued protective placement under Wis. Stat. ch. 55.


OVERVIEW: The patient was ordered protectively placed in 1982. After a second review hearing in 1983, the circuit court ordered the placement continued without change. The issue on appeal was whether Wis. Stat. § 55.06(10)(a) required a circuit court reviewing a protective placement to determine if the conditions warranting placement still existed. On appeal, the court affirmed the orders. The court held that Wis. Stat. ch. 55 made no requirement of periodic court review of placements ordered under Wis. Stat. § 55.06(9)(a). Since the circuit court was under no obligation to review the patient's placement, it likewise had no statutory duty on review to determine if the conditions warranting placement continued to exist. The court found that although no court review was required, § 55.06(10)(a) did require the agency responsible for a protective placement to review his status at least every 12 months after admission, unless a court required more frequent review. Further, the court noted that the patient could at any time petition the circuit court for termination of protective placement on grounds that the conditions warranting placement were no longer present.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders.

 

1794 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


KONNOR v. SKARDA


No. 82-1125


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


116 Wis. 2d 693; 343 N.W.2d 826; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4108



November 23, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha county: JOHN P. BUCKLEY, Judge. Affirmed in part; reversed in part, and cause remanded. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant client challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which dismissed his counterclaim for negligent representation. The trial court granted summary judgment to plaintiff attorneys, who sought attorney fees for services rendered in the client's divorce action, and awarded costs and attorneys fees to the attorneys for their defense to the client's counterclaim, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 814.025.


OVERVIEW: The client argued that the attorneys' motion for summary judgment was brought beyond the eight-month limit allowed by Wis. Stat. § 802.08(1). The court held that the attorneys' motion was for judgment on the pleadings under Wis. Stat. § 802.06(3), for which there was no time limit. Because the trial court considered matters outside of the pleadings, it properly treated the motion as one for summary judgment pursuant to § 802.06(3). The court held that, because no issue of material fact was in dispute, the attorneys were entitled to judgment. Further, the client's claim that the attorneys were negligent for failing to argue for a date other than the date of the divorce degree for the valuation of the marital estate had no merit. In the court's view, the client did not set forth any "exceptional circumstances" that suggested that a deviation from Wisconsin law was appropriate. However, the failure of the attorneys to argue that the client's company stock bonus was income after the divorce degree was a possible claim, and the trial court did not make findings sufficient to support its dismissal on that point. Finally, Wis. Stat. § 814.025 was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of a portion of the client's counterclaim and remanded for further findings as to whether the attorneys failed to present a legitimate argument in the client's divorce action. Thus, whether the entire counterclaim was frivolous and whether the attorneys were entitled to attorney fees and costs was for further review by the trial court. Otherwise, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

STATE v. BARBER


No. 83-1093-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


116 Wis. 2d 696; 343 N.W.2d 828; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4126

OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for a third time for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1). 1796 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. LEURQUIN


No. 83-1062-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


116 Wis. 2d 696; 343 N.W.2d 828; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4093



November 18, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: THOMAS P. DOHERTY, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which found him guilty of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant contrary to Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1) and, because it was his third conviction within five years, sentenced him to 30 days in the House of Correction. Defendant claimed, inter alia, that the statutes under which he was convicted were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with his third violation of operating a motor vehicle on February 23, 1982, while under the influence of an intoxicant, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1). A jury found him guilty on February 15, 1983. The first violation occurred October 25, 1977, with defendant being convicted on December 7, 1977. The court rejected defendant's argument that, because Wis. Stat. § 346.65(2) made a third offense a criminal violation without requiring proof of the first two offenses beyond a reasonable doubt, Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1) unconstitutionally permitted a conviction without proof of every element of the offense beyond a reasonable doubt. The fact of the prior violations was not an element of the crime of violating § 346.63(1). The court also rejected defendant's contention that Wis. Stat. §§ 346.65(2) and 343.307 were ex post facto laws because they existed before the violation appealed by defendant. Finally, the court held that the five-year period referenced in Wis. Stat. § 346.65(2)(b) was to be measured from and to the dates of the refusals or violations which resulted in the revocation or convictions, not from and to the dates of the convictions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1797 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Rubin v. Wauwatosa


No. 83-140


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


116 Wis. 2d 305; 342 N.W.2d 451; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4054


September 15, 1983, Submitted on briefs  
November 18, 1983, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Elliot N. Walstead, Reserve Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which held that an ordinance adopted by the city governing commercial refuse collection was not authorized by Wisconsin law and was unconstitutional. The ordinance had been challenged by respondent business property owners.


OVERVIEW: The city adopted an ordinance that distinguished between "residential" refuse collection and "commercial" refuse collection. The ordinance included within its definition of commercial properties multiple dwelling units and imposed a fee for commercial collection services. Respondents brought an action contending that the city exceeded its statutory authority and that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The trial court held for respondents and the city sought review. The court reversed the decision. The court found that Wis. Stat. §§ 66.049 and 66.60(16)(a) authorized a city to collect refuse from classes of property and to impose fees for its services. Thus, the court said, the city did not exceed its authority by creating refuse collection districts defined by the particular class of property served and employing different methods of payment as between districts. The court also held that the classification scheme did not violate the Equal Protection Clause. The court said that refuse collection is not a "fundamental right" and that the owners of multiple dwelling units were not a suspect classification. The court also found a rational basis for the classification scheme.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a decision that held unconstitutional a city ordinance that imposed charges for commercial refuse collection.

RUFF v. WISCONSIN STATE PERSONNEL COMMN.


No. 82-1572


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


116 Wis. 2d 693; 343 N.W.2d 826; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4128



November 3, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: WILLIAM L. JACKMAN, Reserve Judge, presiding. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former employee challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision of respondent former employer, the Wisconsin State Personnel Commission, which discharged the employee for just cause from the position of assistant investment director for public bonds.


OVERVIEW: The employee argued that he should have been trained for the job, that he was disciplined for exercising his free speech rights, and that his discharge was excessive discipline. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment because the record supported the Commission's findings that the employee was trained, that the discharge was based on his incompetence and failure to improve, and that discharge was a proper sanction. The court found that the employee was expected to be able to do the job at the time he entered the position. The testimony of the employee's supervisor amply evinced the assistance given to the employee on a daily basis. The court also found that the employee had minimal experience in the area of public bonds. The record was replete with evidence that despite assistance from his supervisor, over the five-month period of his employment, he consistently failed to adequately complete or perform required tasks. The court found that there was substantial evidence to support the Commission's finding that the discharge was not excessive or inappropriate discipline. Further, his earlier reprimand for a speech-related activity had no link to his later discharge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1799 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Schmit


No. 82-1489-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


115 Wis. 2d 657; 340 N.W.2d 752; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3942


June 9, 1983, Argued  
October 26, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Dodge County: Thomas W. Wells, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Dodge County (Wisconsin), which dismissed a criminal complaint against defendant for misconduct in public office contrary to Wis. Stat. § 946.12(2).


OVERVIEW: The State appealed from an order dismissing a criminal complaint against the defendant for one count of misconduct in public office contrary to Wis. Stat. § 946.12(2). The issue was whether an act of consensual sexual intercourse between a prison guard and a prisoner, occurring when the guard was on duty, was punishable as an act done and forbidden to be done in the guard's "official capacity." On appeal, the court agreed with the trial court's determination that, under the circumstances of the case, it was not. It might be a violation of ethics and good conduct for a public officer in such a capacity to use his influence upon a board, but it would not be bribery. Because defendant's act did not inherently implicate the power of her public office, it did not fall within the prohibition of § 946.12(2).


OUTCOME: The order of the lower court dismissing a criminal complaint against defendant was affirmed.

 

1800 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Butzlaff v. Van Der Geest & Sons, Inc.


No. 82-1507


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


115 Wis. 2d 535; 340 N.W.2d 742; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3943


July 26, 1983, Submitted on Briefs  
October 11, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Marathon County: Ronald D. Keberle, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant horse owners sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Marathon County (Wisconsin), which dismissed their complaint for damages incurred as a result of respondent neighbor seizing the owners' horses under Wis. Stat. ch. 173.


OVERVIEW: The horse owners failed to properly maintain a portion of a fence on the border of their property. Four horses crossed over onto the neighbor's property and damaged his corn and hay crops. The neighbor held the horses, pursuant to Wis. Stat. ch. 173. The horses were transferred to respondent livestock dealer until damages were paid or the horses were sold. The owners sued for recovery of their horses after posting the damages. The trial court dismissed their complaint for damages and their motion to declare ch. 173 unconstitutional. On appeal, the judgment was affirmed. The court held that the owners were not entitled to damages because the neighbor and the dealer acted in good faith under ch. 173, which had not been declared unconstitutional. The court ruled that because the horses had been returned, there was no remaining due process controversy. There was sufficient evidence for the trial court to find that the owners failed to prove the allegations in their complaint.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.
